Expiation for Disavowal Formulas: Multiple vs. Single
Text excerpt outlining the expiation rule for multiple disavowal oaths.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the rule that multiple distinct disavowal formulas require multiple expiations, while a single formula repeated many times requires only one expiation.

Core Idea
A single formula repeated many times is one oath; different formulas are separate oaths.

When someone uses disavowal of Allah or similar expressions as oaths, the number of expiations depends on whether the formulas are distinct or repeated. The Hanafi school has a clear principle: multiplicity of formulas leads to multiplicity of expiations, while unity of formula leads to unity of expiation, regardless of repetition.

Guided Path
1
Identify the disavowal formula(s)
Determine the exact expression used. Examples: 'I am innocent of Allah' or 'Allah is innocent of me' or 'I am a disbeliever if I do X'.
Some expressions like 'innocent of intercession' are not considered oaths.
2
Distinguish single vs. multiple formulas
If the same phrase is repeated (even a thousand times), it counts as one formula. If different phrases are used, each distinct phrase is a separate formula.
The text uses the example of 'I am innocent of Allah' repeated a thousand times as a single formula.
3
Apply the expiation rule
Single formula → one expiation upon breaking the oath. Multiple distinct formulas → each broken oath requires its own expiation.
This principle is cited from al-Zahiriyyah and upheld in al-Mujtaba and al-Dhakhirah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الأيمان ونذر الله وإن فعل كذا فهو كافر لا بعلمه وغضبه وسخطه ورحمته والنبي والقرآن عن: هـ. وفيها والله ورسوله بريئان منه فتعين أن يكون ما في الولوالجية كذلك والحذف من الكاتب ثم قال في الظهيرية والأصل في جنس هذه المسائل أنه متى تعددت صيغة البراءة تعددت الكفارة وإذا اتحدت اتحدت . وصحح في المجتبي والذخيرة أنهما يمينان قال : ولو قال إن فعلت كذا فأنا بريء من الله ألف مرة ففعل لزمته كفارة واحدة ا هـ . وفي الظهيرية أيضاً: ولو قال إن فعلت كذا فلا إله في السماء يكون يميناً، ولو قال إن فعلت كذا فهو بريء من المؤمنين قالوا يكون يميناً لأن البراءة من المؤمنين تكون لإنكار الإيمان اهـ. وينبغي أن الحالف إذا قصد نفي المكان الله أنه لا يكون يميناً لأنه حينئذ ليس بكفر بل هو الأيمان. وفي الذخيرة : قال هو يمين ولا يكفر. وفيها : لو قال إن فعلت كذا فأنا بريء من الشفاعة الأصح أنه ليس بيمين. وعلله في الظهيرية بأن الشفاعة وإن كانت حقاً لكن من أنكرها صار مبتدعاً لا كافراً ا أيضاً سئل نجم الدين عمن قال إن كلمت فلاناً فهو شريك الكفارة فيما قالوا على الله تعالى مما لا يليق به فكلمه ماذا يجب عليه ؟ قال : كفارة اليمين ا هـ . وأشار المصنف إلى أنه إذا فعل المحلوف عليه لا يكون كافراً لأنه صار يميناً. وقيد بكونه علقه على فعل في المستقبل لأنه لو قال ذلك لشيء قد فعله في الماضي كأن قال إن كنت فعلت كذا فهو كافر وهو عالم أنه قد فعل فهو يمين الغموس لا كفارة فيها إلا التوبة والاستغفار وهل يكفر حتى تكون التوبة اللازمة عليه التوبة من الكفرة وتجديد الإسلام؟ قيل لا . وقيل نعم تنجيز معنی علقه بأمر كائن فكأنه قال ابتداء هو كافر؛ والصحيح أنه إن كان عالماً أنه يمين إما منعقدة أو لا يكفر بالماضي، وإن كان جاهلاً وعنده أنه يكفر بالحلف في الغموس أو بمباشرة الشرط في المستقبل يكفر فيهما لأنه لما أقدم عليه وعنده أنه يكفر فقد رضي بالكفر، كذا في كثير من الكتب. وفي المجتبى والذخيرة والفتوى على أنه إن اعتقد الكفر به يكفر وإلا فلا في المستقبل والماضي جميعاً. وفي قولهم يعلم الله أنه فعل كذا ولم يفعل كذا وهو يعلم خلافه فيه اختلاف المشايخ وعامتهم على أنه يكفر. ثم رقم في المجتبى رقماً آخر : لو قال الله يعمل أني ما فعلت كذا وهو يعلم أنه كاذب فقيل لا يكفر وهو رواية عن أبي يوسف لأنه قصد ترويج الكذب دون الكفر .
The book of oaths. And the vow of Allah, and if he does such-and-such then he is a disbeliever, not by His knowledge, His anger, His wrath, His mercy, the Prophet, and the Quran. From: H. And in it: 'Allah and His Messenger are innocent of him,' so it is determined that what is in al-Walwalijiyyah is likewise, and the omission from the writer. Then he said in al-Zahiriyyah: The principle in this type of issues is that when the formula of disavowal is multiple, the expiation is multiple, and when it is single, it is single. And it is corrected in al-Mujtaba and al-Dhakhirah that they are two oaths. He said: If he said, 'If I do such-and-such, I am innocent of Allah a thousand times,' and he did it, one expiation is incumbent. In al-Zahiriyyah also: If he said, 'If I do such-and-such, there is no god in heaven,' it is an oath. And if he said, 'If I do such-and-such, he is innocent of the believers,' they said it is an oath because disavowal of believers is due to denial of faith. And it is appropriate that if the swearer intends to negate place from Allah, it is not an oath because then it is not disbelief but rather... (?). And in al-Dhakhirah: He said it is an oath and he does not become a disbeliever. And in it: If he said, 'If I do such-and-such, I am innocent of intercession,' the sound opinion is that it is not an oath. And he explained in al-Zahiriyyah that intercession, although it is true, whoever denies it becomes an innovator, not a disbeliever. Also, Najm al-Din was asked about someone who said, 'If I speak to so-and-so, he is a partner in what they said about Allah Exalted that is not befitting,' and he spoke to him; what is incumbent? He said: Expiation of an oath. And the author indicated that when the sworn thing is done, he does not become a disbeliever because it became an oath. And he restricted it to being conditional on a future action, because if he said that about something already done in the past, like if he said, 'If I did such-and-such, I am a disbeliever,' while knowing he did it, then it is an oath of falsehood (yamin ghamus) in which there is no expiation except repentance and seeking forgiveness. Does he become a disbeliever such that necessary repentance includes repentance from disbelief and renewing Islam? It is said no. And it is said yes, because he attached meaning to an existing matter, so it is as if he said initially he is a disbeliever. The correct view is that if he knows it is an oath, either (the oath) is binding or not, he does not become a disbeliever regarding the past; and if he is ignorant and thinks that he becomes a disbeliever by swearing falsely or by directly fulfilling the condition in the future, then he becomes a disbeliever in both cases because when he proceeded with it while thinking it is disbelief, he consented to disbelief. This is as in many books. And in al-Mujtaba, al-Dhakhirah, and the fatwa is that if he believes that disbelief occurs through it, he becomes a disbeliever; otherwise not, in both future and past. And regarding their saying, 'Allah knows that he did such-and-such,' while he did not, and he knows the opposite, there is disagreement among the shaykhs, and most of them hold that he becomes a disbeliever. Then there is another sign in al-Mujtaba: If he said, 'Allah knows that I did not do such-and-such,' while knowing he is lying, it is said he does not become a disbeliever, and it is a narration from Abu Yusuf because he intended to promote falsehood, not disbelief.
Source pages p. 480

Commentary
This passage deals with the legal classification of various oath formulas involving disavowal of Allah or conditional statements of disbelief. The author, Ibn Nujaym in al-Bahr al-Ra'iq, explains that if one swears by saying 'I am disassociated from Allah' or 'I am a disbeliever if I do X,' it is considered a binding oath (yamin). However, if the statement is about a past action, it becomes a yamin ghamus (false oath) with no expiation except repentance. A key intra-Hanafi dispute emerges regarding whether such a person becomes an apostate (kafir). The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is that if he believes it causes disbelief, he becomes a disbeliever; otherwise not. Multiple formulas of disavowal result in multiple expiations if they are separate oaths, but if the same formula is repeated, only one expiation is due. The text also discusses specific expressions like 'no god in heaven' and 'innocent of believers' which are considered oaths, while 'innocent of intercession' is not an oath because denial of intercession is bid'ah, not kufr. The overall emphasis is on intention, custom, and the juristic principle that oaths are determined by what is customary among people.

Key Terms
يمين الغموس (yamin al-ghamus): A false oath regarding a past event, where the swearer knowingly lies. In such oaths, no expiation is required; only repentance suffices.
براءة (bara'ah): Disavowal or dissociation, as in saying 'I am innocent of Allah' or 'Allah is innocent of me'. In oath context, it is a valid oath formula if customary.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If someone says 'If I eat this, I am innocent of Allah' and then repeats the same phrase for a second action, how many expiations are due if both actions are done?
A) One expiation
B) Two expiations
C) No expiation because it is a false statement
D) It depends on the person's intention

Key Takeaway
The number of expiations for disavowal oaths depends on the number of distinct formulas, not the number of times they are repeated.

Conditional Disbelief and Apostasy: The Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Text excerpt explaining the intra-Hanafi dispute on apostasy from conditional disbelief statements.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the intra-Hanafi dispute on whether conditional disbelief statements cause actual apostasy, and identify the mufta bihi position based on the swearer's belief.

Core Idea
The mufta bihi is that conditional disbelief becomes actual disbelief only if the swearer believes it does.

One of the most consequential questions in Hanafi oath law is whether saying 'If I do X, I am a kafir' makes one an apostate when the condition is fulfilled. The later authorities have resolved a dispute that centers not on the words themselves, but on the swearer's belief about the effect of his words. This lesson unpacks that dispute and its practical implications.

Guided Path
1
Classify the oath as future-conditional or past-related
Future-conditional: 'If I do X, I am a kafir.' Past-related: 'If I did X, I am a kafir' (though actually done) – this is yamin ghamus. Each has different rules.
The text explicitly distinguishes past and future.
2
Assess the swearer's belief
Did he think his statement would cause him to become a disbeliever? The mufta bihi: if he believed it causes kufr, he becomes a kafir; otherwise not.
This applies to both future and past, according to al-Mujtaba and al-Dhakhirah.
3
Apply the mufta bihi for future-conditional oaths
If he believes it causes kufr, he becomes a kafir upon breaking the oath and must renew Islam and pay expiation. If he does not believe it causes kufr, he only pays expiation for the broken oath.
The text says: 'the fatwa is that if he believes it causes disbelief, he becomes a disbeliever; otherwise not.'
4
Handle past-related oaths (yamin ghamus)
For a false oath about the past, no expiation is due, only repentance. But if he believed it causes kufr, he becomes a kafir and must repent from kufr and renew Islam.
There is disagreement: some say he becomes a kafir automatically, but the correct view is that he only becomes a kafir if he believed it causes kufr.
5
Analyze the 'Allah knows' dispute
If someone says 'Allah knows that I did not do X' while lying, some Hanafi shaykhs hold he becomes a kafir; others (including a narration from Abu Yusuf) say no, because he intended falsehood, not disbelief.
The majority view holds he becomes a kafir, but the later fatwa is conditional on belief.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الأيمان ونذر الله وإن فعل كذا فهو كافر لا بعلمه وغضبه وسخطه ورحمته والنبي والقرآن عن: هـ. وفيها والله ورسوله بريئان منه فتعين أن يكون ما في الولوالجية كذلك والحذف من الكاتب ثم قال في الظهيرية والأصل في جنس هذه المسائل أنه متى تعددت صيغة البراءة تعددت الكفارة وإذا اتحدت اتحدت . وصحح في المجتبي والذخيرة أنهما يمينان قال : ولو قال إن فعلت كذا فأنا بريء من الله ألف مرة ففعل لزمته كفارة واحدة ا هـ . وفي الظهيرية أيضاً: ولو قال إن فعلت كذا فلا إله في السماء يكون يميناً، ولو قال إن فعلت كذا فهو بريء من المؤمنين قالوا يكون يميناً لأن البراءة من المؤمنين تكون لإنكار الإيمان اهـ. وينبغي أن الحالف إذا قصد نفي المكان الله أنه لا يكون يميناً لأنه حينئذ ليس بكفر بل هو الأيمان. وفي الذخيرة : قال هو يمين ولا يكفر. وفيها : لو قال إن فعلت كذا فأنا بريء من الشفاعة الأصح أنه ليس بيمين. وعلله في الظهيرية بأن الشفاعة وإن كانت حقاً لكن من أنكرها صار مبتدعاً لا كافراً ا أيضاً سئل نجم الدين عمن قال إن كلمت فلاناً فهو شريك الكفارة فيما قالوا على الله تعالى مما لا يليق به فكلمه ماذا يجب عليه ؟ قال : كفارة اليمين ا هـ . وأشار المصنف إلى أنه إذا فعل المحلوف عليه لا يكون كافراً لأنه صار يميناً. وقيد بكونه علقه على فعل في المستقبل لأنه لو قال ذلك لشيء قد فعله في الماضي كأن قال إن كنت فعلت كذا فهو كافر وهو عالم أنه قد فعل فهو يمين الغموس لا كفارة فيها إلا التوبة والاستغفار وهل يكفر حتى تكون التوبة اللازمة عليه التوبة من الكفرة وتجديد الإسلام؟ قيل لا . وقيل نعم تنجيز معنی علقه بأمر كائن فكأنه قال ابتداء هو كافر؛ والصحيح أنه إن كان عالماً أنه يمين إما منعقدة أو لا يكفر بالماضي، وإن كان جاهلاً وعنده أنه يكفر بالحلف في الغموس أو بمباشرة الشرط في المستقبل يكفر فيهما لأنه لما أقدم عليه وعنده أنه يكفر فقد رضي بالكفر، كذا في كثير من الكتب. وفي المجتبى والذخيرة والفتوى على أنه إن اعتقد الكفر به يكفر وإلا فلا في المستقبل والماضي جميعاً. وفي قولهم يعلم الله أنه فعل كذا ولم يفعل كذا وهو يعلم خلافه فيه اختلاف المشايخ وعامتهم على أنه يكفر. ثم رقم في المجتبى رقماً آخر : لو قال الله يعمل أني ما فعلت كذا وهو يعلم أنه كاذب فقيل لا يكفر وهو رواية عن أبي يوسف لأنه قصد ترويج الكذب دون الكفر .
The book of oaths. And the vow of Allah, and if he does such-and-such then he is a disbeliever, not by His knowledge, His anger, His wrath, His mercy, the Prophet, and the Quran. From: H. And it is said yes, because he attached meaning to an existing matter, so it is as if he said initially he is a disbeliever. Swearing by Allah's Attributes: Classification and Ruling
Classifying Allah's attributes by custom for oath validity

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to classify Allah's attributes into three categories based on customary usage and determine whether swearing by each constitutes a valid oath, applying the Hanafi principle that custom ('urf) governs oath validity.

Core Idea
The validity of an oath by Allah's attributes depends on how people customarily use that attribute.

In this passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq, Ibn Nujaym explains that swearing by Allah's attributes is not automatically an oath. Instead, the ruling hinges on customary usage and the swearer's intention. The Hanafi school categorizes attributes into three types, each with distinct rules. Understanding this classification helps avoid unintended oaths and ensures that expiation is applied correctly when required.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three categories of attributes
From al-Bada'i, attributes are divided into: (1) those used only for Allah (e.g., might, greatness) — swearing by them is an oath; (2) those used for Allah and others equally (e.g., power, will) — also an oath unless a different intention; (3) those predominantly used for non-Allah (e.g., mercy, anger) — not an oath unless the attribute itself is intended.
The key is how people customarily use the word.
2
Apply the alternative custom-based view
Some Hanafi shaykhs state: whatever people customarily treat as an oath is an oath, except where the Law prohibits. This simplifies the classification to common practice.
This view is more practical but may lead to variation by region.
3
Analyze specific examples given in the text
The text lists examples: 'By the might of Allah' is an oath; 'By the mercy of Allah' is not an oath unless intended. 'By the power of Allah' is disputed: al-Zahiriyyah says no, but the author sides with al-Walwalijiyyah that it is an oath because using 'power' for 'determination' is rare.
Note the authority levels: al-Asl (zahir al-riwayah), al-Walwalijiyyah (later fatwa).
4
Distinguish between swearing by attributes and by the name 'Allah'
Swearing by Allah's name ('Wallahi') is always an oath. Swearing by attributes is conditional. The text notes that phrases like 'La ilaha illa Allah' are not oaths unless intended.
The attribute is not equivalent to the name.
5
Determine the mufta bihi for disputed attributes
For 'amanat Allah', the mufta bihi from al-Asl is that it is an oath, contra al-Tahawi. For 'qudrat Allah', the mufta bihi is that it is an oath, following al-Walwalijiyyah. The author rejects al-Zahiriyyah's view.
The tarjih is based on frequency of usage and the principle that ambiguity is resolved in favor of oath validity.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (لا) بعلمه وغضبه وسخطه ورحمته أي لا يكون اليمين بعلم الله ونحوه لأن الحلف بهذه الألفاظ غير متعارف والعرف معتبر في الخلف بالصفات ولأن العلم يذكر ويراد به المعلوم ويقال اللهم اغفر علمك فينا أي معلومك ولأن الرحمة يراد بها أثرها وهو المطر والجنة، والغضب والسخط يراد بهما العقوبة. وفي البدائع وأما الصفة فصفات الله تعالى مع أنها كلها لذاته على ثلاثة أقسام : منها ما لا يستعمل في عرف الناس وعاداتهم إلا في نفسها فالحلف بها يكون يميناً، ومنها ما يستعمل في الصفة وفي غيرها استعمالاً على السواء والحلف بها يكون يميناً أيضاً، ومنها ما يستعمل في الصفة وفي غيرها لكن استعمالها في غير الصفة هو الغالب فالحلف بها لا يكون يميناً. ومن مشايخنا من قال : ما تعارفه الناس يميناً يكون يميناً إلا ما ورد الشرع بالنهي عنه، وما لم يتعارفوه لا يكون يميناً، وبيان هذه الجملة إذا قال وعزة الله وعظمته وجلاله وكبريائه يكون حالفاً، وكذا وقدرة الله ما لم ينو المقدور وكذا وقوته وإرادته ومشيئته ورضاه ومحبته وإرادته وكلامه بخلاف الرحمة والغضب والسخط والعلم إلا إذا أراد به الصفة وأما وسلطان الله فقال القدوري : إن أراد به القدرة كان حالفاً وإلا فلا. ولو قال وأمانة الله ذكر في الأصل أنه يكون يميناً خلافاً للطحاوي لأنها طاعته، ووجه ما في الأصل أن الأمانة المضافة إلى الله تعالى عنه القسم يراد بها صفته . ولو ووجه الله فهو يمين لأن الوجه المضاف إلى الله تعالى يراد به الذات. ولو قال لا إله إلا الله لا أفعل كذا لا يكون يميناً إلا أن ينوي وكذا قوله سبحان الله والله أكبر لا أفعل كذا لعدم العادة، وملكوت الله وجبروته يمين من صفاته تعالى التي لا تستعمل إلا في الصفة ا هـ. ومن الغريب ما في الظهيرية لو قال وقدرة الله لا يكون يميناً وإن كان الله تعالى لا يوصف بضدها لأن المراد بالقدرة المذكورة التقدير عرفاً على ما عرف في الزيادات والله عز وجل قد يقدر وقد لا يقدر اهـ. وهو مردود لما في الولوالجية وغيرها : لو قال وقدرة الله كان يميناً لأن استعمال القدرة على المقدور به لم يكثر ككثرة استعمال العلم على المعلوم حتى لو نوى المقدور لا يكون يميناً ا هـ . وأشار المصنف إلى أنه لو قال وعذاب الله وثوابه ورضاه ولعنة الله وأمانته أنه لا يكون يميناً، وفي الخانية : لو قال بصفة الله لا أفعل كذا لا يكون يميناً لأن من صفاته ما يذكر في غيره فلا يكون ذكر الصفة كذكر الاسم.
His saying: '(Not) by His knowledge, His anger, His wrath, His mercy' i.e., the oath is not (valid) by Allah's knowledge and the like, because swearing by these expressions is not customary, and custom is considered in oaths by attributes, and because knowledge is mentioned and what is meant is the known (object), and it is said 'O Allah, forgive Your knowledge in us' meaning Your known (object), and because mercy is intended by its effect, which is rain and Paradise, and anger and wrath are intended by their punishment. And in al-Bada'i: As for the attribute, the attributes of Allah the Exalted, although they are all [related] to His essence, are of three types: Among them are those that in the custom and habits of people are not used except for themselves, so swearing by them is an oath; among them are those that are used for the attribute and for other things equally, and swearing by them is also an oath; among them are those that are used for the attribute and for other things, but their use for other things is predominant, so swearing by them is not an oath. And some of our shaykhs said: What people customarily consider an oath is an oath, except what the Law has forbidden, and what they do not customarily consider is not an oath. The explanation of this statement: If he says 'By the might of Allah, by His greatness, by His majesty, by His pride,' he is swearing; similarly, by the power of Allah unless he intends the thing measured; similarly by His strength, His will, His wish, His pleasure, His love, His will, His speech, as opposed to mercy, anger, wrath, and knowledge, unless he intends the attribute. As for 'by the authority of Allah,' al-Quduri said: If he intends power then he is swearing, otherwise not. And if he says 'by the trust of Allah,' it is mentioned in al-Asl that it is an oath, contrary to al-Tahawi because it is His obedience, and the basis in al-Asl is that the trust attributed to Allah the Exalted in swearing is intended as His attribute. And if he says 'by the face of Allah,' it is an oath because the face attributed to Allah the Exalted is intended as the essence. And if he says 'there is no god but Allah, I will not do such-and-such,' it is not an oath unless he intends; similarly his saying 'Glory be to Allah,' 'Allah is Most Great,' 'I will not do such-and-such' due to lack of custom. And 'the dominion of Allah' and 'the power of Allah' are an oath from His attributes that are not used except for the attribute. And among the strange things is what is in al-Zahiriyyah: If he says 'by the power of Allah,' it is not an oath, even though Allah the Exalted is not described by its opposite, because what is meant by the mentioned power is determination (taqdir) customarily, as is known in al-Ziyadat, and Allah the Exalted may determine or may not determine. But this is rejected because of what is in al-Walwalijiyyah and others: If he says 'by the power of Allah,' it is an oath because the use of power in the sense of the determined object is not as frequent as the frequent use of knowledge in the sense of the known, so that if he intended the determined object, it would not be an oath. And the author indicated that if he says 'by the punishment of Allah, His reward, His pleasure, His curse, His trust,' it is not an oath. And in al-Khaniyyah: If he says 'by an attribute of Allah, I will not do such-and-such,' it is not an oath because among His attributes are those that are mentioned in other contexts, so mentioning the attribute is not like mentioning the name.
Source pages p. 481

Commentary
This passage explains that swearing by Allah's attributes is not automatically an oath; it depends on customary usage. The author, quoting al-Bada'i, divides attributes into three categories: (1) attributes used only for Allah (e.g., might, greatness) – swearing by them is an oath; (2) attributes used both for Allah and other things equally (e.g., power, will) – also an oath unless the swearer intends something else; (3) attributes predominantly used for other things (e.g., mercy, anger) – not an oath unless the intention is the attribute itself. A later opinion from some Hanafi scholars bases the ruling entirely on custom: whatever people commonly treat as an oath is one, except where prohibited. The text then gives specific examples: swearing by Allah's face, by His trust (al-amanah) is an oath, but swearing by His punishment or reward is not. There is a notable dispute about 'power of Allah': al-Dhakhirah considers it an oath, while al-Zahiriyyah does not, but the author sides with al-Walwalijiyyah that it is an oath because using 'power' for 'determination' is rare. Overall, the ruling is tied to linguistic custom (urf) and intention.

Key Terms
صفات الله (sifat Allah): Attributes of Allah, such as knowledge, power, mercy. The text classifies them based on customary usage to determine if swearing by them is an oath.
عرف (urf): Customary usage among people. It is the key determinant for whether swearing by an attribute constitutes an oath.
قدرة الله (qudrat Allah): The power of Allah. The passage discusses whether swearing by it is an oath, with a dispute between al-Zahiriyyah and al-Walwalijiyyah.
أمانة الله (amanat Allah): The trust of Allah. The text notes a difference between al-Asl (oath) and al-Tahawi (not an oath).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which attribute, when sworn by, is NOT an oath unless the swearer specifically intends the attribute itself?
A) The might of Allah
B) The greatness of Allah
C) The mercy of Allah
D) The power of Allah

Key Takeaway
The validity of an oath by Allah's attributes is determined by customary usage and intention, not by the mere mention of an attribute.

Swearing by Other Than Allah: The Ruling on Invalid Oaths
Stating the ruling that swearing by the Prophet, Quran, or Kaaba does not constitute a valid oath

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on swearing by the Prophet, Quran, or Kaaba and identify the proof from the hadith.

Core Idea
Swearing by other than Allah is not a valid oath; the Prophet commanded us to swear only by Allah or remain silent.

This lesson examines a short but important fiqh ruling: swearing by the Prophet Muhammad, the Quran, or the Kaaba does not constitute a valid oath in the Hanafi school. The reason is that oaths are only valid when they invoke Allah by His Names or Attributes. The text cites a clear hadith prohibiting swearing by other than Allah, and distinguishes between swearing by created entities and swearing by the Quran, which is a unique case.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What is the act being ruled upon? (Swearing by the Prophet, Quran, or Kaaba.) What is the ruling? (It is not a valid oath; no expiation is required if broken.)
This is the core takeaway of the passage.
2
Locate the dalil
Find the proof cited by the author. Here it is the hadith: 'Whoever is to swear, let him swear by Allah or remain silent.'
The hadith is narrated by multiple sources (Bukhari, Abu Dawud, etc.).
3
Understand the legal basis
Analyze the dalil. The imperative 'falyahlif' indicates a command to swear by Allah, and the alternative 'aw liyadhar' implies prohibition of swearing by other than Allah. Hence, swearing by any created entity is invalid.
In Hanafi usul, al-amr yufidu al-wujub, and the khitab implies prohibition for the opposite.
4
Distinguish the case of the Quran
The author notes 'swearing by the Quran is different from the first' because the Quran is the speech of Allah, an attribute, so swearing by it is considered swearing by Allah.
This is a known Hanafi position: the Quran is ghayr makhluq and swearing by it is valid.
5
Apply the ruling
If someone says 'By the Prophet, I will do X' and does not do it, no expiation is due. However, such speech is haram and should be avoided.
The ruling is straightforward: invalid oath, no kaffarah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (والنبي والقرآن (والكعبة أي لا يكون حالفاً بها لأن الحلف بالنبي والكعبة حلف بغير الله تعالى لقوله له من كان حالفاً فليحلف بالله أو ليذر » (۱) والحلف بالقرآن غير الأول اهـ. والمراد بالأول هو كون بريء من الله ورسوله يمين واحد وعبارة الذخيرة قريبة من عبارة التتارخانية التي نقلناها .
His saying: '(And the Prophet, the Quran, and the Kaaba)' i.e., he is not swearing by them because swearing by the Prophet and the Kaaba is swearing by other than Allah the Exalted, due to his saying (peace be upon him): 'Whoever is to swear, let him swear by Allah or remain silent.' And swearing by the Quran is different from the first (i.e., the previous discussion). And what is meant by 'the first' is that being innocent of Allah and His Messenger is one oath. And the expression in al-Dhakhirah is close to the expression in al-Tatar Khaniyyah that we have transmitted.
Source pages p. 481

Commentary
This short passage concludes that swearing by the Prophet, the Quran, or the Kaaba does not constitute a valid oath. The reason given is that swearing by other than Allah is prohibited by the hadith: 'Whoever is to swear, let him swear by Allah or remain silent.' Swearing by the Quran is an exception because the Quran is the speech of Allah, which is an attribute, but the author notes that this is a different matter. The reference to 'first' relates back to the earlier discussion about oaths of disavowal. The passage emphasizes that the basis for all oaths is Allah alone.

Key Terms
الكعبة (al-Ka'bah): The sacred house in Mecca; swearing by it is not a valid oath because it is a created object.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling on swearing by the Prophet Muhammad (e.g., 'By the Prophet, I will do X')?
A) It is a valid oath and expiation is required if broken
B) It is not a valid oath because it is swearing by other than Allah
C) It is valid only if the swearer intends the Prophet's honor
D) It is valid but makruh

Key Takeaway
An oath is only valid if made by Allah or His attributes; swearing by created things, including the Prophet, is not a valid oath and does not require expiation.

The Three Categories of Allah's Attributes in Oaths (Hanafi Classification)
Classification of divine attributes for oath validity based on custom.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to classify Allah's attributes into three categories based on customary usage and determine whether swearing by each constitutes a valid oath.

Core Idea
An oath is valid only if sworn by an attribute customarily exclusive to Allah; custom ('urf) is the decisive criterion.

In this passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq, al-Marghinani expands on the Hanafi classification of Allah's attributes for oaths. The ruling is not based on the attribute's essence but on how people customarily use it. Understanding this classification will help you apply the correct ruling to common oath expressions in daily life.

Guided Path
1
Understand the three-category system
The passage divides attributes into three types based on 'urf: (1) exclusively divine, (2) used equally for Allah and others, (3) predominantly used for others. Each has a default ruling on whether swearing by it is a valid oath.
Note that the second category automatically forms an oath, while the third requires intention.
2
Identify the role of 'urf
Custom ('urf) is the benchmark. An attribute's classification depends on how people commonly use it in speech, not on theological definitions. This is a hallmark of Hanafi fiqh.
This contrasts with schools that rely on linguistic analysis alone.
3
Apply classification to examples
Work through the examples: 'izzah (might), 'azamah (greatness) are first category → oath; qudrah (power) is second → oath unless intending the empowered; rahmah (mercy) is third → not an oath unless intending the attribute.
Memorize the key examples provided in the text.
4
Recognize intra-Hanafi disagreements
Note the differences: al-Tahawi on 'amanah (trust) and al-Zahiriyya on qudrah. The relied-upon (mufta bihi) position follows the majority: 'amanah is an oath, qudrah is an oath.
These disagreements show that even within the school, custom can be interpreted differently.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وفي البدائع وأما الصفة فصفات الله تعالى مع أنها كلها لذاته على ثلاثة أقسام : منها ما لا يستعمل في عرف الناس وعاداتهم إلا في نفسها فالحلف بها يكون يميناً، ومنها ما يستعمل في الصفة وفي غيرها استعمالاً على السواء والحلف بها يكون يميناً أيضاً، ومنها ما يستعمل في الصفة وفي غيرها لكن استعمالها في غير الصفة هو الغالب فالحلف بها لا يكون يميناً. ومن مشايخنا من قال : ما تعارفه الناس يميناً يكون يميناً إلا ما ورد الشرع بالنهي عنه، وما لم يتعارفوه لا يكون يميناً، وبيان هذه الجملة إذا قال وعزة الله وعظمته وجلاله وكبريائه يكون حالفاً، وكذا وقدرة الله ما لم ينو المقدور وكذا وقوته وإرادته ومشيئته ورضاه ومحبته وإرادته وكلامه بخلاف الرحمة والغضب والسخط والعلم إلا إذا أراد به الصفة وأما وسلطان الله فقال القدوري : إن أراد به القدرة كان حالفاً وإلا فلا. ولو قال وأمانة الله ذكر في الأصل أنه يكون يميناً خلافاً للطحاوي لأنها طاعته، ووجه ما في الأصل أن الأمانة المضافة إلى الله تعالى عنه القسم يراد بها صفته . ولو ووجه الله فهو يمين لأن الوجه المضاف إلى الله تعالى يراد به الذات. ولو قال لا إله إلا الله لا أفعل كذا لا يكون يميناً إلا أن ينوي وكذا قوله سبحان الله والله أكبر لا أفعل كذا لعدم العادة، وملكوت الله وجبروته يمين من صفاته تعالى التي لا تستعمل إلا في الصفة ا هـ. ومن الغريب ما في الظهيرية لو قال وقدرة الله لا يكون يميناً وإن كان الله تعالى لا يوصف بضدها لأن المراد بالقدرة المذكورة التقدير عرفاً على ما عرف في الزيادات والله عز وجل قد يقدر وقد لا يقدر اهـ. وهو مردود لما في الولوالجية وغيرها : لو قال وقدرة الله كان يميناً لأن استعمال القدرة على المقدور به لم يكثر ككثرة استعمال العلم على المعلوم حتى لو نوى المقدور لا يكون يميناً ا هـ . وأشار المصنف إلى أنه لو قال وعذاب الله وثوابه ورضاه ولعنة الله وأمانته أنه لا يكون يميناً، وفي الخانية : لو قال بصفة الله لا أفعل كذا لا يكون يميناً لأن من صفاته ما يذكر في غيره فلا يكون ذكر الصفة كذكر الاسم.
And in al-Bada'i: As for the attribute, the attributes of Allah Almighty, even though all of them are [related] to His essence, are of three types: Among them is that which is not used in the custom and habits of people except for the attribute itself, so swearing by it is an oath. Among them is that which is used for the attribute and for other things equally, so swearing by it is also an oath. Among them is that which is used for the attribute and for other things, but its use for other than the attribute is predominant, so swearing by it is not an oath. And some of our scholars said: Whatever people customarily consider an oath is an oath, except what the Shari'ah has prohibited, and whatever they do not customarily consider is not an oath. Explanation of this summary: If one says, 'By the might of Allah, His greatness, His majesty, His grandeur,' he is swearing. Similarly, 'By the power of Allah,' unless he intends [His] power over something. Similarly, 'By His strength, His will, His desire, His pleasure, His love, His will, His speech,' as opposed to mercy, anger, wrath, and knowledge, unless he intends the attribute. As for 'By the authority of Allah,' al-Quduri said: If he intends power, he is swearing; otherwise not. And if one says, 'By the trust of Allah,' it is mentioned in al-Asl that it is an oath, contrary to al-Tahawi, because trust is His obedience. The justification in al-Asl is that the trust added to Allah Almighty is intended by oath to be His attribute. And if one says, 'By the face of Allah,' it is an oath because the face added to Allah Almighty is intended to mean the essence. And if one says, 'There is no god but Allah, I will not do such-and-such,' it is not an oath unless he intends [it as such]. Similarly, his saying, 'Glory be to Allah' and 'Allah is Great,' 'I will not do such-and-such' due to lack of custom. And 'By the dominion of Allah and His power' is an oath from among His attributes that are not used except for the attribute. End quote. And among the strange things is what is in al-Zahiriyya: If he says, 'By the power of Allah,' it is not an oath, even though Allah Almighty is not described by its opposite, because what is meant by the mentioned power is [His] decree customarily, as is known in al-Ziyadat, and Allah Almighty may decree and may not decree, end quote. This is rejected because what is in al-Walwaljiah and other works: If he says, 'By the power of Allah,' it is an oath, because the use of power for what is empowered has not become as frequent as the use of knowledge for the known, such that if he intends the empowered thing, it is not an oath. End quote. And the author indicated that if he says, 'By the punishment of Allah, His reward, His pleasure, the curse of Allah, and His trust,' that it is not an oath. And in al-Khaniyyah: If he says, 'By the attribute of Allah, I will not do such-and-such,' it is not an oath, because among His attributes are those that are mentioned in connection with other things, so mentioning the attribute is not like mentioning the name.
Source pages p. 481

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq is an expansion (sharh) on the ruling of oaths sworn by Allah's attributes. It opens by presenting the classification from al-Bada'i: attributes are divided into three categories based on customary usage. The first category consists of attributes that are never used except for Allah in common parlance—swearing by these (like 'izzah, 'azamah, etc.) constitutes a valid oath. The second category comprises attributes used equally for Allah and for other things—swearing by these is also an oath. The third category includes attributes predominantly used for other than Allah—swearing by these is not an oath unless one intends the attribute itself. The author then provides examples for each category, including specific rulings on 'power' (qudrah), 'authority' (sultan), 'trust' (amanah), 'face' (wajh), and expressions like 'la ilaha illa Allah'. A minority view from al-Zahiriyya that swearing by 'qudrah' is not an oath is rejected as strange. The correct Hanafi position, following al-Walwaljiah, is that it is an oath. The author also notes that swearing by expressions like 'punishment of Allah' or 'trust of Allah' is not an oath, and that swearing by 'the attribute of Allah' is not an oath because attributes can apply to others.

Key Terms
الصفة (al-sifah): An attribute of Allah, such as might, greatness, etc., which may be used as a basis for swearing an oath.
اليمين (al-yamin): An oath that is legally binding, triggering expiation if broken.
العرف (al-'urf): Common custom and usage of people in speech, which determines whether an expression is considered an oath.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi classification, which of the following is NOT a valid oath?
A) وعزة الله (By the might of Allah)
B) وقدرة الله (By the power of Allah) without intending the empowered thing
C) ورحمة الله (By the mercy of Allah) without intending the attribute
D) وجلاله (By His majesty)

Key Takeaway
The validity of an oath sworn by an attribute of Allah depends on customary usage: exclusive attributes automatically form an oath, equally-used attributes also form an oath, and predominantly other-used attributes require intention to be an oath.

Swearing by the Prophet, Quran, and Kaaba
Ruling on invalidity of oaths by other than Allah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on swearing by the Prophet, Quran, and Kaaba, and explain the proof from the hadith.

Core Idea
An oath is only by Allah or His names/attributes; swearing by a creation is not a valid oath.

In this lesson, we examine a ruling from Kanz al-Daqaiq: that swearing by the Prophet, the Quran, or the Kaaba does not constitute a binding Islamic oath. The author cites the famous hadith commanding oaths only by Allah. Understanding this distinction is crucial for knowing when an oath becomes binding and when expiation is required.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is swearing by the Prophet, Quran, or Kaaba. The ruling is that such swearing is not a valid oath (yamin). It does not create a binding obligation, and breaking it does not require expiation (kaffarah).
2
Locate the dalil
The author cites the hadith: 'Whoever is to swear, let him swear by Allah or be silent' (مَن كَانَ حَالِفًا فَلْيَحْلِفْ بِاللَّهِ أَوْ لِيَذَرْ). This is a sound hadith narrated by Bukhari and others.
The hadith is the primary proof.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The imperative 'فليحلف' indicates obligation (wujub) to swear only by Allah, and the alternative 'أو ليذر' (or be silent) implies prohibition of swearing by other than Allah. Since the Prophet and Kaaba are creations, swearing by them falls under the prohibition.
The Quran, as speech of Allah, is debated, but the Hanafi ruling treats it similarly.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Some scholars (e.g., Hanbalis) consider swearing by the Quran valid because it is the uncreated speech of Allah. The Hanafis generally do not, as common custom ('urf) does not treat it as an oath, and the hadith's generality includes it.
The difference stems from theological views on the Quran's nature.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi tarjih
The Hanafi position (mufta bihi) is that swearing by the Prophet, Quran, or Kaaba is not a valid oath. This is based on the hadith and the principle that oaths must be by Allah or His attributes. The view is supported by the majority of Hanafi scholars.
The ruling is from Zahir al-Riwayah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (والنبي والقرآن والكعبة أي لا يكون حالفاً بها لأن الحلف بالنبي والكعبة حلف بغير الله تعالى لقوله ﷺ « من كان حالفاً فليحلف بالله أو ليذر » (۱) والحلف بالقرآن غير الأول اهـ. والمراد بالأول هو كون بريء من الله ورسوله يمين واحد وعبارة الذخيرة قريبة من عبارة التتارخانية التي نقلناها . (۱) رواه البخاري في كتاب الأيمان باب ٤. أبو داود في كتاب الأيمان باب ٤. الترمذي في كتاب النذور باب ٩. النسائي في كتاب الأيمان باب .٤ الموطأ في كتاب النذور حديث ١٤. أحمد في مسنده (١/ ٤٧( )١١/٢، ٣٤ . البحر الرائق/ ج ٤/ م ٣١
His saying: (And the Prophet, the Quran, and the Kaaba) means he is not an oath-taker by them, because swearing by the Prophet and the Kaaba is swearing by other than Allah Almighty due to his saying ﷺ: 'Whoever is to swear, let him swear by Allah or be silent.' And swearing by the Quran is other than the first. End. And what is meant by 'the first' is that being free from Allah and His Messenger is one oath. And the expression of al-Dhakhirah is close to the expression of al-Tatar Khaniyyah which we have transmitted.
Source pages p. 481

Commentary
This passage is from the sharh of the matn 'Kanz al-Daqa'iq' and addresses the ruling on oaths sworn by the Prophet, the Quran, or the Kaaba. The author clarifies that swearing by any of these is not a valid oath (yamin) because it is swearing by other than Allah. He cites the hadith of the Prophet (ﷺ): 'Whoever is to swear, let him swear by Allah or be silent.' This hadith, narrated by al-Bukhari and others, establishes that oaths should only be by Allah. Swearing by the Prophet or Kaaba is clearly by a created being, so it is not an oath. As for the Quran, there is nuance: if one swears by the Quran, it might be considered swearing by the speech of Allah, which is an attribute, but the author notes that it is 'other than the first' meaning it differs from the previous case. The discussion alludes to the theological debate about whether the Quran is created or uncreated; if one considers it created, then swearing by it is swearing by something created. However, the Hanafi position is that the Quran is the uncreated speech of Allah, but for legal purposes, the ruling is that swearing by the Quran is not an oath because common custom (urf) does not treat it as such, as indicated by the author later.

Key Terms
النبي (al-nabi): The Prophet Muhammad (ﷺ). Swearing by him is considered swearing by a creation, not by the Creator.
القرآن (al-qur'an): The Quran, the speech of Allah. Swearing by it is debated; Hanafis generally do not consider it a valid oath.
الكعبة (al-ka'bah): The Kaaba in Mecca. Swearing by it is prohibited as it is a created object.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Because the Prophet did not allow it
B) Because it is swearing by other than Allah, which is prohibited by hadith
C) Because it is disrespectful
D) Because it requires a special intention

Key Takeaway
Swearing by any created being or object is not a valid Islamic oath; only oaths by Allah or His attributes are binding.

Swearing by Haqq Allah – Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Intra-Hanafi dispute on the validity of swearing by 'Haqq Allah'.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the intra-Hanafi positions on swearing by 'Haqq Allah' and identify the thamarah al-khilaf (practical consequence) regarding expiation.

Core Idea
The validity of an oath by 'Haqq Allah' hinges on whether 'haqq' is an attribute or created obedience – custom settles the tarjih.

This passage from Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq delves into a subtle intra-Hanafi disagreement: does swearing by 'Haqq Allah' constitute a binding oath? The answer depends on how one interprets 'haqq' – is it an attribute of Allah, or does it mean the obedience owed to Him? The dispute has practical consequences for whether breaking the oath requires expiation. Let's examine the positions and the role of custom in the final tarjih.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the core question
We are dealing with the phrase 'Haqq Allah' used in an oath. The question: is it a valid oath (yamin) or not?
This is a linguistic and jurisprudential issue, not about intention alone.
2
Map the intra-Hanafi positions
State the views of Abu Hanifa and Muhammad al-Shaybani (not an oath) and the two narrations from Abu Yusuf (one not an oath, one it is an oath). Note the later preferred view (al-mukhtar) from al-Ikhtiyar.
The dispute is recorded in the classical sources; the later view relies on custom.
3
Analyze the dalil of each position
Understand the evidence: Abu Hanifa's group says 'haqq' means obedience (created), so swearing by it is swearing by other than Allah. The other group says 'haqq' is a divine attribute (al-Haqq), so it is swearing by Allah. Custom reinforces the attribute interpretation.
The linguistic analysis of 'haqq' is the core of the dispute.
4
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf and the mufta bihi
The practical consequence: if it is not an oath, no expiation; if it is, expiation is required. The later preferred view (mufta bihi) says it is an oath due to custom, so expiation is required.
This shows how custom ('urf) can influence tarjih even within a madhhab.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (وحق الله أي لا يكون يميناً وهو قول أبي حنيفة وهو قول محمد وإحدى الروايتين عن أبي يوسف، وعنه رواية أخرى أنه يكون يميناً لأن الحق من صفات الله تعالى وهو حقيقة فصار كأنه قال والله الحق والحلف به متعارف ولهما أنه يراد به طاعة الله إذ الطاعات حقوقه فيكون حلفاً بغير الله تعالى. وذكر في الاختيار أن المختار أنه يكون يميناً اعتباراً بالعرف اهـ. قيد بالحق المضاف لأنه لو قال والحق يكون يميناً ولو قال حقاً لا يكون يميناً لأن المنكر منه يراد به تحقيق الوعد فكأنه قال افعل كذا حقيقة لا محالة وهذا قول البعض والصحيح أنه إن أراد اسم الله تعالى يكون يميناً ؛ كذا في الخانية. وفي المجتبى : وحقاً أو حقاً اختلاف المشايخ والأكثر على أنه ليس بيمين والحاصل أن الحق إما أن يكون معرفاً أو
His saying: (And the right of Allah) means it is not an oath. This is the saying of Abu Hanifah and the saying of Muhammad and one of the two narrations from Abu Yusuf. From him is another narration that it is an oath, because 'the right' is among the attributes of Allah Almighty and it is real, so it is as if he said, 'By Allah, the True,' and swearing by it is customary. Their [Abu Yusuf and Muhammad's] evidence is that what is meant by it is the obedience of Allah, since acts of obedience are His rights, so it becomes swearing by other than Allah Almighty. And it is mentioned in al-Ikhtiyar that the preferred view is that it is an oath, considering custom. End. Restriction is made to the added 'right' because if he says 'And the right' without addition, it is an oath; and if he says 'right' without definite article, it is not an oath, because the indefinite form is intended to emphasize the promise, as if he said 'I will do such-and-such truly, undoubtedly.' This is the saying of some; the correct view is that if he intends the name of Allah Almighty, it is an oath. Thus in al-Khaniyyah. And in al-Mujtaba: 'And right' or 'right' – there is difference of opinion among the scholars; the majority is that it is not an oath. The conclusion is that 'the right' is either definite or...
Source pages p. 482

Commentary
This passage discusses the intra-Hanafi dispute on the phrase 'Haqq Allah' (the right of Allah) as an oath. Abu Hanifa, Muhammad al-Shaybani, and one narration from Abu Yusuf hold that it is not an oath, because 'right' here usually means the obedience owed to Allah, so it is swearing by a created action (obedience), not by an attribute of Allah. Another narration from Abu Yusuf considers it an oath, arguing that 'right' is an attribute of Allah (e.g., 'Allah is the Truth') and since it is a divine attribute, swearing by it is like swearing by Allah. The author of al-Ikhtiyar prefers the view that it is an oath considering the common custom of people using it as an oath. The passage then distinguishes definite and indefinite forms: 'al-Haqq' with the definite article is an oath, while 'Haqq' (indefinite) is not, unless one intends Allah's name. The majority view in al-Mujtaba is that it is not an oath. The practical consequence: if someone says 'Haqq Allah, I will not do X' and then breaks it, according to Abu Hanifa no expiation is required, but according to the preferred view (al-mukhtar) expiation is required.

Key Terms
حق الله (haqq allah): Literally 'the right of Allah'; used in oaths. Disputed whether it refers to the attribute of Allah or to the obedience due to Him.
العرف (al-'urf): Custom, common practice. In later Hanafi fatwa, custom is given weight to determine if an expression is an oath.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Hanifa, what is the ruling if someone says 'Haqq Allah, I will not do this' and then does it?
A) It is a valid oath, expiation is required
B) It is not a valid oath, no expiation required
C) It is a sin but no expiation
D) It is valid only if he intends the attribute

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, the ruling on swearing by 'Haqq Allah' depends on interpretation and custom; the later preferred view considers it a valid oath, requiring expiation if broken.

8 min
Swearing by the Qur'an and by Created Beings: Validity and Kufr
Defining valid oaths: swearing by Quran, God's attributes, and self-condemnation expressions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state when swearing by the Qur'an constitutes a valid yamin and when swearing by created things leads to kufr.

Core Idea
Swearing by the Qur'an is valid due to custom; swearing by other than Allah with belief in its obligation is kufr.

This lesson examines two crucial questions: Is swearing by the physical Qur'an a valid oath? And what about swearing by someone's life? The Hanafi school rules based on custom and the danger of equating created things with Allah. We will explore the proofs and the severe warning against swearing by other than Allah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act
What exactly is being ruled upon? Swearing by the Qur'an (the physical mushaf) and swearing by created things like life of the sultan.
2
Understand the objection
The objection: The Qur'an is composed of created letters, so it is a created object, and swearing by creation is not a valid oath.
This objection relies on the fact that only Allah is worthy of oaths.
3
Apply the Hanafi response
The Hanafi response: The Qur'an as revealed speech is uncreated; the letters are a physical manifestation. Custom (urf) makes swearing by the mushaf valid, as people commonly swear by it.
The three Imams (Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad) agree on this ruling.
4
Recognize the ruling
Conclusion: Swearing by the Qur'an is a valid oath. If broken, expiation is required.
5
Analyze the kufr warning
Swearing by created things (e.g., 'by your life', 'by the life of the sultan') with belief that it is obligatory leads to kufr, because it elevates creation to the level of Allah.
The quote from Ibn Mas'ud illustrates the gravity: a false oath by Allah is better than a true oath by other than Allah.

قوله: (وإن فعلته فعلي غضب الله وسخطه أو أنا زان وسارق أو شارب خمر أو أكل ربا) أي لا يكون يميناً. أما في الأول فلأنه دعا على نفسه ولا يتعلق ذلك بالشرط ولأنه غير متعارف، وأما في قوله هو زان إلى آخره فلأن حرمة هذه الأشياء تحتمل النسخ والتبديل فلم تكن في معنى حرمة اسم الله تعالى ولأنه ليس بمتعارف؛ كذا في الهداية. والأولى الاقتصار على أنه ليس بمتعارف لأن كون الحرمة تحتمل الارتفاع أو لا تحتمله لا أثر له مع أنه لا حاجة إلى التعليل بعدم التعارف أيضاً لأن معنى اليمين أن يعلق ما امتناعه يوجب عن الفعل بسبب لزوم وجوده عند الفعل، وليس بمجرد وجود الفعل يصير زانياً أو سارقاً لأنه لا إلا بفعل مستأنف يدخل في الوجود ووجود هذه الفعل ليس لازماً لوجود المحلوف عليه حتى يكون موجباً امتناعه عنه فلا يكون يميناً بخلاف الكفر فإنه بالرضا به يكفر من غير توقف على عمل آخر أو اعتقاد والرضا يتحقق بمباشرة الشرط فيوجب عنده الكفر لولا قول من العلماء بالكفارة كما في فتح القدير. وفي المجتبى لو قال هو يأكل الميتة إن فعل كذا أو يستحل الخمر أو الخنزير فليس بيمين؛ أصله أن التعليق بما تسقط حرمته بحال ما كالميتة والخمر والخنزير لا يكون يميناً وما لا يسقط كألفاظ الكفر فيمين. ولو قال فعله المجوس أو اليهود فعلى عنقي إن فعلت كذا ففعل لا شيء عليه ا هـ. وهو يفيد أن استحلال الخمر والخنزير ليس بكفر إلا أن يقال إن جزاء الشرط هو الاستحلال في المستقبل بخلاف ما لو قال إن فعلت كذا فأنا مستحل للخمر والخنزير. وفي الولوالجية : وأما في

Book of Oaths. And the Ka'ba, and the right of God, and if I do it then upon me is the wrath of God and His displeasure, or I am an adulterer, or a thief, or a drinker of wine, or an eater of usury. It is customary, although it is intended by it the letters and inscriptions in Fath al-Qadir. Then it is not hidden that swearing by the Qur'an now is customary, so it is an oath as is the saying of the three Imams. The reasoning that it is not an oath because it is other than the Exalted, since it is created, because it is letters and other than the created is the internal speech, is refuted by the fact that the Qur'an is the speech of Allah, revealed, uncreated. And it is not hidden that the revealed in reality is only the letters that have passed and ceased to exist, and that which is proven pre-eternal is impossible to cease. However, they required that because the common people, if told that the Qur'an is created, they transgress to speech absolutely. As for swearing by the speech of Allah the Exalted, it must revolve with custom. As for swearing by Jan Mureed and similar, like swearing by the life of your head and the life of the sultan, then if he believes that acting righteously thereby is obligatory, he disbelieves. In Tatimmat al-Fatawa, Ali al-Razi said: I fear for the one who says 'by my life and your life' that he disbelieves, and were it not that the common people say it not knowing, I would say it is shirk. From Ibn Mas'ud: 'That I swear by Allah falsely is dearer to me than to swear by other than Allah truthfully.' End quote. He restricted by swearing by these things because disassociating from them is an oath, like his saying 'I am disassociated from the Prophet if I do such' as we have detailed before. And the author indicated that if he said 'by the religion of Allah, and His obedience, or His limits, or His law, or the mus-haf', it is not an oath a fortiori, as in al-Khaniyya. His saying: (And the right of Allah, i.e., it is not an oath, and this is the saying of Abu Hanifa, and it is the saying of Muhammad and one of the two narrations from Abu Yusuf; and from him is another narration that it is an oath, because 'right' is among the attributes of Allah the Exalted, and it is literal, so it becomes as if he said 'by Allah, the Truth', and swearing by it is customary. And for them (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), it is intended by it the obedience of Allah, since acts of obedience are His rights, so it is an oath by other than Allah the Exalted. And it is mentioned in al-Ikhtiyar that the chosen opinion is that it is an oath, considering custom. End quote. He restricted by the possessive construction (right of Allah) because if he said 'and al-Haqq' (the Truth), it is an oath, and if he said 'haqqan', it is not an oath, because the indefinite form is intended to affirm the promise, as if he said 'do such truthfully without doubt'. And this is the saying of some, and the correct is that if he intends the name of Allah the Exalted, it is an oath. Thus in al-Khaniyya. In al-Mujtaba: 'and haqqan or haqqan' – the mashayikh differ, and the majority is that it is not an oath. And the summary is that al-haqq is either definite or indefinite in usage. His saying: (And His trust) contradicts what he mentioned earlier from al-Asl, that it is an oath, contrary to al-Tahawi. His saying: (And it is mentioned in al-Ikhtiyar etc.) Al-Nahr said: He refuted it in Fath al-Qadir by saying that customariness after the attribute is shared between the attribute of Allah the Exalted and the attribute of others, and the word 'haqq' does not immediately indicate what is an attribute of Allah, but rather what is from His rights. His saying: (And haqqan or haqqan) al-Ramli said: meaning with waw and without waw. His saying: (And in the possessive construction, if it is with ba, then it is an oath by agreement). He weakened it in al-Fath where he said: And among the weak sayings is what al-Balkhi said that his saying 'bi-haqq illah' is an oath because people swear by it, and he weakened it because it is like 'wa-haqq illah' in the possessive, and you know the difference in it and that it is not an oath, so likewise 'bi-haqq illah'. His saying: (Then there is the previous difference) i.e., mentioned first after the words of the text. His saying: (And because it is not customary) al-Nahr said: The apparent of their words is that if they got accustomed to swearing by it, it would be an oath; and the apparent of what is in al-Fath is that if it became customary to swear by it, it is not an oath, where he said: The meaning of the oath is that he suspends... up to what comes. Book of Oaths. Wine or eater of usury, and its letters are the ba, waw, and ta, and may be implicit, and its expiation is freeing a slave or feeding ten (poor). (These) indefinite or in possessive construction. So al-haqq definite, whether with waw or with ba, is an oath by agreement as in al-Khaniyya and al-Zahira. And indefinite is an oath according to the most correct opinion if he intends, and possessive construction: if it is with ba, then it is an oath by agreement because people swear by it; if with waw, then there is the previous difference, and the chosen is that it is an oath as before. And by this it is known that the chosen is that it is an oath in the three phrases absolutely. And the author indicated that if he said 'by the right of the Messenger' or 'by the right of faith' or 'by the right of mosques' or 'by the right of fasting' or 'prayer', it is not an oath; thus in al-Khaniyya. And in al-Mujtaba, 'the sanctity of Allah' is analogous to his saying 'and the right of Allah'. In Fatawa al-Nasafi: 'By the sanctity of the testimony of Allah' and 'by the sanctity of la ilaha illa Allah' is not an oath. It becomes likewise. His saying: (And if I do it then upon me is the wrath of Allah and His displeasure, or I am an adulterer, thief, wine-drinker, or eater of usury) i.e., it is not an oath. As for the first, because he invoked upon himself and that is not connected to the condition, and because it is not customary. As for his saying 'he is an adulterer' etc., because the sanctity of these things is subject to abrogation and change, so they are not in the meaning of the sanctity of the name of Allah the Exalted, and because it is not customary; thus in al-Hidaya. And the preferred is to restrict to it not being customary, because the sanctity being subject to elevation or not has no effect, especially since there is no need for the rationale of lack of customariness as well, because the meaning of the oath is to suspend something whose prevention causes (deterrence) from the action due to the necessity of its existence upon the action. And it is not that by mere existence of the action he becomes an adulterer or thief, because it only (occurs) by a subsequent action that comes into existence, and the existence of this action is not necessary for the existence of the thing sworn upon, such that it would prevent him from it. So it is not an oath, contrary to disbelief, for by consenting to it he disbelieves without waiting for another action or belief, and consent is realized by performing the condition, so it necessitates disbelief for him, were it not for the saying of some scholars regarding expiation, as in Fath al-Qadir. And in al-Mujtaba: If he said 'he eats carrion if he does such' or 'he considers wine or pork lawful', it is not an oath; its principle is that suspending upon something whose sanctity falls away in some situation, like carrion, wine, pork, is not an oath; and what does not fall away, like words of disbelief, is an oath. And if he said 'the action of the Magians or Jews is upon my neck if I do such', then he does it, there is nothing upon him. End quote. And it indicates that considering wine and pork lawful is not disbelief, unless it is said that the consequence of the condition is future consideration, contrary to if he said 'if I do such, then I am considering wine and pork lawful'. And in al-Walwaljiyya: And regarding... his saying: (Subject to abrogation and change, i.e., subject to dropping. As for wine, it is apparent; as for theft, it is in case of necessity to eat another's property, and likewise if a woman is coerced with a sword to commit adultery; and as for adultery, it is in dar al-harb.) Thus in al-Nahr, and its origin is from al-Fath, and the saying of al-Tibyan: because it is subject to change rationally, so it is not like disbelief in sanctity, indicates the lack of restriction to those situations as is apparent from al-Hidaya. His saying: (Because the meaning of the oath is to suspend something that necessitates...) i.e., to suspend something like disbelief, which necessitates that thing preventing the oath-taker from the action sworn upon, like entering.
Source pages p. 482

Commentary
This passage from Al-Bahr al-Raiq, a commentary on Kanz al-Daqaiq, discusses the ruling of various expressions commonly used in oaths and determines which constitute a valid yamin (oath) in Hanafi fiqh. The passage first addresses swearing by the Qur'an: although the Qur'an is composed of letters and is created in its physical form, it is the uncreated speech of Allah. The Hanafi position is that swearing by the Qur'an is now customary ('urf) and therefore constitutes a valid oath, agreeing with the three Imams (Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad). The earlier objection that the Qur'an is created (and thus not sacred like Allah) is refuted by distinguishing between the physical mushaf and the eternal divine speech. Next, the passage discusses swearing by life (e.g., 'by your life' or 'by the life of the sultan'). If the swearer believes that fulfilling an oath by such expressions is obligatory, he commits kufr (disbelief) because such oaths are akin to swearing by other than Allah. Quoting Ali al-Razi, the passage warns that saying 'by my life and your life' could lead to kufr, and Ibn Mas'ud is cited preferring a false oath by Allah over a true oath by other than Allah. The passage then explains that disassociating (tabarri) from something sacred, like saying 'I am disassociated from the Prophet', constitutes an oath. The author notes that saying 'by the religion of Allah, His obedience, limits, law, or the mushaf' does not constitute an oath, because these are not considered names of Allah. The main discussion centers on the phrase 'bi-haqq Allah' (by the right of Allah). Abu Hanifa, Muhammad, and one narration from Abu Yusuf hold that it is not an oath, because 'haqq' commonly means 'obedience' (a right of Allah) and not the attribute of Allah. Another narration from Abu Yusuf says it is an oath because 'haqq' is an attribute of Allah, so it is like saying 'by Allah, the Truth'. The chosen position (al-mukhtar) in al-Ikhtiyar is that it is an oath due to custom. The passage then details rulings for different forms: 'al-Haqq' (definite) is an oath by agreement, whether with waw or ba; 'haqqan' (indefinite) is an oath only if the swearer intends Allah's name; and 'bi-haqq illah' (with ba) is an oath by agreement because it is customary. The passage concludes that the chosen view makes all three forms oaths. Swearing by other sacred things like 'the right of the Messenger' or 'the right of mosques' is not an oath. Finally, the passage discusses self-condemnation expressions like 'upon me is the wrath of Allah' or 'I am an adulterer/thief/wine-drinker/usurer'. These are not oaths, because invoking wrath is a supplication against oneself, not a suspension; and declaring oneself a sinner does not make one instantly a sinner upon the condition, since becoming an adulterer requires a separate act. In contrast, declaring oneself a disbeliever (kafir) upon an action would be an oath, because mere consent to kufr makes one a disbeliever without further action. Thus, the underlying principle: a valid oath must involve suspending something that deters the speaker from the action, such as kufr, and the thing suspended must be immediate upon the action, not contingent on future acts.

Key Terms
يمين (yamin): A binding oath that suspends the occurrence of something upon an action, deterring the person.
متعارف (muta'arif): Customary – used as the basis for considering an expression a valid oath.
كفر (kufr): Disbelief – incurred if one believes swearing by other than Allah is obligatory.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling on swearing by the life of the sultan without believing it is obligatory?
A) It is a valid oath and expiation is required if broken.
B) It is not a valid oath, but it is permissible (mubah).
C) It is not a valid oath and the expression is prohibited (haram).
D) It leads to kufr regardless.

Key Takeaway
Swearing by the Qur'an is a valid oath due to custom; swearing by created beings is prohibited and can lead to kufr if believed obligatory.

The Dispute on 'Haqq Allah' and Self-Condemnation Expressions
Defining valid oaths: swearing by Quran, God's attributes, and self-condemnation expressions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the intra-Hanafi dispute on 'haqq Allah' and state the chosen (mukhtar) position, and distinguish self-condemnation expressions from valid oaths.

Core Idea
'Haqq Allah' is a valid oath according to the chosen view due to custom; self-condemnation is not an oath because it lacks deterrence.

This lesson dives into a classic Hanafi debate: Is saying 'by the right of Allah' (wa-haqq Allah) a valid oath? The imams differed, and the later preferred opinion relies on custom. We also examine why phrases like 'upon me is the wrath of Allah' or 'I am an adulterer' do not constitute oaths, based on the underlying principle of deterrence.

Guided Path
1
State the issue
The phrase 'wa-haqq Allah' – is it a valid yamin? Three positions: Abu Hanifa and Muhammad say no; Abu Yusuf has two narrations; the chosen view says yes due to custom.
The passage also clarifies that 'al-Haqq' (definite) is an oath by agreement.
2
Follow the opposing argument
Opponents argue that 'haqq' here means obedience, not an attribute, so swearing by it is like swearing by other than Allah.
They also note that 'haqq Allah' is a possessive construction, not a name of Allah.
3
Analyze the Hanafi response
The response: custom (urf) has made this phrase common for oaths, and it can be interpreted as an attribute of Allah. Thus, it is valid.
The chosen view in al-Ikhtiyar adopts this.
4
Distinguish self-condemnation
Expressions like 'upon me the wrath of Allah' or 'I am an adulterer' are not oaths. Why? Because they do not deter; the consequence is not immediate upon the action.
The principle: a valid oath suspends something that deters the speaker, like kufr.
5
Apply the principle
If someone says 'if I do X, I am a kafir', that is an oath because kufr is immediate upon consent. But 'I am an adulterer' requires a future act, so not immediate.
This distinction is crucial in determining validity.

(حق) لا يتبادر منه ما هو صفة الله بل ما هو من حقوقه قوله : (وحقاً أو حقاً قال الرملي : يعني بالواو وبلا واو قوله: (ومضافاً إن كان بالباء فيمين اتفاقاً) ضعفه في الفتح حيث قال : ومن الأقوال الضعيفة ما قال البلخي إن قوله بحق الله يمين لأن الناس يحلفون به وضعفه لما علمت أنه مثل وحق الله بالإضافة وعلمت المغايرة فيه وأنه ليس يميناً فكذا بحق الله قوله : ففيه الاختلاف السابق) أي المذكور أولاً عقب عبارة المتن قوله: (ولأنه غير متعارف) قال في النهر : ظاهر كلامهم أنه لو تعودوا الحلف به كان يميناً وظاهر ما في الفتح أنه لو تعورف الحلف به لا يكون يميناً حيث قال : إن معنى اليمين أن يعلق إلى آخر ما يأتي .

قوله: (وإن فعلته فعلي غضب الله وسخطه أو أنا زان وسارق أو شارب خمر أو أكل ربا) أي لا يكون يميناً. أما في الأول فلأنه دعا على نفسه ولا يتعلق ذلك بالشرط ولأنه غير متعارف، وأما في قوله هو زان إلى آخره فلأن حرمة هذه الأشياء تحتمل النسخ والتبديل فلم تكن في معنى حرمة اسم الله تعالى ولأنه ليس بمتعارف؛ كذا في الهداية. والأولى الاقتصار على أنه ليس بمتعارف لأن كون الحرمة تحتمل الارتفاع أو لا تحتمله لا أثر له مع أنه لا حاجة إلى التعليل بعدم التعارف أيضاً لأن معنى اليمين أن يعلق ما امتناعه يوجب عن الفعل بسبب لزوم وجوده عند الفعل، وليس بمجرد وجود الفعل يصير زانياً أو سارقاً لأنه لا إلا بفعل مستأنف يدخل في الوجود ووجود هذه الفعل ليس لازماً لوجود المحلوف عليه حتى يكون موجباً امتناعه عنه فلا يكون يميناً بخلاف الكفر فإنه بالرضا به يكفر من غير توقف على عمل آخر أو اعتقاد والرضا يتحقق بمباشرة الشرط فيوجب عنده الكفر لولا قول من العلماء بالكفارة كما في فتح القدير. وفي المجتبى لو قال هو يأكل الميتة إن فعل كذا أو يستحل الخمر أو الخنزير فليس بيمين؛ أصله أن التعليق بما تسقط حرمته بحال ما كالميتة والخمر والخنزير لا يكون يميناً وما لا يسقط كألفاظ الكفر فيمين. ولو قال فعله المجوس أو اليهود فعلى عنقي إن فعلت كذا ففعل لا شيء عليه ا هـ. وهو يفيد أن استحلال الخمر والخنزير ليس بكفر إلا أن يقال إن جزاء الشرط هو الاستحلال في المستقبل بخلاف ما لو قال إن فعلت كذا فأنا مستحل للخمر والخنزير. وفي الولوالجية : وأما في
