Book of Oaths. And the Ka'ba, and the right of God, and if I do it then upon me is the wrath of God and His displeasure, or I am an adulterer, or a thief, or a drinker of wine, or an eater of usury. It is customary, although it is intended by it the letters and inscriptions in Fath al-Qadir. Then it is not hidden that swearing by the Qur'an now is customary, so it is an oath as is the saying of the three Imams. The reasoning that it is not an oath because it is other than the Exalted, since it is created, because it is letters and other than the created is the internal speech, is refuted by the fact that the Qur'an is the speech of Allah, revealed, uncreated. And it is not hidden that the revealed in reality is only the letters that have passed and ceased to exist, and that which is proven pre-eternal is impossible to cease. However, they required that because the common people, if told that the Qur'an is created, they transgress to speech absolutely. As for swearing by the speech of Allah the Exalted, it must revolve with custom. As for swearing by Jan Mureed and similar, like swearing by the life of your head and the life of the sultan, then if he believes that acting righteously thereby is obligatory, he disbelieves. In Tatimmat al-Fatawa, Ali al-Razi said: I fear for the one who says 'by my life and your life' that he disbelieves, and were it not that the common people say it not knowing, I would say it is shirk. From Ibn Mas'ud: 'That I swear by Allah falsely is dearer to me than to swear by other than Allah truthfully.' End quote. He restricted by swearing by these things because disassociating from them is an oath, like his saying 'I am disassociated from the Prophet if I do such' as we have detailed before. And the author indicated that if he said 'by the religion of Allah, and His obedience, or His limits, or His law, or the mus-haf', it is not an oath a fortiori, as in al-Khaniyya. His saying: (And the right of Allah, i.e., it is not an oath, and this is the saying of Abu Hanifa, and it is the saying of Muhammad and one of the two narrations from Abu Yusuf; and from him is another narration that it is an oath, because 'right' is among the attributes of Allah the Exalted, and it is literal, so it becomes as if he said 'by Allah, the Truth', and swearing by it is customary. And for them (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), it is intended by it the obedience of Allah, since acts of obedience are His rights, so it is an oath by other than Allah the Exalted. And it is mentioned in al-Ikhtiyar that the chosen opinion is that it is an oath, considering custom. End quote. He restricted by the possessive construction (right of Allah) because if he said 'and al-Haqq' (the Truth), it is an oath, and if he said 'haqqan', it is not an oath, because the indefinite form is intended to affirm the promise, as if he said 'do such truthfully without doubt'. And this is the saying of some, and the correct is that if he intends the name of Allah the Exalted, it is an oath. Thus in al-Khaniyya. In al-Mujtaba: 'and haqqan or haqqan' – the mashayikh differ, and the majority is that it is not an oath. And the summary is that al-haqq is either definite or indefinite in usage. His saying: (And His trust) contradicts what he mentioned earlier from al-Asl, that it is an oath, contrary to al-Tahawi. His saying: (And it is mentioned in al-Ikhtiyar etc.) Al-Nahr said: He refuted it in Fath al-Qadir by saying that customariness after the attribute is shared between the attribute of Allah the Exalted and the attribute of others, and the word 'haqq' does not immediately indicate what is an attribute of Allah, but rather what is from His rights. His saying: (And haqqan or haqqan) al-Ramli said: meaning with waw and without waw. His saying: (And in the possessive construction, if it is with ba, then it is an oath by agreement). He weakened it in al-Fath where he said: And among the weak sayings is what al-Balkhi said that his saying 'bi-haqq illah' is an oath because people swear by it, and he weakened it because it is like 'wa-haqq illah' in the possessive, and you know the difference in it and that it is not an oath, so likewise 'bi-haqq illah'. His saying: (Then there is the previous difference) i.e., mentioned first after the words of the text. His saying: (And because it is not customary) al-Nahr said: The apparent of their words is that if they got accustomed to swearing by it, it would be an oath; and the apparent of what is in al-Fath is that if it became customary to swear by it, it is not an oath, where he said: The meaning of the oath is that he suspends... up to what comes. Book of Oaths. Wine or eater of usury, and its letters are the ba, waw, and ta, and may be implicit, and its expiation is freeing a slave or feeding ten (poor). (These) indefinite or in possessive construction. So al-haqq definite, whether with waw or with ba, is an oath by agreement as in al-Khaniyya and al-Zahira. And indefinite is an oath according to the most correct opinion if he intends, and possessive construction: if it is with ba, then it is an oath by agreement because people swear by it; if with waw, then there is the previous difference, and the chosen is that it is an oath as before. And by this it is known that the chosen is that it is an oath in the three phrases absolutely. And the author indicated that if he said 'by the right of the Messenger' or 'by the right of faith' or 'by the right of mosques' or 'by the right of fasting' or 'prayer', it is not an oath; thus in al-Khaniyya. And in al-Mujtaba, 'the sanctity of Allah' is analogous to his saying 'and the right of Allah'. In Fatawa al-Nasafi: 'By the sanctity of the testimony of Allah' and 'by the sanctity of la ilaha illa Allah' is not an oath. It becomes likewise. His saying: (And if I do it then upon me is the wrath of Allah and His displeasure, or I am an adulterer, thief, wine-drinker, or eater of usury) i.e., it is not an oath. As for the first, because he invoked upon himself and that is not connected to the condition, and because it is not customary. As for his saying 'he is an adulterer' etc., because the sanctity of these things is subject to abrogation and change, so they are not in the meaning of the sanctity of the name of Allah the Exalted, and because it is not customary; thus in al-Hidaya. And the preferred is to restrict to it not being customary, because the sanctity being subject to elevation or not has no effect, especially since there is no need for the rationale of lack of customariness as well, because the meaning of the oath is to suspend something whose prevention causes (deterrence) from the action due to the necessity of its existence upon the action. And it is not that by mere existence of the action he becomes an adulterer or thief, because it only (occurs) by a subsequent action that comes into existence, and the existence of this action is not necessary for the existence of the thing sworn upon, such that it would prevent him from it. So it is not an oath, contrary to disbelief, for by consenting to it he disbelieves without waiting for another action or belief, and consent is realized by performing the condition, so it necessitates disbelief for him, were it not for the saying of some scholars regarding expiation, as in Fath al-Qadir. And in al-Mujtaba: If he said 'he eats carrion if he does such' or 'he considers wine or pork lawful', it is not an oath; its principle is that suspending upon something whose sanctity falls away in some situation, like carrion, wine, pork, is not an oath; and what does not fall away, like words of disbelief, is an oath. And if he said 'the action of the Magians or Jews is upon my neck if I do such', then he does it, there is nothing upon him. End quote. And it indicates that considering wine and pork lawful is not disbelief, unless it is said that the consequence of the condition is future consideration, contrary to if he said 'if I do such, then I am considering wine and pork lawful'. And in al-Walwaljiyya: And regarding... his saying: (Subject to abrogation and change, i.e., subject to dropping. As for wine, it is apparent; as for theft, it is in case of necessity to eat another's property, and likewise if a woman is coerced with a sword to commit adultery; and as for adultery, it is in dar al-harb.) Thus in al-Nahr, and its origin is from al-Fath, and the saying of al-Tibyan: because it is subject to change rationally, so it is not like disbelief in sanctity, indicates the lack of restriction to those situations as is apparent from al-Hidaya. His saying: (Because the meaning of the oath is to suspend something that necessitates...) i.e., to suspend something like disbelief, which necessitates that thing preventing the oath-taker from the action sworn upon, like entering.
Source pages p. 482

Commentary
This passage from Al-Bahr al-Raiq, a commentary on Kanz al-Daqaiq, discusses the ruling of various expressions commonly used in oaths and determines which constitute a valid yamin (oath) in Hanafi fiqh. The passage first addresses swearing by the Qur'an: although the Qur'an is composed of letters and is created in its physical form, it is the uncreated speech of Allah. The Hanafi position is that swearing by the Qur'an is now customary ('urf) and therefore constitutes a valid oath, agreeing with the three Imams (Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad). The earlier objection that the Qur'an is created (and thus not sacred like Allah) is refuted by distinguishing between the physical mushaf and the eternal divine speech. Next, the passage discusses swearing by life (e.g., 'by your life' or 'by the life of the sultan'). If the swearer believes that fulfilling an oath by such expressions is obligatory, he commits kufr (disbelief) because such oaths are akin to swearing by other than Allah. Quoting Ali al-Razi, the passage warns that saying 'by my life and your life' could lead to kufr, and Ibn Mas'ud is cited preferring a false oath by Allah over a true oath by other than Allah. The passage then explains that disassociating (tabarri) from something sacred, like saying 'I am disassociated from the Prophet', constitutes an oath. The author notes that saying 'by the religion of Allah, His obedience, limits, law, or the mushaf' does not constitute an oath, because these are not considered names of Allah. The main discussion centers on the phrase 'bi-haqq Allah' (by the right of Allah). Abu Hanifa, Muhammad, and one narration from Abu Yusuf hold that it is not an oath, because 'haqq' commonly means 'obedience' (a right of Allah) and not the attribute of Allah. Another narration from Abu Yusuf says it is an oath because 'haqq' is an attribute of Allah, so it is like saying 'by Allah, the Truth'. The chosen position (al-mukhtar) in al-Ikhtiyar is that it is an oath due to custom. The passage then details rulings for different forms: 'al-Haqq' (definite) is an oath by agreement, whether with waw or ba; 'haqqan' (indefinite) is an oath only if the swearer intends Allah's name; and 'bi-haqq illah' (with ba) is an oath by agreement because it is customary. The passage concludes that the chosen view makes all three forms oaths. Swearing by other sacred things like 'the right of the Messenger' or 'the right of mosques' is not an oath. Finally, the passage discusses self-condemnation expressions like 'upon me is the wrath of Allah' or 'I am an adulterer/thief/wine-drinker/usurer'. These are not oaths, because invoking wrath is a supplication against oneself, not a suspension; and declaring oneself a sinner does not make one instantly a sinner upon the condition, since becoming an adulterer requires a separate act. In contrast, declaring oneself a disbeliever (kafir) upon an action would be an oath, because mere consent to kufr makes one a disbeliever without further action. Thus, the underlying principle: a valid oath must involve suspending something that deters the speaker from the action, such as kufr, and the thing suspended must be immediate upon the action, not contingent on future acts.

Key Terms
حق الله (haqq Allah): The right of Allah – debated whether it means an attribute or obedience.
مختار (mukhtar): The chosen/preferred opinion in the school.
تعليق (ta'liq): Suspension – the structure of an oath linking a consequence to an action.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following is NOT considered a valid yamin according to the chosen Hanafi position?
A) 'By the right of Allah' (wa-haqq Allah).
B) 'If I do this, I am a kafir.'
C) 'If I do this, I am an adulterer.'
D) 'By the truth (al-Haqq).'

Key Takeaway
The chosen Hanafi view holds 'wa-haqq Allah' as a valid oath due to custom; self-condemnation expressions are not oaths because they lack immediate deterrence.

Oath Validity with 'Bi-Haqq' and 'Bi-Hurma' Phrases
Ruling on oath phrases with 'haqq' and 'hurma'

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify whether a given oath phrase (using 'haqq' or 'hurma') is a valid yamin according to Hanafi fiqh, and apply the rules for definite, indefinite, and genitive constructions.

Core Idea
An oath with 'bi-haqq' is valid except when the object is a prophet, faith, mosque, fasting, or prayer.

Oaths are a serious matter in Islamic law, and their validity depends on the precise phrasing. The Hanafi school has detailed rules for phrases like 'by the right of Allah' versus 'by the right of the Prophet'. This lesson unpacks the conditions under which such phrases constitute a binding oath requiring expiation if broken.

Guided Path
1
Identify the oath letter
Determine whether the phrase uses the letter ba', waw, or ta'. In the passages, focus on ba' and waw as they appear with 'haqq'.
The matn mentions the letters of oath are ba', waw, and ta'.
2
Classify the object of oath
Is the word following 'haqq' definite (mu'arraf, with alif lam), indefinite (nakira), or in genitive construction (mudaf)? This determines the default ruling.
Examples: 'al-haqq' is definite; 'haqqun' is indefinite; 'haqq Allah' is genitive.
3
Apply the general rule
If the object is definite, the phrase is an oath by consensus. If indefinite, it is an oath only if the person intended an oath. If genitive, with ba' it is an oath by consensus; with waw there is disagreement but the chosen view is that it is an oath.
Intention matters only for indefinite objects.
4
Check for the 'haqq al-rasul' exception
If the object is the Prophet (or faith, mosque, fasting, prayer), the phrase is not an oath even if it uses ba'. This is a specific exception mentioned in al-Khaniya.
The phrase 'bi-haqq al-rasul' is not an oath unconditionally.
5
State the final ruling
Conclude whether the phrase is a valid yamin (requiring kaffarah if broken) or not. If valid, also note the default expiation (freeing a slave or feeding ten poor).
The ruling can affect judicial oaths and personal vows.

خمر أو آكل ربا وحروفه الباء والواو والتاء وقد تضمر وكفارته تحرير رقبة أو اطعام عشرة منكراً أو مضافاً، فالحق معرفاً سواء كان بالواو أو بالباء يمين اتفاقاً كما في الخانية والظهيرية، ومنكراً يمين على الأصح إن نوى ومضافاً إن كان بالباء فيمين اتفاقاً، لأن الناس يحلفون به، وإن كان بالواو ففيه الاختلاف السابق والمختار أنه يمين كما سبق. وبهذا علم أن المختار أنه يمين في الألفاظ الثلاثة مطلقاً. وأشار المصنف إلى أنه لو قال بحق الرسول أو بحق الإيمان أو بحق المساجد أو بحق الصوم أو الصلاة لا يكون يميناً؛ كذا في الخانية . وفي المجتبى وحرمة الله نظير قوله وحق الله. وفي فتاوى النسفي : بحرمة شهد الله وبحرمة لا إله إلا الله ليس بيمين.
Wine or eating usury, and its letters are ba', waw, and ta', and it may be implied, and its expiation is freeing a slave or feeding ten [poor]. Indefinite or genitive; the definite, whether with waw or ba', is an oath by agreement, as in al-Khaniya and al-Dhahiyra. Indefinite is an oath according to the soundest view if he intends, and genitive if with ba' is an oath by agreement, because people swear by it. If with waw, there is the previous disagreement, and the chosen view is that it is an oath, as previously. By this it is known that the chosen view is that it is an oath in all three expressions absolutely. The author indicated that if he says 'by the right of the Messenger' or 'by the right of faith' or 'by the right of mosques' or 'by the right of fasting' or 'by the right of prayer', it is not an oath; thus in al-Khaniya. In al-Mujtaba: 'by the sanctity of Allah' is similar to his saying 'by the right of Allah'. In Fatawa al-Nasafi: 'by the sanctity of the testimony of Allah' and 'by the sanctity of la ilaha illa Allah' is not an oath.
Source pages p. 483

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq discusses the validity of oaths (yamin) depending on how they are phrased. The matn states that the letters of oath are ba', waw, and ta', and the expiation is mentioned. Then the commentator explains that when the object of oath (المحلوف به) is definite (معرفة) like 'Allah', whether using waw or ba', it is an oath by consensus. When indefinite (نكرة), it is an oath on the soundest view if the person intends an oath. When it is in genitive construction (مضاف) like 'by the right of the Messenger', if using ba' it is an oath by consensus because people commonly swear that way. If using waw, there is disagreement but the chosen view (المختار) is that it is an oath. The author also notes that saying 'by the right of the Messenger', 'by the right of faith', etc., is not an oath according to al-Khaniya, though 'by the sanctity of Allah' is like 'by the right of Allah' per al-Mujtaba. Finally, al-Nasafi's fatawa state that 'by the sanctity of the testimony of Allah' and 'by the sanctity of la ilaha illa Allah' are not oaths.

Key Terms
يمين (yamin): An oath that triggers expiation (kaffarah) when violated, typically using the letters ba', waw, or ta' with the name of Allah.
منكر (munkar): Indefinite (grammatically, without alif lam), e.g., 'بإله'?
معرف (mu'arraf): Definite (with alif lam or proper noun).
مضاف (mudaf): Genitive construction, e.g., 'حق الله' where 'حق' is in idafah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which of the following is NOT a valid oath?
A) بحق الله (with ba')
B) وحق الله (with waw)
C) بحق الصوم
D) بحق إله (with intention)

Key Takeaway
An oath with 'haqq' or 'hurma' is valid only when the object is Allah directly; all other objects, including prophets and acts of worship, do not form a valid yamin.

Why Phrases Like 'غضب الله' and 'أنا زان' Are Not Oaths
Explanation of why certain phrases are not oaths with supporting proof and ancillary cases.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi definition of a valid oath (yamin) and apply it to determine whether a given conditional statement constitutes an oath.

Core Idea
A valid oath requires immediate necessity; claiming a sin fails because sin requires a separate act.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq clarifies a common confusion: people may think that saying 'If I do X, may Allah be angry with me' or 'If I do X, I am an adulterer' constitutes a binding oath. The Hanafi school explains why such utterances are not legally recognized as yamin, grounding the distinction in the nature of immediate consequence. Understanding this principle clarifies the boundary between valid oaths and mere emotional expressions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two categories of utterances
The text first addresses invoking Allah's anger, then claiming to be a sinner (adulterer, thief, etc.). Identify these two categories and note how each is treated.
The first is a du'a, the second a label that requires a separate act.
2
Analyze the reasoning for the first category
Why is 'upon me the anger of Allah' not an oath? Because it is a supplication (du'a), not a condition-consequence attachment, and it is not customary in oath-taking.
Custom plays a significant role in defining oaths.
3
Analyze the reasoning for the second category
Why is 'I am an adulterer' not an oath? Two reasons are given: (1) the prohibition of sin is abrogable, (2) more importantly, becoming an adulterer requires a separate, subsequent act—it is not immediate upon the conditioned act.
The primary reason is lack of immediacy.
4
Extract the core principle
The text defines an oath: hanging a consequence that is necessary and immediate upon the act. The standard example is kufr: consenting to disbelief makes one a disbeliever instantly, without needing another act.
This is the benchmark for validity.
5
Apply the principle to ancillary cases
The text extends the analysis to cases like carrion, wine, pork, and even considering them lawful. Since their prohibition can fall away in necessity, they are not suitable for valid oaths.
The principle is consistent across rulings.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله: (وإن فعلته فعلي غضب الله وسخطه أو أنا زان وسارق أو شارب خمر أو أكل ربا) أي لا يكون يميناً. أما في الأول فلأنه دعا على نفسه ولا يتعلق ذلك بالشرط ولأنه غير متعارف، وأما في قوله هو زان إلى آخره فلأن حرمة هذه الأشياء تحتمل النسخ والتبديل فلم تكن في معنى حرمة اسم الله تعالى ولأنه ليس بمتعارف ؛ كذا في الهداية. والأولى الاقتصار على أنه ليس بمتعارف لأن كون الحرمة تحتمل الارتفاع أو لا تحتمله لا أثر له مع أنه لا حاجة إلى التعليل بعدم التعارف أيضاً لأن معنى اليمين أن يعلق ما امتناعه يوجب عن الفعل بسبب لزوم وجوده عند الفعل، وليس بمجرد وجود الفعل يصير زانياً أو سارقاً لأنه لا إلا بفعل مستأنف يدخل في الوجود ووجود هذه الفعل ليس لازماً لوجود المحلوف عليه حتى يكون موجباً امتناعه عنه فلا يكون يميناً بخلاف الكفر فإنه بالرضا به يكفر من غير توقف على عمل آخر أو اعتقاد والرضا يتحقق بمباشرة الشرط فيوجب عنده الكفر لولا قول من العلماء بالكفارة كما في فتح القدير. وفي المجتبى لو قال هو يأكل الميتة إن فعل كذا أو يستحل الخمر أو الخنزير فليس بيمين؛ أصله أن التعليق بما تسقط حرمته بحال ما كالميتة والخمر والخنزير لا يكون يميناً وما لا يسقط كألفاظ الكفر فيمين. ولو قال فعله المجوس أو اليهود فعلى عنقي إن فعلت كذا ففعل لا شيء عليه ا هـ. وهو يفيد أن استحلال الخمر والخنزير ليس بكفر إلا أن يقال إن جزاء الشرط هو الاستحلال في المستقبل بخلاف ما لو قال إن فعلت كذا فأنا مستحل للخمر والخنزير. وفي الولوالجية : وأما في استحلال الدم فلا يكون كفراً لا محالة فإن حالة الضرورة يصير حلالاً. وكذلك لحم الخنزير ا هـ . فأفاد أن ما يباح للضرورة ولا يكفر مستحله. وفي الظهيرية: لو قال عصيت الله تعالى أن فعلت كذا أو قال عصيت الله في كل ما افترض علي لا يكون يميناً .
His saying: (And if I do it, then upon me is the anger of Allah and His wrath, or I am an adulterer and a thief or a wine drinker or an eater of usury) meaning it is not an oath. As for the first, because he is invoking a curse upon himself and that is not attached to the condition, and because it is not customary. As for his saying 'he is an adulterer' etc., because the prohibition of these things is subject to abrogation and substitution, so they are not in the meaning of the prohibition of the name of Allah, and because it is not customary; thus in al-Hidaya. The better view is to restrict it to its not being customary, because whether the prohibition can be lifted or not has no effect, and moreover there is no need for the reasoning of not being customary either. The meaning of an oath is that one attaches something whose prevention [from the conditioned act] causes [the swearer to refrain] due to the necessity of its existence upon the act. And merely by the existence of the act does one become an adulterer or thief, because that only happens through a subsequent act coming into existence, and the existence of this act is not necessary for the existence of the thing sworn upon, so that it would cause him to refrain. Therefore it is not an oath, unlike disbelief (kufr), because by consenting to it one disbelieves without needing another act or belief, and consent is realized by directly fulfilling the condition, so it causes disbelief at that moment, were it not for the saying of some scholars about expiation, as in Fath al-Qadir. In al-Mujtaba: If he says 'he eats carrion if he does such and such' or 'he considers wine or pork lawful', it is not an oath. The principle is that hanging [an oath] on something whose prohibition falls away in some circumstances, like carrion, wine, and pork, is not an oath, and what does not fall away, like words of disbelief, is an oath. And if he says 'the act of the Magians or Jews is upon my neck if I do such and such', and he does it, nothing is upon him. This shows that considering wine and pork lawful is not disbelief, unless it is said that the result of the condition is future consideration, unlike if he says 'if I do such and such, I consider wine and pork lawful'. In al-Walwaljiya: As for considering blood lawful, it is definitely not disbelief, because in a state of necessity it becomes permissible, and likewise pork. So it is understood that what is permissible due to necessity does not cause its considerer to become a disbeliever. In al-Dhahiyra: If he says 'I disobeyed Allah if I do such and such' or 'I disobeyed Allah in all that He made obligatory upon me', it is not an oath.
Source pages p. 483

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq explains why certain phrases do not constitute valid oaths (yamin). The commentator discusses two categories: (1) invoking something like the anger of Allah upon oneself, which is a supplication (du'a) and not a conventional oath; (2) claiming to be a sinner (adulterer, thief, etc.) because the prohibition of these acts can be abrogated or lifted in certain circumstances (e.g., necessity), unlike the name of Allah which is eternal. The better explanation, however, is simply that such phrasing is not customary among the people as oaths. The core principle is that a true oath must involve attaching a necessary consequence (like disbelief) to the conditioned act, such that the mere existence of the act triggers that consequence immediately. For example, stating 'if I enter the house, I will be a disbeliever' is an oath because disbelief occurs instantly with the act. But claiming to be a sinner does not happen instantly; it requires a separate, subsequent act. Thus, it is not an oath. The passage then discusses cases where the thing sworn by (e.g., carrion, wine) can become permissible in necessity, so swearing by considering them lawful is not an oath. The same applies to saying 'I disobeyed Allah' etc.

Key Terms
يمين (yamin): A legally recognized oath that, if violated, requires expiation; defined by attaching a necessary consequence to the conditioned act.
تعليق (ta'liq): The act of hanging a consequence upon a condition, central to the formation of an oath.
كفر (kufr): Disbelief; in this context, it is the only thing that, when attached as a condition, constitutes a valid oath because it is immediate and irreversible under normal circumstances.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why does the Hanafi school consider the statement 'إن فعلت كذا فأنا زان' (If I do such and such, I am an adulterer) not to be a valid oath?
A) Because adultery is not a sin.
B) Because the prohibition of adultery can be abrogated.
C) Because becoming an adulterer does not happen instantly upon the act; it requires a separate subsequent act.
D) Because such phrasing is not mentioned in the Quran.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi law, a valid oath must attach an immediate necessary consequence to the condition; self-cursing or sin-claiming phrases lack this immediacy and thus are not oaths.

The Letters of Oath and the Criterion for a Valid Yamin
Linguistic and legal analysis of oath letters and validity criterion

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the three letters of oath (ba', waw, ta') in Arabic, explain their hierarchy, and apply the Hanafi criterion that a valid oath requires an eternal prohibition (hurma mu'abbada).

Core Idea
Only ba', waw, and ta' are valid oath letters; a valid oath must be attached to something eternally forbidden.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq provides a detailed linguistic and legal analysis of the particles used to form oaths in Arabic. It sets out the Hanafi position that only three letters—ba', waw, and ta'—are valid, and it explains the underlying principle: a true oath (yamin) is one where the consequence is an eternal prohibition that never becomes permissible. Understanding this criterion is essential for distinguishing valid oaths from mere conditional statements.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three oath letters
List ba', waw, and ta' as the only valid particles for initiating oaths in Hanafi law. Note their occurrence in Quranic verses: 'fawarabbi' (waw), 'billah' (ba'), 'tallah' (ta').
These three are considered the 'harf al-qasam'.
2
Analyze the hierarchy of the letters
Ba' is the original letter; waw is a substitute for ba' and is one degree lower, used only with manifest nouns (not pronouns); ta' is a substitute for waw. The verb of swearing cannot be pronounced with waw.
This hierarchy affects the syntax of oath formulas.
3
Understand the criterion for a valid oath
A valid oath requires that the attached consequence (muqassam bihi) be something with eternal prohibition (hurma mu'abbada), like kufr. Acts that can become permissible in necessity (e.g., eating carrion) do not form valid oaths when considered lawful.
This is a distinctive Hanafi rule.
4
Apply the criterion to examples
Distinguish between valid conditional statements (e.g., 'If I enter, I am a disbeliever') and invalid ones (e.g., 'If I do X, I will eat carrion'). The former is a valid oath; the latter is not due to the possibility of permissibility.
The key is whether the prohibition is absolute or conditional.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (وحروفه الباء والواو والتاء) أي وحروف القسم ولو عاد الضمير على اليمين لأنثه لأنها مؤنثة سماعاً كقوله والله وبالله وتالله لأن كل ذلك معهود في الأيمان ومذكور في القرآن قال تعالى فورب السماء والأرض أنه لحق وقال تعالى تالله لقد أرسلنا وقال تعالى بالله إن الشرك لظلم عظيم وفيه احتمال كونه متعلقاً بقوله تعالى ﴿لا تشرك وقدم الباء قالوا: هي الأصل لأنها صلة الحلف والأصل أحلف أو أقسم بالله ، وهي تلصق فعل القسم بالمحلوف به ثم حذف الفعل لكثرة الاستعمال مع فهم المقصود. ولأصالتها دخلت في المظهر والمضمر نحو بك لأفعلن ثم ثني بالواو ولأنها بدل منها للمناسبة المعنوية، وهي ما في الالصاق من الجمع الذي هو معنى الواو ولكونها بدلاً انحطت عنها بدرجة فدخلت على المظهر لا على المضمر ولا يجوز إظهار الفعل معها لا تقول أحلف بالله كما تقول أحلف والله وأما التاء فبدل عن الواو لأنها من حروف الزيادة وقد أبدلت كثيراً بسبب مثالاً. وقوله بسبب متعلق بيوجب أي أن ذلك الشيء المعلق يوجب امتناع الحالف عن الفعل أن ذلك المعلق يلزم وجوده عند الفعل فإذا قال إن دخلت فهو كافر فإن الكفر يوجب امتناع الحالف عن الدخول بسبب لزوم وجود الكفر عند الدخول قوله : (فأفاد أن ما يباح للضرورة لا يكفر مستحله) قال بعض الفضلاء إن أراد بقوله لا يكفر مستحله أنه لا يكفر من اعتقد أنه حلال في حالة الضرورة فقط فهو صحيح لكنه لا جدوى له لعدم الشك في حله حينئذ، وإن أراد أنه لا يكفر مستحله مطلقاً سواء اعتقد أنه حلال في حالة الاضطرار والاختيار فهو وهم باطل أوقعه فيه توهمه أن قول الولوالجية لا محالة قيد في النفي وهو لا يكون وليس كذلك بل قيد في المنفي وهو يكون . قال في المحيط : ولو قال هو يأكل الميتة إن فعل كذا لا يكون يميناً وكان يجب أن يكون يميناً لأن استحلال الجرام كفر فقد علق الكفر بالشرط وتعليق الكفر بالشرط يمين كما لو قال دخل الدار قلنا: استحلال هذه الأشياء ليس بكفر لا محالة فإن في حالة الضرورة تصير هذه الأشياء حلالاً ولا يكون كفراً، وإذا احتمل أن يكون استحلال هذه كفراً كما في غاية حالة الضرورة فيكون يميناً واحتمل أن لا يكون كفراً كما في حالة الضرورة فلا يكون يميناً لا يصير يميناً بالشك بخلاف قوله هو يهودي إن فعل كذا لأن اليهودي من أنكر رسالة محمد صلى الله تعالى عليه وسلم وإنكار رسالة محمد صلى الله تعالى عليه وسلم كفر على كل حال. فالحاصل أن كل شيء هو حرام حرمة مؤبدة بحيث لا تسقط بحال من الأحوال كالكفر وأشباهه فاستحلاله معلقاً بالشرط يكون يميناً، وكل شيء هو حرام بحيث : تسقط حرمته بحال كالميتة والخمر وأشباهه فاستحلاله معلقاً بالشرط لا يكون يميناً.
His saying: (And its letters are ba', waw, and ta') i.e., the letters of oath. If the pronoun refers to 'yamin', it is feminine because it is considered feminine by usage, like 'wallah', 'billah', 'tallah'; all of these are customary in oaths and mentioned in the Quran. He said, exalted: 'But by the Lord of the heaven and earth, indeed it is truth' (51:23) and 'By Allah, we have sent' (15:36?) and 'By Allah, indeed association is great injustice' (31:13). There is also the possibility that it is connected to His saying 'Do not associate...' (31:13). They said: Ba' is the original because it is the particle of swearing; the original is 'I swear by Allah' (ahliftu billah or aqsimu billah). It attaches the verb of swearing to the thing sworn by. Then the verb is omitted due to frequent usage and understanding of the intended meaning. Due to its originality, it enters both the manifest and the pronoun, e.g., 'bika la af'alann'. Then the waw was used as a substitute for it due to the semantic connection, which is in the attachment of combination, which is the meaning of waw. And because it is a substitute, it is one degree lower, so it enters the manifest but not the pronoun, and it is not permissible to pronounce the verb with it; you cannot say 'ahliftu billah' as you say 'ahliftu wallah'. As for ta', it is a substitute for waw because it is a letter of increase and has been substituted often for example. And his saying 'due to' is connected to 'obligates' meaning that the thing attached obligates the refraining of the swearer from the act, because that attached thing necessarily comes into existence when the act is done. So if he says 'if I enter, then I am a disbeliever', disbelief obligates the swearer to refrain from entering due to the necessity of the occurrence of disbelief upon entering. His saying: (So it is understood that what is permissible due to necessity does not cause its considerer to become a disbeliever). Some scholars said: If by his saying 'does not cause its considerer to become a disbeliever' he means that he does not become a disbeliever if he believes it is permissible only in the state of necessity, then this is correct but of no benefit since there is no doubt about its permissibility then. But if he means that he does not become a disbeliever absolutely, whether he believes it is permissible in necessity or in choice, then this is a false delusion that led him to think that the saying of al-Walwaljiya 'definitely' is a restriction on the negation, but it is not like that; rather, it is a restriction on the negated thing, i.e., the state. He said in al-Muhit: If he says 'he eats carrion if he does such and such', it is not an oath, and it would be necessary that it be an oath because considering major sins permissible is disbelief, so he has attached disbelief to a condition, and attaching disbelief to a condition is an oath, as if he said 'enter the house'. We say: considering these things permissible is definitely not disbelief, because in a state of necessity these things become halal and not disbelief. So if it is possible that considering these things is disbelief, as [in the case] beyond necessity, then it would be an oath; and if it is possible that it is not disbelief, as in the state of necessity, then it is not an oath, and it does not become an oath through doubt, unlike his saying 'he is a Jew if he does such and such', because a Jew is one who denies the message of Muhammad, may Allah bless him and grant him peace, and denial of the message of Muhammad is disbelief in all cases. The conclusion is that everything that is forbidden with an eternal prohibition that never falls away in any circumstance, like disbelief and its like, its consideration [as lawful] when attached to a condition is an oath; and everything that is forbidden in a way that its prohibition falls away in some circumstances, like carrion, wine, and their like, its consideration when attached to a condition is not an oath.
Source pages p. 484

Commentary
This final passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq provides a detailed analysis of the letters of oath (ba', waw, ta') and the fundamental meaning of a valid yamin. The commentator explains that ba' is the original letter of swearing, functioning to attach the verb of swearing to the object. The waw is a substitute for ba', used only with manifest nouns, not pronouns, and the verb cannot be pronounced with it. Ta' is a substitute for waw. The passage also revisits the principle that a valid oath requires a necessary, immediate consequence. It distinguishes between acts that are eternally forbidden (like kufr) - where considering them lawful when attached to a condition makes a valid oath - and acts that can become permissible in necessity (like eating carrion), where considering them lawful does not constitute a valid oath due to the possibility of permissibility. The text concludes by summarizing this rule.

Key Terms
حرف القسم (harf al-qasam): A particle used to initiate an oath, specifically ba', waw, and ta' in Arabic.
تعليق بالشرط (ta'liq bi al-shart): Attaching a consequence to a condition; in oaths, the consequence must be unavoidable and immediate.
حرمة مؤبدة (hurma mu'abbada): An eternal prohibition that never falls away under any circumstances, such as disbelief or major sins that are absolutely forbidden.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which of the following statements would be considered a valid oath (yamin) according to Hanafi jurisprudence?
A) 'If I go to the store, I will eat chocolate.'
B) 'If I miss prayer, I will become a Jew.'
C) 'If I lie, I will eat carrion.'
D) 'If I insult my father, I will divorce my wife.'

Key Takeaway
The validity of an oath hinges on its attachment to an eternally forbidden consequence; only ba', waw, and ta' are the valid letters of swearing in the Hanafi school.

When Conditional Istihlal Becomes an Oath
Explains when conditional istihlal constitutes an oath

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish conditional istihlal statements that constitute an oath from those that do not, using the Hanafi criterion of permanent vs. temporary prohibition.

Core Idea
Istihlal of an eternally forbidden act attached to a condition is an oath; of a provisionally forbidden act is not.

In Hanafi law, a conditional statement that implies considering an act permissible (istihlal) can sometimes be an oath if it attaches disbelief (kufr) to the condition. However, not every istihlal of a forbidden act amounts to disbelief. This lesson unpacks the key distinction: whether the prohibition is absolute and eternal, like kufr itself, or can be lifted in cases of necessity, like carrion. Understanding this difference is essential for correctly identifying when a conditional statement triggers the legal consequences of an oath.

Guided Path
1
Identify the statement type
Recognize a conditional istihlal: e.g., 'If I do X, I make Y permissible.' The statement implies that doing X makes Y halal for the speaker.
The statement must be in the form of a condition (shart) and a result (jazā).
2
Determine the nature of Y's prohibition
Ask: Is the prohibition of Y permanent (eternal) or can it be lifted in some circumstances, like necessity?
Permanent: e.g., kufr, shirk, denial of prophethood. Temporary: e.g., carrion, wine, pork (permissible in dire necessity).
3
Apply the Hanafi rule
If the prohibition is permanent, the statement is an oath (yamin) because it attaches disbelief to the condition. If temporary, it is not an oath because the istihlal is not necessarily disbelief.
The text states: 'Everything that is prohibited with an eternal prohibition... its istihlal when attached to a condition is an oath.'
4
Verify with examples from the text
The text contrasts 'He eats carrion if he does such' (not an oath) with 'He is a Jew if he does such' (an oath). Carrion's prohibition is liftable; being a Jew implies permanent disbelief.
Another example: 'I have disobeyed Allah if I do such' is not an oath because disobedience can be forgiven or mitigated.
5
Avoid the common mistake
Do not assume all istihlal of forbidden things is kufr. The permissibility of necessity (ḍarūra) can remove the sin, thus the statement does not indicate disbelief.
The text says: 'it does not become an oath by doubt.'

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الاستحلال فلأن استحلال الدم لا يكون كفراً لا محالة فإن حالة الضرورة يصير . وكذلك لحم الخنزير ا هـ . فأفاد أن ما يباح للضرورة ولا يكفر مستحله. وفي الظهيرية: لو قال عصيت الله تعالى أن فعلت كذا أو قال عصيت الله في كل ما افترض علي لا يكون يميناً . قال في المحيط : ولو قال هو يأكل الميتة إن فعل كذا لا يكون يميناً وكان يجب أن يكون يميناً لأن استحلال الجرام كفر فقد علق الكفر بالشرط وتعليق الكفر بالشرط يمين كما لو قال دخل الدار قلنا: استحلال هذه الأشياء ليس بكفر لا محالة فإن في حالة الضرورة تصير هذه الأشياء حلالاً ولا يكون كفراً، وإذا احتمل أن يكون استحلال هذه كفراً كما في غاية حالة الضرورة فيكون يميناً واحتمل أن لا يكون كفراً كما في حالة الضرورة فلا يكون يميناً لا يصير يميناً بالشك بخلاف قوله هو يهودي إن فعل كذا لأن اليهودي من أنكر رسالة محمد صلى الله تعالى عليه وسلم وإنكار رسالة محمد صلى الله تعالى عليه وسلم كفر على كل حال. فالحاصل أن كل شيء هو حرام حرمة مؤبدة بحيث لا تسقط بحال من الأحوال كالكفر وأشباهه فاستحلاله معلقاً بالشرط يكون يميناً، وكل شيء هو حرام بحيث : تسقط حرمته بحال كالميتة والخمر وأشباهه فاستحلاله معلقاً بالشرط لا يكون يميناً
Istihlal: because making blood permissible is not necessarily disbelief; in a state of necessity it becomes permissible. Likewise the meat of swine. So it indicates that what is permissible in necessity, its istihlal is not disbelief. And in al-Dhahiriya: If one says 'I have disobeyed Allah if I do such' or 'I have disobeyed Allah in all that He made obligatory on me', it is not an oath. In al-Muhit: If one says 'He eats carrion if he does such', it is not an oath, but it should be an oath because istihlal of carrion is disbelief, so he has attached disbelief to a condition and attaching disbelief to a condition is an oath, like saying 'he enters the house'. We say: Istihlal of these things is not necessarily disbelief, for in a state of necessity these things become permissible and are not disbelief. And since it is possible that istihlal of these is disbelief (as in the extreme case of necessity) so it would be an oath, and possible that it is not disbelief (as in necessity), so it is not an oath; it does not become an oath by doubt, unlike the statement 'He is a Jew if he does such', because the Jew is one who denies the message of Muhammad, may Allah bless him and grant him peace, and denial of his message is disbelief in every case. The conclusion: Everything that is prohibited with an eternal prohibition such that it never ceases in any circumstances, like disbelief and its likes, its istihlal when attached to a condition is an oath. And everything that is prohibited such that its prohibition is removed in some circumstances, like carrion, wine and their likes, its istihlal when attached to a condition is not an oath.
Source pages p. 484

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq is a discussion on the ruling of conditional statements involving istihlal (considering something permissible). The author explains that not every istihlal of a prohibited thing constitutes disbelief; in a state of necessity, things like carrion become permissible, so claiming they are permissible is not disbelief. The key distinction is whether the prohibition is absolute (like kufr) or can be lifted (like carrion in necessity). If the prohibition is permanent, then saying 'if I do X, I make it permissible' is an oath because it attaches disbelief to the condition. If the prohibition can be lifted, it is not an oath. The text also clarifies that a statement like 'I have disobeyed Allah' without specifying an act is not an oath. The ruling is based on legal reasoning (talil) distinguishing between eternal and temporary prohibitions.

Key Terms
استحلال (istihlal): Considering something permissible that is normally prohibited, often a cause of disbelief if the thing is definitely haram.
يمين (yamin): An oath that triggers legal consequences, such as expiation or nullification.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to al-Bahr al-Ra'iq, which of the following conditional statements would constitute an oath?
A) 'If I eat carrion, I make it permissible.'
B) 'If I drink wine, I make it permissible.'
C) 'If I deny the Prophet, I make it permissible.'
D) 'If I eat pork in necessity, I make it permissible.'

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school distinguishes between permanent and temporary prohibitions: conditional istihlal of an eternally forbidden act is an oath; of a provisionally forbidden act is not.

Letters of Oath: Ba, Waw, and Ta
Explains the letters of oath, their usage, and when they are implicit

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three primary letters of oath in Hanafi fiqh and identify which nouns each letter can enter on (explicit or implicit).

Core Idea
Ba is the original letter of oath; waw and ta are substitutes with decreasing scope.

This lesson from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq explains the grammatical and legal rules governing the letters used in oaths. Understanding which letters are valid and how they are used is essential for correctly forming and interpreting oaths in Hanafi fiqh.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three main letters
List the letters ba (ب), waw (و), and ta (ت) as the primary letters of oath. Note that ba is the original, waw is one degree lower, and ta is two degrees lower.
These are the only letters mentioned by the author; others are listed in al-Tabyin but not relied upon.
2
Determine the noun type for each letter
For ba: enters on both explicit (مظهر) and implicit (مضمر) nouns. For waw: enters only on explicit nouns. For ta: enters only on the name of Allah (explicit).
The verb showing the oath (e.g., 'ahlifu') cannot be used with waw or ta, but can be used with ba (though often dropped).
3
Understand the effect of omitting the letter
When the letter of oath is omitted (إضمار), the noun may be in the genitive (jar) if the trace remains, or in the accusative/nominative if not. Jar is only allowed for the name of Allah.
Idmar (implication) leaves a grammatical trace, unlike hadhf (deletion).

Source Text

His statement: 'And its letters are ba, waw, and ta' i.e., the letters of oath. If the pronoun refers to yamin, it would be feminine because it is feminine audibly, like his statement 'Wallahi, Billahi, Tawallahi' because all that is customary in oaths and mentioned in the Quran. He said, exalted: 'So by the Lord of the heaven and earth, it is truth.' And He said, exalted: 'By Allah, we sent out.' And He said, exalted: 'By Allah, indeed association is a great injustice.' And in it is a possibility that it is related to His statement 'Do not associate'. And they introduced the ba: they said it is the original because it is the means of swearing, and the original is 'I swear by Allah' or 'I vow by Allah', and it attaches the act of swearing to the one sworn by. Then the verb was deleted due to abundant usage with understanding of the intended meaning. Due to its originality, it enters on both explicit and implicit nouns, like 'bika la af'alanna'. Then the waw is second, because it is a substitute for it due to the meaningful correspondence, which is in the attachment of the conjunction that is the meaning of waw. And because it is a substitute, it is one degree lower, so it enters on explicit nouns, not implicit ones, and it is not permissible to show the verb with it; you do not say 'ahlifu billahi' as you say 'ahlifu wallahi'. As for ta, it is a substitute for waw because it is from the letters of augmentation and has been substituted often, like in tijah, tikhma, turath. So it is two degrees lower, so it does not enter on explicit nouns except the name of Allah alone. What is narrated of their saying 'tarbi' and 'tarb al-Ka'ba' is not analogous, nor 'tahiyyatika'. And it is not permissible to show the verb with it; you do not say 'ahlifu tallahi'. The author, like others, did not mention more than three. And perhaps the ta comes without wonder without the lam. End. His statement: 'And it may be implied' i.e., the letters of oath, so he is swearing like his saying 'Allah la af'alu kaza' because deleting the letter is customary among them for brevity. Then when the letter is deleted and not compensated by 'ha' of warning, nor the interrogative hamza, nor cutting the alif wasl, it is not permissible to lower except in the name of Allah. Rather, it is set in the accusative by implying a verb, or raised as a predicate of an implied subject, except in two names where raising is adhered to: 'yamin Allah' and 'la'amr Allah'. This is in al-Tabyin. The author said 'implied' and did not say 'deleted' to distinguish between them, because implication leaves a trace unlike deletion. And according to this, in the case of nasb, the letter is deleted because its trace does not appear, and in the case of jar, it is implied because its trace appears, which is the jar on the noun. In al-Dhahiriya: 'Billahi la af'alu kaza' and he makes the ha silent, or nasb, or rafa, it is an oath. If he says 'Allahu la af'alu kaza' and makes the ha silent or nasb, it is not an oath unless he inflects it with jar, then it is an oath. And it is said it is an oath absolutely. If he says 'bilihi' with kasra on the lam, 'la af'alu kaza', they said it is not an oath unless he inflects the ha with kasra and intends the oath. End. And it should be that if he uses nasb, it is an oath without disagreement because the linguists did not differ on the permissibility of each of the two ways, but nasb is more abundant as mentioned by Abd al-Qahir in his Muqtasid. This is in Ghayat al-Bayan, and by it is refuted what is in al-Mabsut that nasb is the madhhab of the Basrans and khafd is the madhhab of the Kufans, unless he intended that the disagreement is about preferability, not about permissibility. His statement: 'And it is the lam and noon'. Al-Ramli said: i.e.

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq elaborates on the letters used for oaths (حروف القسم) in Hanafi fiqh. The author explains that the original letter is the ba, which is used for both explicit (مظهر) and implicit (مضمر) nouns. The waw is a substitute, but only enters on explicit nouns, and the verb cannot be shown with it. The ta is a substitute for waw and is used only with the name of Allah. The discussion includes the ruling when the letter is omitted: if the omission is understood, the noun may be in the accusative or nominative, but jar (genitive) is only allowed for Allah's name. The text also addresses common phrases like 'بله' and different vowel endings, clarifying when they constitute a valid oath. The author cites sources like al-Tabyin, al-Dhahiriya, and Ghayat al-Bayan to support the Hanafi position.

Key Terms
حروف القسم (huruf al-qasm): The letters used to form an oath: ba, waw, and ta, as well as other particles mentioned.
إضمار (idmar): The implied presence of a letter of oath, leaving a grammatical trace (e.g., jar on the noun).
مظهر (muzhir): An explicit noun that is pronounced with the letter of oath.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
The primary letters of oath are ba (original, explicit and implicit), waw (explicit only), and ta (only for Allah's name). When omitted, the noun's inflection shows if the letter is implied or deleted.

Conditions for a Valid Affirmative Oath: Lam, Nun, and Customary Usage
Explaining form of affirmative oaths and the customary exception

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the essential form of a valid affirmative oath in Hanafi fiqh and apply the ruling to cases where emphatic particles are omitted, considering the role of custom.

Core Idea
A valid affirmative oath requires lam and nun; without them, it is construed as negation, but custom may change the ruling.

Swearing by Allah is a serious matter in Islamic law. But what exactly makes a statement an 'oath' that triggers legal consequences? The Hanafi school has detailed rules about the linguistic form of oaths. This passage from Bahr al-Ra'iq explains that for an affirmative oath (e.g., 'By Allah, I will do X'), the emphatic particles lam and nun must be explicitly stated. If they are omitted, the statement is interpreted as a negation—meaning no oath is formed, and no expiation is required if the person fails to act. However, a later debate among Hanafi scholars considers whether the custom of common people, who regularly omit these particles, should be taken into account, effectively validating their oaths.

Guided Path
1
Identify the form of a valid affirmative oath
Read the passage to find the exact Arabic phrasing required for a valid affirmative oath. The text states: 'في الإثبات أن تقول: والله لا أفعلن كذا ووالله لقد فعلت كذا مقروناً بكلمة التوكيد'. This shows that emphatic particles (lam and nun) are mandatory.
Also note the evidence from Quran 21:57: 'تالله لأكيدن أصنامكم'.
2
Determine the ruling when lam and nun are omitted
The author explains that if someone says 'والله أفعل كذا اليوم' without the emphatic, it is interpreted as a negation (meaning 'I will not do it'), so breaking it incurs no expiation. Identify the linguistic reasoning: the sentence is treated as containing an implied 'لا'.
3
Analyze the intra-Hanafi dispute about common people
Trace the argument between al-Maqdisi (who holds that without lam and nun, no oath is formed) and al-Ramli (who argues that custom should validate such oaths because common people habitually omit the particles). Note the authority cited: al-Zahiriyyah and al-Walwalijiyyah.
Al-Ramli's view is supported by the practice of the common people and by the principle that ungrammatical speech does not nullify the oath.
4
Apply the relied-upon position
The text indicates that the mufta bihi position is that oaths lacking lam and nun are valid if customary usage so indicates. This is based on the change in language since early Islam. In modern practice, most affirmative oaths are understood by custom even without the emphatic particles.
This is an example of istihsan (juristic preference) overriding strict analogy.
5
Distinguish between affirmative and negative oaths
Note that the discussion applies only to affirmative oaths. For negative oaths (e.g., 'والله لا أفعل'), the particles are not required; the presence of 'لا' suffices.
This distinction is crucial: different rules apply depending on whether the oath is positive or negative.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الأيمان
مساكين كهما في الظهار أو كسوتهم بما يستر عامة البدن وإن عجز عن أحدها صام فيه. قيد بإضمار الحروف لأنه لا يضمر في المقسم عليه حرف التأكيد وهو اللام والنون بل بد من ذكرهما لما في المحيط والحلف بالعربية أن تقول في الإثبات والله لا أفعلن كذا ووالله لقد فعلت كذا مقروناً بكلمة التوكيد وفي النفي تقول والله لا أفعل كذا ووالله ما فعلت كذا حتى لو قال والله أفعل كذا اليوم فلم يفعل لا تلزمه الكفارة ويكون بمعنى قوله لا أفعل كذا فتكون كلمة (لا) مضمرة فيه لأن الحلف في الإثبات عند العرب لا يكون إلا بحرف التأكيد وهو اللام والنون كقوله والله لا أفعلن كذا قال الله تعالى تالله لأكيدن أصنامكم [الأنبياء : ٥٧] وإضمار الكلمة في الكلام استعملته العرب كقوله تعالى واسأل القرية ﴾ [يوسف : ۸۳] أي أهلها فأما إضمار بعض الكلمة في البعض ما استعملته العرب اهـ.
قوله : (وكفارته تحرير رقبة أو إطعام عشرة مساكين كهما في الظهار أو كسوتهم بما يستر عامة البدن أي وكفارة اليمين بمعنى القسم أو الحلف لما قدمنا أنها مؤنثة والأصل في ذلك قوله تعالى فكفارته اطعام عشرة مساكين من أوسط ما تطعمون أهليكم أو كسوتهم أو تحرير رقبة [المائدة : ۸۹] وكلمة «أو» للتخيير فكان الواجب أحد الأشياء الثلاثة، والتخيير لا بد منهما عند البصريين. وقال الكوفيون والفارسي: يجوز الاقتصار على أحدهما؛ ذكره الاسنائي في الكوكب الدري قوله : (حتى لو قال والله أفعل كذا اليوم فلم يفعل لا تلزمه الكفارة الخ) قال الرملي بعد نقله نحوه عن الاختيار قال شيخ شيخنا الشيخ علي المقدسي في شرح الكنز المنظوم أقول : على هذا أكثر ما يقع من العوام لا يكون يميناً لعدم اللام والنون فلا كفارة عليهم فيها لكن ينبغي أن تلزمهم لتعارفهم الحلف بذلك . ويؤيده ما نقلناه عن الظهيرية أنه لو سكن الهاء أو رفع أو نصب في بالله يكون يميناً مع أن العرب ما نطقت بغير الجر فليتأمل. وينبغي أن يكون يميناً وإن خلا من اللام والنون ويدل عليه قوله في الولوالجية : سبحان الله أفعل لا إله إلا الله أفعل كذا ليس بيمين إلا أن ينويه ا هـ . أقول : قوله على هذا ما يقع من العوام لا يكون يميناً ظاهراً كلامهم جميعاً أنه . يمين لكن على النفي لا على الإثبات لأنهم قالوا فيكون معنى قوله والله أفعل أي لا أفعل هذا ولا دلالة فيما عن الظهيرية والولوالجية لمدعاه أما الأول فلأنه تغيير إعرابي لا يمنع الموضوع فلا يضر تسكين الهاء ولا رفعها ولا نصبها وقد تقرر أن اللحن لا يمنع الانعقاد وأما الثاني فلأنه ليس المتنازع فيه إذ المتنازع الإثبات والنفي لا أنه يمين فكلا النقلين لا يدل على المدعي فتأمل كلامه فإنه ظاهر النقد والله تعالى أعلم والنقل يجب اتباعه ا هـ . أقول : مراد المقدسي بقوله لا يكون يميناً» أي على الإثبات كما هو مراد الحالف. ومعنى قوله فلا كفارة عليهم فيها أي على تقدير ترك ذلك الشيء. وما اعترضه الرملي فيه نظر؛ أما الأول فلأن ما نحن فيه من جملة اللحن قد فسره في القاموس بالخطأ، وأما الثاني فلأن مراده بالاستشهاد بما في الولوالجية من جهة أنه جعله يميناً . نقله النية مع أنه مثبت وحرف
لا ينافي التكليف لأن صحته بإمكان الامتثال وهو ثابت لأنه بفعل أحدها يبطل قول من قال إن التخيير يمنع صحة التكليف فأوجب خصال الكفارة مع السقوط بالبعض كما أشار إليه في التحرير. وفي شرح المنار : ولو أدى الكل لا يقع عن الكفارة إلا واحدة وهو ما كان أعلى قيمة. ولو ترك الكل يعاقب على واحد منها وهو ما كان أدنى قيمة لأن الفرض يسقط بالأدنى. وهي من الكفر بمعنى الستر وإضافتها إلى اليمين إضافة إلى الشرط مجازاً لأن السبب عندنا الحنث كما سيأتي. وعبر بالتحرير بمعنى الإعتاق دون العتق اتباعاً للآية، وليفيد أن الشرط الإعتاق فلو ورث من يعتق عليه فنوى عن الكفارة لا يجوز. وأفاد بقوله كما في الظهار أي التحرير والإطعام هنا كالتحرير والإطعام في كفارة الظهار أنه يجوز الرقبة، مسلمة كانت أو كافرة، ذكراً كان أو أنثى صغيرة كانت أو كبيرة ولا يجوز فائت جنس المنفعة ولا المدبر وأم الولد ولا المكاتب الذي أدى بعض شيء ويجوز في الإطعام التمليك والإباحة، فإن ملك أعطى نصف صاع من براً وصاعاً من تمراً أو صاعاً من شعير لكل مسكين، وإن أباح غداهم وعشاهم، فإن كان بخبز البر لا يحتاج إلى الإدام وإن كان بغير خبز البر احتاج إليه على التفاصيل المتقدمة في كفارة الظهار وفي الخلاصة : لو أعطى عشرة مساكين كل مسكين الحنطة عن كفارة الأيمان لا يجوز إلا عن كفارة واحدة عند أبي حنيفة وأبي يوسف، وكذا في كفارة الظهار وفي نسخة الإمام السرخسي : لو أطعم خمسة مساكين وكسا خمسة مساكين أجزأه ذلك عن الطعام إن كان الطعام أرخص من الكسوة، وعلى القلب لا يجوز. وهذا في طعام الإباحة، أما إذا ملك الطعام فيجوز ويقوم مقام الكسوة، ولو أدى إلى مسكين مداً وخرج السراويل بقوله بما يستر حنطة ونصف صاع من شعير يجوز ا هـ . من عامة البدن، وصححه في الهداية لأن لابسه يسمى عرياناً في العرف ولذا قال في الخانية : لو حلف لا يلبس ثوباً من غزل فلانة فلبس من غزلها سراويل لم يحنث في يمينه لكن ما لا يجزئه عن الكسوة يجزئه عن الطعام باعتبار القيمة فلا بد أن يعطيه قميصاً أو جبة أو ازاراً أو قباء سابلاً بحيث يتوشح به عند أبي حنيفة وأبي يوسف وإلا فهو كالسراويل، ولا تجزىء العمامة إلا أنه إن أمكن أن يتخذ منها ثوب يجزيء مما ذكرنا جاز، أما القلنسوة فلا تجزىء بحال. قال الطحاوي: هذا كله إذا دفع إلى الرجل، أما إذا دفع إلى المرأة فلا بد من الخمار مع الثوب لأن صلاتها لا تصح بدونه قال في فتح القدير : وهذا يشابه الرواية عن محمد في ألف . من من التوكيد مفقود فيه. هذا وقال بعض الفضلاء ما بحثه المقدسي وجيه وقول بعض الناس أنه يصادم المنقول يجاب عنه بأن المنقول في المذهب كان على عرف صدر الإسلام قبل أن تتغير اللغة، وأما الآن فلا يأتون باللام والنون في مثبت القسم أصلاً ويفرقون بين الإثبات والنفي بوجود لا وعدمها، وما اصطلاحهم على هذا إلا كاصطلاح لغة الفرس ونحوها في الأيمان لمن تدبر قوله : (قال في فتح
Book of Oaths. ... They are like those in zihar regarding the feeding or clothing that covers the majority of the body. If unable to do any of them, he fasts. It is restricted by the omission of letters because the letter of emphasis, which is lam and nun, is not omitted in the thing sworn by; rather, it must be mentioned according to al-Muhit. Swearing in Arabic means that in affirmation you say 'By Allah, I will indeed do such-and-such' and 'By Allah, I have indeed done such-and-such' accompanied by the particle of emphasis, and in negation you say 'By Allah, I will not do such-and-such' and 'By Allah, I have not done such-and-such'. So if he says 'By Allah, I do such-and-such today' and then does not do it, no expiation is incumbent upon him, and it is interpreted as his saying 'I will not do such-and-such', so the word 'la' is implied in it, because swearing in affirmation among the Arabs is only with the letter of emphasis, which is lam and nun, as in his saying 'By Allah, I will indeed do such-and-such'. Allah Almighty said: 'By Allah, I will surely plot against your idols' [Al-Anbiya 21:57]. And ellipsis of a word in speech is used by the Arabs, as in His saying 'And ask the village' [Yusuf 12:82], meaning its people. As for omitting part of a word from another part, the Arabs have not used that. End. His statement: 'And its expiation is freeing a slave or feeding ten poor people as in zihar, or clothing them with what covers the majority of the body' meaning that the expiation of an oath (yamin meaning qasam or half) is as we stated, that it is feminine. The basis for that is the verse: 'So its expiation is feeding ten poor people from the average of what you feed your families, or clothing them, or freeing a slave' [Al-Ma'idah 5:89]. The word 'or' is for choice, so the obligation is one of the three things. The choice must be from them according to the Basrans. The Kufans and al-Farisi said: it is permissible to confine to one of them; al-Isna'i mentioned this in al-Kawkab al-Durri. His statement: 'So if he says, 'By Allah, I do such-and-such today' and does not do it, no expiation is incumbent upon him' etc. Al-Ramli said after quoting something similar from al-Ikhtiyar: The shaykh of our shaykh, Shaykh Ali al-Maqdisi, in his commentary on al-Kanz al-Manzum said: I say: based on this, most of what occurs from the common people is not an oath due to the absence of lam and nun, so no expiation is upon them in it. But it is fitting that it be incumbent upon them due to their customary use of swearing by that. This is supported by what we narrated from al-Zahiriyyah that if he makes the ha quiet or raises it or lowers it in 'billah', it is an oath, even though the Arabs never uttered other than with the genitive. So let it be considered. It should be an oath even if devoid of lam and nun, and this is indicated by his statement in al-Walwalijiyyah: 'Subhan Allah, I do; La ilaha illa Allah, I do such-and-such' is not an oath unless he intends it. End. I say: his statement 'based on this, what occurs from the common people is not an oath' apparently all their statements are that it is an oath, but on negation, not on affirmation, because they said it means that his saying 'By Allah, I do' means 'I will not do this'. There is no indication in what is from al-Zahiriyyah and al-Walwalijiyyah for his claim. As for the first, it is a change in inflection that does not prevent the intended meaning, so making the ha quiet or raising it or lowering it does not harm, and it is established that ungrammatical speech does not prevent the validity. As for the second, it is not the point of contention, for the point of contention is affirmation and negation, not that it is an oath. So both narrations do not indicate his claim. So ponder his speech, for it is clear criticism. And Allah knows best, and following the transmitted is obligatory. End. I say: al-Maqdisi intended by his saying 'it is not an oath' meaning in affirmation, as is the intention of the swearer. The meaning of his saying 'so no expiation is upon them in it' is on the assumption of leaving that thing. And al-Ramli's objection to it is questionable. As for the first, because what we are dealing with is part of ungrammatical speech, and he explained in al-Qamus that it means error. As for the second, because his reference to what is in al-Walwalijiyyah is by way of making it an oath. He transmitted the intention while it is positive and a letter. ... does not contradict obligation because its validity is possible by compliance, and it is established because doing one of them invalidates the statement of whoever said that choice prevents the validity of obligation. So he made the varieties of expiation obligatory with dropping by some, as indicated in al-Tahrir. In Sharh al-Manar: If he performs all, only one counts as expiation, and that is the highest value. If he abandons all, he is punished for one of them, which is the lowest value, because the obligation is fulfilled by the lowest. It (kafarah) is from 'kufr' meaning concealment, and its addition to 'yamin' is an addition to the condition metaphorically, because the cause according to us is the breach (hanth) as will come. He expressed 'tahrir' to mean emancipation, not mere freeing, following the verse, and to indicate that the condition is emancipation, so if he inherits a slave whom he is obliged to free and intends it as expiation, it is not valid. He benefited by his saying 'as in zihar' that emancipation and feeding here are like emancipation and feeding in zihar expiation: that the slave is permissible whether Muslim or disbeliever, male or female, young or old, but not permissible one whose benefit is lacking, nor a mudabbar, nor umm walad, nor a mukatab who has paid something. In feeding, giving ownership and permission are permissible. If he gives ownership, he gives half a sa' of wheat, or a sa' of dates, or a sa' of barley to each poor person. If he permits them to eat lunch and dinner, if the bread is from wheat, he does not need a condiment, but if it is from other than wheat, he needs it, according to the details that preceded in zihar expiation. In al-Khulasah: If he gives ten poor people each a quantity of wheat for the expiation of oaths, it is not valid except for one expiation according to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf. Similarly in zihar expiation. In the copy of Imam al-Sarakhsi: If he feeds five poor people and clothes five poor people, that suffices for the food if the food is cheaper than the clothing, otherwise it is not valid. This is regarding food of permission; if he gives ownership of the food, it is permissible and stands in place of clothing. If he gives a poor person a mudd and takes out trousers, by his saying 'what covers' from the majority of the body, wheat and half a sa' of barley are permissible. End. From the majority of the body, and it was declared correct in al-Hidayah because the wearer is called naked in common usage. Hence it is said in al-Khaniyyah: If he swears not to wear a garment made from the yarn of so-and-so, and then wears trousers made from her yarn, he does not break his oath. But what does not suffice for clothing suffices for food by consideration of value. So he must give him a shirt, or a robe, or a loincloth, or a long cloak that can be wrapped around, according to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf. Otherwise, it is like trousers. A turban does not suffice unless it can be made into a garment that suffices from what we mentioned; then it is permissible. As for a skullcap, it never suffices. Al-Tahawi said: All this is if he gives to a man; if he gives to a woman, then a head covering is required along with the garment because her prayer is not valid without it. He said in Fath al-Qadir: This resembles the narration from Muhammad in ... the emphasis is missing from it. This, and some virtuous people said what al-Maqdisi researched is sound. And the statement of some that it contradicts the transmitted is answered by the fact that the transmitted in the madhhab was based on the custom of the early period of Islam before the language changed. But now, they do not bring lam and nun in the positive of the oath at all, and they distinguish between affirmation and negation by the presence or absence of 'la'. And their convention on this is just like the convention of the Persian language and the like in oaths for those who reflect. His statement: 'He said in Fath' (incomplete).
Source pages p. 486

Commentary
This passage from Kitab al-Ayman discusses the rulings on oaths, covering both the conditions for a valid oath and the expiation for breaking it. The author begins by explaining that in Arabic, an affirmative oath must include the emphatic particles lam and nun (e.g., 'Wallahi la af'alanna'). If someone says 'Wallahi af'alu' without the emphatic, it is interpreted as a negation (i.e., 'I will not do'), so breaking it does not require expiation. The Quranic verse (Al-Anbiya 21:57) is cited as evidence. The author then discusses the expiation (kafarah) as stated in the Quran (Al-Ma'idah 5:89): freeing a slave, feeding ten poor people, or clothing them. The word 'or' indicates choice, and there is a grammatical dispute between Basrans (who require a full choice) and Kufans (who allow restriction to one). The text then delves into a debate among later Hanafi scholars, particularly al-Maqdisi and al-Ramli, about whether common people who omit the emphatic particles in their oaths are bound by them. Al-Maqdisi leans toward the view that such oaths are not valid as affirmations, but al-Ramli and others argue that custom should be considered, and thus the oath should be binding. The later part details the rules of kafarah: the types of slaves that can be freed (any except those with missing benefit, mudabbars, umm walad, or mukatab who have paid part), the quantities for feeding (half sa' of wheat, etc.), and what constitutes sufficient clothing (covering the majority of the body, with specific garments listed for men and a head covering for women). The passage concludes with a note that the original ruling was based on early Islamic custom, but nowadays people's convention has changed, so oaths without emphatic particles may be considered valid by custom.

Key Terms
يمين (yamin): An oath, a solemn vow invoking Allah's name, which creates a binding obligation.
توكيد (tawkid): Emphasis; in oaths, the emphatic particles lam and nun (e.g., 'اللام والنون') used in affirmative oaths.
حنث (hanth): Breach of an oath by doing what was sworn not to do, or vice versa.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the mufta bihi view in the passage, what is the ruling if a common person says 'Wallahi af'alu' (without lam and nun) and then does not do it?
A) No kafarah because the statement is not an oath.
B) Kafarah is wajib because custom validates the oath.
C) Kafarah is only wajib if he intended an oath.
D) He must repeat the oath correctly.

Key Takeaway
A valid affirmative oath requires lam and nun in classical Hanafi law, but later reliance on custom makes oaths without them binding if common usage so dictates.

Expiation (Kafarah) for Breaking an Oath: Quranic Basis and Detailed Rules
Exposition of kafarah rules based on Quran 5:89

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three options for kafarah, explain the choice (takhyeer) debate, and apply the detailed rules regarding the types of slaves, food quantities, and clothing requirements.

Core Idea
Kafarah for a broken oath is wajib: freeing a slave, feeding ten poor, or clothing them, with detailed fiqhi conditions for each.

Once an oath is validly made and then broken, expiation becomes obligatory. This passage from Bahr al-Ra'iq details the rules of kafarah based on Quran 5:89. The verse gives three options: freeing a slave, feeding ten poor people, or clothing them. But what exactly counts? The passage clarifies the types of slaves that can be freed, the quantities of food, and what constitutes sufficient clothing. It also addresses a grammatical dispute about the word 'aw' (or) — does it require a full choice among options or can one restrict to one? The Hanafi position, following the Kufan school, permits restriction. The lesson will walk through these details, ensuring you can apply the rules correctly.

Guided Path
1
State the three options from the Quran
Read the passage where it quotes Quran 5:89. The three options are: freeing a slave, feeding ten poor people, or clothing them. Note that the word 'aw' indicates choice.
The Hanafi school interprets 'aw' as a disjunctive giving a choice; any one option fulfills the obligation.
2
Understand the takhyeer (choice) dispute
The passage mentions that Basran grammarians argued 'aw' requires a choice among all options, meaning the person must consider all three and pick one. The Kufans and al-Farisi said one may restrict to a single option from the start. The Hanafi school follows the Kufan view.
This affects whether a person can decide in advance to only feed, or must keep all options open.
3
Identify valid and invalid types of slaves for emancipation
The text lists: any slave, Muslim or non-Muslim, male or female, young or old is permissible. But excluded are: a slave whose benefit is completely lost (e.g., blind, severely disabled), a mudabbar (promised freedom after master's death), umm walad (slave mother of master's child), and a mukatab who has paid part of his contract. Memorize these exclusions.
The key principle: the slave must be capable of normal work; those with permanent major disability are not valid.
4
Detail the rules for feeding poor people
Feeding can be done by giving ownership (tamlik) or by inviting to a meal (ibaha). If giving ownership, the amount is: half a sa' of wheat, or a sa' of dates or barley per person. If inviting, one must provide a full meal with condiments if the bread is not from wheat.
The quantities are based on the sa' measure, roughly 2.5 kg for wheat, 5 kg for dates/barley.
5
Detail the rules for clothing poor people
Clothing must cover the majority of the body. For a man: a shirt, robe, loincloth, or long cloak that can be wrapped. A turban suffices only if it can be made into a garment; a skullcap never suffices. For a woman: a head covering (khimar) is required in addition to a garment covering the majority of the body.
The clothing should be such that the person is not considered 'naked' in common custom.
