كتاب الأيمان
مساكين كهما في الظهار أو كسوتهم بما يستر عامة البدن وإن عجز عن أحدها صام فيه. قيد بإضمار الحروف لأنه لا يضمر في المقسم عليه حرف التأكيد وهو اللام والنون بل بد من ذكرهما لما في المحيط والحلف بالعربية أن تقول في الإثبات والله لا أفعلن كذا ووالله لقد فعلت كذا مقروناً بكلمة التوكيد وفي النفي تقول والله لا أفعل كذا ووالله ما فعلت كذا حتى لو قال والله أفعل كذا اليوم فلم يفعل لا تلزمه الكفارة ويكون بمعنى قوله لا أفعل كذا فتكون كلمة (لا) مضمرة فيه لأن الحلف في الإثبات عند العرب لا يكون إلا بحرف التأكيد وهو اللام والنون كقوله والله لا أفعلن كذا قال الله تعالى تالله لأكيدن أصنامكم [الأنبياء : ٥٧] وإضمار الكلمة في الكلام استعملته العرب كقوله تعالى واسأل القرية ﴾ [يوسف : ۸۳] أي أهلها فأما إضمار بعض الكلمة في البعض ما استعملته العرب اهـ.
قوله : (وكفارته تحرير رقبة أو إطعام عشرة مساكين كهما في الظهار أو كسوتهم بما يستر عامة البدن أي وكفارة اليمين بمعنى القسم أو الحلف لما قدمنا أنها مؤنثة والأصل في ذلك قوله تعالى فكفارته اطعام عشرة مساكين من أوسط ما تطعمون أهليكم أو كسوتهم أو تحرير رقبة [المائدة : ۸۹] وكلمة «أو» للتخيير فكان الواجب أحد الأشياء الثلاثة، والتخيير لا بد منهما عند البصريين. وقال الكوفيون والفارسي: يجوز الاقتصار على أحدهما؛ ذكره الاسنائي في الكوكب الدري قوله : (حتى لو قال والله أفعل كذا اليوم فلم يفعل لا تلزمه الكفارة الخ) قال الرملي بعد نقله نحوه عن الاختيار قال شيخ شيخنا الشيخ علي المقدسي في شرح الكنز المنظوم أقول : على هذا أكثر ما يقع من العوام لا يكون يميناً لعدم اللام والنون فلا كفارة عليهم فيها لكن ينبغي أن تلزمهم لتعارفهم الحلف بذلك . ويؤيده ما نقلناه عن الظهيرية أنه لو سكن الهاء أو رفع أو نصب في بالله يكون يميناً مع أن العرب ما نطقت بغير الجر فليتأمل. وينبغي أن يكون يميناً وإن خلا من اللام والنون ويدل عليه قوله في الولوالجية : سبحان الله أفعل لا إله إلا الله أفعل كذا ليس بيمين إلا أن ينويه ا هـ . أقول : قوله على هذا ما يقع من العوام لا يكون يميناً ظاهراً كلامهم جميعاً أنه . يمين لكن على النفي لا على الإثبات لأنهم قالوا فيكون معنى قوله والله أفعل أي لا أفعل هذا ولا دلالة فيما عن الظهيرية والولوالجية لمدعاه أما الأول فلأنه تغيير إعرابي لا يمنع الموضوع فلا يضر تسكين الهاء ولا رفعها ولا نصبها وقد تقرر أن اللحن لا يمنع الانعقاد وأما الثاني فلأنه ليس المتنازع فيه إذ المتنازع الإثبات والنفي لا أنه يمين فكلا النقلين لا يدل على المدعي فتأمل كلامه فإنه ظاهر النقد والله تعالى أعلم والنقل يجب اتباعه ا هـ . أقول : مراد المقدسي بقوله لا يكون يميناً» أي على الإثبات كما هو مراد الحالف. ومعنى قوله فلا كفارة عليهم فيها أي على تقدير ترك ذلك الشيء. وما اعترضه الرملي فيه نظر؛ أما الأول فلأن ما نحن فيه من جملة اللحن قد فسره في القاموس بالخطأ، وأما الثاني فلأن مراده بالاستشهاد بما في الولوالجية من جهة أنه جعله يميناً . نقله النية مع أنه مثبت وحرف
لا ينافي التكليف لأن صحته بإمكان الامتثال وهو ثابت لأنه بفعل أحدها يبطل قول من قال إن التخيير يمنع صحة التكليف فأوجب خصال الكفارة مع السقوط بالبعض كما أشار إليه في التحرير. وفي شرح المنار : ولو أدى الكل لا يقع عن الكفارة إلا واحدة وهو ما كان أعلى قيمة. ولو ترك الكل يعاقب على واحد منها وهو ما كان أدنى قيمة لأن الفرض يسقط بالأدنى. وهي من الكفر بمعنى الستر وإضافتها إلى اليمين إضافة إلى الشرط مجازاً لأن السبب عندنا الحنث كما سيأتي. وعبر بالتحرير بمعنى الإعتاق دون العتق اتباعاً للآية، وليفيد أن الشرط الإعتاق فلو ورث من يعتق عليه فنوى عن الكفارة لا يجوز. وأفاد بقوله كما في الظهار أي التحرير والإطعام هنا كالتحرير والإطعام في كفارة الظهار أنه يجوز الرقبة، مسلمة كانت أو كافرة، ذكراً كان أو أنثى صغيرة كانت أو كبيرة ولا يجوز فائت جنس المنفعة ولا المدبر وأم الولد ولا المكاتب الذي أدى بعض شيء ويجوز في الإطعام التمليك والإباحة، فإن ملك أعطى نصف صاع من براً وصاعاً من تمراً أو صاعاً من شعير لكل مسكين، وإن أباح غداهم وعشاهم، فإن كان بخبز البر لا يحتاج إلى الإدام وإن كان بغير خبز البر احتاج إليه على التفاصيل المتقدمة في كفارة الظهار وفي الخلاصة : لو أعطى عشرة مساكين كل مسكين الحنطة عن كفارة الأيمان لا يجوز إلا عن كفارة واحدة عند أبي حنيفة وأبي يوسف، وكذا في كفارة الظهار وفي نسخة الإمام السرخسي : لو أطعم خمسة مساكين وكسا خمسة مساكين أجزأه ذلك عن الطعام إن كان الطعام أرخص من الكسوة، وعلى القلب لا يجوز. وهذا في طعام الإباحة، أما إذا ملك الطعام فيجوز ويقوم مقام الكسوة، ولو أدى إلى مسكين مداً وخرج السراويل بقوله بما يستر حنطة ونصف صاع من شعير يجوز ا هـ . من عامة البدن، وصححه في الهداية لأن لابسه يسمى عرياناً في العرف ولذا قال في الخانية : لو حلف لا يلبس ثوباً من غزل فلانة فلبس من غزلها سراويل لم يحنث في يمينه لكن ما لا يجزئه عن الكسوة يجزئه عن الطعام باعتبار القيمة فلا بد أن يعطيه قميصاً أو جبة أو ازاراً أو قباء سابلاً بحيث يتوشح به عند أبي حنيفة وأبي يوسف وإلا فهو كالسراويل، ولا تجزىء العمامة إلا أنه إن أمكن أن يتخذ منها ثوب يجزيء مما ذكرنا جاز، أما القلنسوة فلا تجزىء بحال. قال الطحاوي: هذا كله إذا دفع إلى الرجل، أما إذا دفع إلى المرأة فلا بد من الخمار مع الثوب لأن صلاتها لا تصح بدونه قال في فتح القدير : وهذا يشابه الرواية عن محمد في ألف . من من التوكيد مفقود فيه. هذا وقال بعض الفضلاء ما بحثه المقدسي وجيه وقول بعض الناس أنه يصادم المنقول يجاب عنه بأن المنقول في المذهب كان على عرف صدر الإسلام قبل أن تتغير اللغة، وأما الآن فلا يأتون باللام والنون في مثبت القسم أصلاً ويفرقون بين الإثبات والنفي بوجود لا وعدمها، وما اصطلاحهم على هذا إلا كاصطلاح لغة الفرس ونحوها في الأيمان لمن تدبر قوله : (قال في فتح
Book of Oaths. ... They are like those in zihar regarding the feeding or clothing that covers the majority of the body. If unable to do any of them, he fasts. It is restricted by the omission of letters because the letter of emphasis, which is lam and nun, is not omitted in the thing sworn by; rather, it must be mentioned according to al-Muhit. Swearing in Arabic means that in affirmation you say 'By Allah, I will indeed do such-and-such' and 'By Allah, I have indeed done such-and-such' accompanied by the particle of emphasis, and in negation you say 'By Allah, I will not do such-and-such' and 'By Allah, I have not done such-and-such'. So if he says 'By Allah, I do such-and-such today' and then does not do it, no expiation is incumbent upon him, and it is interpreted as his saying 'I will not do such-and-such', so the word 'la' is implied in it, because swearing in affirmation among the Arabs is only with the letter of emphasis, which is lam and nun, as in his saying 'By Allah, I will indeed do such-and-such'. Allah Almighty said: 'By Allah, I will surely plot against your idols' [Al-Anbiya 21:57]. And ellipsis of a word in speech is used by the Arabs, as in His saying 'And ask the village' [Yusuf 12:82], meaning its people. As for omitting part of a word from another part, the Arabs have not used that. End. His statement: 'And its expiation is freeing a slave or feeding ten poor people as in zihar, or clothing them with what covers the majority of the body' meaning that the expiation of an oath (yamin meaning qasam or half) is as we stated, that it is feminine. The basis for that is the verse: 'So its expiation is feeding ten poor people from the average of what you feed your families, or clothing them, or freeing a slave' [Al-Ma'idah 5:89]. The word 'or' is for choice, so the obligation is one of the three things. The choice must be from them according to the Basrans. The Kufans and al-Farisi said: it is permissible to confine to one of them; al-Isna'i mentioned this in al-Kawkab al-Durri. His statement: 'So if he says, 'By Allah, I do such-and-such today' and does not do it, no expiation is incumbent upon him' etc. Al-Ramli said after quoting something similar from al-Ikhtiyar: The shaykh of our shaykh, Shaykh Ali al-Maqdisi, in his commentary on al-Kanz al-Manzum said: I say: based on this, most of what occurs from the common people is not an oath due to the absence of lam and nun, so no expiation is upon them in it. But it is fitting that it be incumbent upon them due to their customary use of swearing by that. This is supported by what we narrated from al-Zahiriyyah that if he makes the ha quiet or raises it or lowers it in 'billah', it is an oath, even though the Arabs never uttered other than with the genitive. So let it be considered. It should be an oath even if devoid of lam and nun, and this is indicated by his statement in al-Walwalijiyyah: 'Subhan Allah, I do; La ilaha illa Allah, I do such-and-such' is not an oath unless he intends it. End. I say: his statement 'based on this, what occurs from the common people is not an oath' apparently all their statements are that it is an oath, but on negation, not on affirmation, because they said it means that his saying 'By Allah, I do' means 'I will not do this'. There is no indication in what is from al-Zahiriyyah and al-Walwalijiyyah for his claim. As for the first, it is a change in inflection that does not prevent the intended meaning, so making the ha quiet or raising it or lowering it does not harm, and it is established that ungrammatical speech does not prevent the validity. As for the second, it is not the point of contention, for the point of contention is affirmation and negation, not that it is an oath. So both narrations do not indicate his claim. So ponder his speech, for it is clear criticism. And Allah knows best, and following the transmitted is obligatory. End. I say: al-Maqdisi intended by his saying 'it is not an oath' meaning in affirmation, as is the intention of the swearer. The meaning of his saying 'so no expiation is upon them in it' is on the assumption of leaving that thing. And al-Ramli's objection to it is questionable. As for the first, because what we are dealing with is part of ungrammatical speech, and he explained in al-Qamus that it means error. As for the second, because his reference to what is in al-Walwalijiyyah is by way of making it an oath. He transmitted the intention while it is positive and a letter. ... does not contradict obligation because its validity is possible by compliance, and it is established because doing one of them invalidates the statement of whoever said that choice prevents the validity of obligation. So he made the varieties of expiation obligatory with dropping by some, as indicated in al-Tahrir. In Sharh al-Manar: If he performs all, only one counts as expiation, and that is the highest value. If he abandons all, he is punished for one of them, which is the lowest value, because the obligation is fulfilled by the lowest. It (kafarah) is from 'kufr' meaning concealment, and its addition to 'yamin' is an addition to the condition metaphorically, because the cause according to us is the breach (hanth) as will come. He expressed 'tahrir' to mean emancipation, not mere freeing, following the verse, and to indicate that the condition is emancipation, so if he inherits a slave whom he is obliged to free and intends it as expiation, it is not valid. He benefited by his saying 'as in zihar' that emancipation and feeding here are like emancipation and feeding in zihar expiation: that the slave is permissible whether Muslim or disbeliever, male or female, young or old, but not permissible one whose benefit is lacking, nor a mudabbar, nor umm walad, nor a mukatab who has paid something. In feeding, giving ownership and permission are permissible. If he gives ownership, he gives half a sa' of wheat, or a sa' of dates, or a sa' of barley to each poor person. If he permits them to eat lunch and dinner, if the bread is from wheat, he does not need a condiment, but if it is from other than wheat, he needs it, according to the details that preceded in zihar expiation. In al-Khulasah: If he gives ten poor people each a quantity of wheat for the expiation of oaths, it is not valid except for one expiation according to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf. Similarly in zihar expiation. In the copy of Imam al-Sarakhsi: If he feeds five poor people and clothes five poor people, that suffices for the food if the food is cheaper than the clothing, otherwise it is not valid. This is regarding food of permission; if he gives ownership of the food, it is permissible and stands in place of clothing. If he gives a poor person a mudd and takes out trousers, by his saying 'what covers' from the majority of the body, wheat and half a sa' of barley are permissible. End. From the majority of the body, and it was declared correct in al-Hidayah because the wearer is called naked in common usage. Hence it is said in al-Khaniyyah: If he swears not to wear a garment made from the yarn of so-and-so, and then wears trousers made from her yarn, he does not break his oath. But what does not suffice for clothing suffices for food by consideration of value. So he must give him a shirt, or a robe, or a loincloth, or a long cloak that can be wrapped around, according to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf. Otherwise, it is like trousers. A turban does not suffice unless it can be made into a garment that suffices from what we mentioned; then it is permissible. As for a skullcap, it never suffices. Al-Tahawi said: All this is if he gives to a man; if he gives to a woman, then a head covering is required along with the garment because her prayer is not valid without it. He said in Fath al-Qadir: This resembles the narration from Muhammad in ... the emphasis is missing from it. This, and some virtuous people said what al-Maqdisi researched is sound. And the statement of some that it contradicts the transmitted is answered by the fact that the transmitted in the madhhab was based on the custom of the early period of Islam before the language changed. But now, they do not bring lam and nun in the positive of the oath at all, and they distinguish between affirmation and negation by the presence or absence of 'la'. And their convention on this is just like the convention of the Persian language and the like in oaths for those who reflect. His statement: 'He said in Fath' (incomplete).
Source pages p. 486

Commentary
This passage from Kitab al-Ayman discusses the rulings on oaths, covering both the conditions for a valid oath and the expiation for breaking it. The author begins by explaining that in Arabic, an affirmative oath must include the emphatic particles lam and nun (e.g., 'Wallahi la af'alanna'). If someone says 'Wallahi af'alu' without the emphatic, it is interpreted as a negation (i.e., 'I will not do'), so breaking it does not require expiation. The Quranic verse (Al-Anbiya 21:57) is cited as evidence. The author then discusses the expiation (kafarah) as stated in the Quran (Al-Ma'idah 5:89): freeing a slave, feeding ten poor people, or clothing them. The word 'or' indicates choice, and there is a grammatical dispute between Basrans (who require a full choice) and Kufans (who allow restriction to one). The text then delves into a debate among later Hanafi scholars, particularly al-Maqdisi and al-Ramli, about whether common people who omit the emphatic particles in their oaths are bound by them. Al-Maqdisi leans toward the view that such oaths are not valid as affirmations, but al-Ramli and others argue that custom should be considered, and thus the oath should be binding. The later part details the rules of kafarah: the types of slaves that can be freed (any except those with missing benefit, mudabbars, umm walad, or mukatab who have paid part), the quantities for feeding (half sa' of wheat, etc.), and what constitutes sufficient clothing (covering the majority of the body, with specific garments listed for men and a head covering for women). The passage concludes with a note that the original ruling was based on early Islamic custom, but nowadays people's convention has changed, so oaths without emphatic particles may be considered valid by custom.

Key Terms
كفارة (kafarah): Expiation or atonement for breaking an oath, consisting of freeing a slave, feeding ten poor, or clothing them.
تخيير (takhyeer): Choice among alternatives; in kafarah, one may choose any of the three options.
حنث (hanth): Breach of an oath by doing what was sworn not to do, or vice versa.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which of the following slaves is NOT valid for emancipation in kafarah?
A) A young female slave who is a Muslim.
B) An old male slave who is a disbeliever.
C) A mudabbar slave (promised freedom after master's death).
D) A male slave who is blind in one eye but otherwise healthy.

Key Takeaway
Kafarah for breaking an oath is wajib with three valid options; knowing the detailed conditions for each ensures the expiation is legally correct.

The Criterion for Clothing in Kaffarat al-Yamin
Definition ruling clarifying the criterion for clothing in kaffarat al-yamin.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi criterion for valid clothing in kaffarat al-yamin and apply it to distinguish between sufficient and insufficient garments.

Core Idea
The clothing in kaffarah must establish the name 'clothed', not necessarily make prayer valid.

When giving clothing as expiation for a broken oath, the Hanafi school does not require that the garment be prayer-valid. Instead, the criterion is customary: the recipient must no longer be called 'naked'. This lesson clarifies the legal definition, including the special requirement for women's khimar and the effect of a worn-out garment.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its criterion
The act is giving clothing (kiswah) as part of kaffarat al-yamin. The criterion (zahir al-jawab) is that the garment must establish the name of being clothed (muktasi) and negate the name of being naked ('aryan). This is based on the linguistic meaning of 'iksaa'.
2
Distinguish from prayer validity
The text uses the example of a woman wearing a flowing shirt and a khimar that covers her head and ears but not her neck: she is 'clothed' by custom, yet her prayer is invalid. Thus, prayer validity is not the standard.
This refutes al-Tahawi's reasoning that khimar is needed because prayer is invalid without it.
3
Apply the condition for women
For a woman, a khimar (head covering) is required to remove the name of being naked, even if the garment covers the body. A loincloth (sarawil) alone is insufficient for both men and women.
The khimar must cover the head and ears; covering the neck is not needed for the name 'clothed'.
4
Consider suitability of the garment
The garment must be suitable for the recipient's condition or, according to Shams al-A'imma, for the middle class of people. A worn-out garment is acceptable if it can be used for more than three months (half the life of a new one).
This ensures the expiation is meaningful and beneficial.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال الطحاوي: هذا كله إذا دفع إلى الرجل، أما إذا دفع إلى المرأة فلا بد من الخمار مع الثوب لأن صلاتها لا تصح بدونه قال في فتح القدير : وهذا يشابه الرواية عن محمد في دفع السراويل أنه للمرأة لا يكفي. وهذا كله خلاف ظاهر الجواب، وإنما ظاهر الجواب ما يثبت به اسم المكتسي وينتفي عنه اسم العريان وعليه بنى عدم اجزاء السراويل لا صحة الصلاة وعدمها فإنه لا دخل له في الأمر بالكسوة إذا ليس معناه إلا جعل الفقير مكتسياً وفي الخلاصة : وفي الثوب يعتبر حال القابض إن كان يصلح للقابض يجوز وإلا فلا. وقال بعض مشايخنا : إن كان يصلح لأوساط الناس يجوز. وقال شمس الأئمة : وهذا أشبه بالصواب، ولو أعطى ثوباً خليقاً عن كفارة اليمين إن أمكن الانتفاع به أكثر من نصف مدة الجديد يعني أكثر من ثلاثة أشهر جاز ا هـ. دفع السراويل أنه للمرأة لا يكفي. وهذا كله خلاف ظاهر الجواب، وإنما ظاهر الجواب ما يثبت به اسم المكتسي وينتفي عنه اسم العريان وعليه بنى عدم اجزاء السراويل لا صحة الصلاة وعدمها فإنه لا دخل له في الأمر بالكسوة إذا ليس معناه إلا جعل الفقير مكتسياً وفي الخلاصة : وفي الثوب يعتبر حال القابض إن كان يصلح للقابض يجوز وإلا فلا. وقال بعض مشايخنا : إن كان يصلح لأوساط الناس يجوز. وقال شمس الأئمة : وهذا أشبه بالصواب، ولو أعطى ثوباً خليقاً عن كفارة اليمين إن أمكن الانتفاع به أكثر من نصف مدة الجديد يعني أكثر من ثلاثة أشهر جاز ا هـ. عليه باقي عبارة الفتح حيث قال : والمرأة إذا كانت لابسة قميصاً سابلاً أو إزاراً وخماراً غطى رأسها وأذنيها دون عنقها لا شك في ثبوت اسم أنها مكتسية لا عريانة ومع هذا لا تصح صلاتها، فالعبرة بثبوت ذلك الاسم صحت الصلاة أو لا ا هـ.
Al-Tahawi said: All of this is when (the payment) is made to a man. As for when it is made to a woman, then the khimar is indispensable with the garment, because her prayer is not valid without it. He said in Fath al-Qadir: This resembles the narration from Muhammad regarding the dispensing of a loincloth that it is insufficient for a woman. And all of this is contrary to the apparent answer. Rather, the apparent answer is what establishes the name of being clothed and negates the name of being naked; and upon this was based the non-sufficiency of a loincloth, not the validity or invalidity of prayer, for the latter has no bearing on the command of clothing, since its meaning is only to make the poor person clothed. And in al-Khulasa: Regarding the garment, consideration is given to the condition of the recipient: if it is suitable for the recipient, it is permitted; otherwise not. And some of our scholars said: If it is suitable for the middle class of people, it is permitted. And Shams al-A'imma said: This is closer to correctness, and if one gives a worn-out garment for the expiation of an oath, if it is possible to benefit from it for more than half the duration of a new one — meaning more than three months — it is permitted, end quote. (Then repeat from page break) ... Upon it (the issue) rests the rest of the expression of al-Fath where he said: A woman, if she is wearing a flowing shirt or a wrap and a khimar that covers her head and ears but not her neck, there is no doubt that the name of being clothed is established and she is not naked, yet her prayer is not valid with that. So the criterion is the establishment of that name, whether the prayer is valid or not, end quote.
Source pages p. 487

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq explains the ruling on clothing as an option for expiation of oaths (kaffarat al-yamin). It opens with a quote from al-Tahawi distinguishing between giving clothing to a man versus a woman. For a woman, a khimar (head covering) is required in addition to the garment (thawb), because her prayer is not valid without it. However, the author of Fath al-Qadir notes that this reasoning is not the correct foundation; rather, the correct criterion is that the recipient should be described as 'clothed' (muktasi) and not 'naked' ('aryan). This is based on the custom and literal meaning. Thus, a loincloth (sarawil) is insufficient because it does not remove the name of being naked entirely. For women, the khimar is needed to cover the head and ears; covering the neck is not required for the name 'clothed' even if prayer may be invalid without it. The passage further discusses other rulings: the garment must be suitable for the recipient according to their condition or the middle class; a worn-out garment is acceptable if it can be used for more than three months (half the life of a new one). These rulings follow the Hanafi school's principles of considering 'urf (custom) and practicality in expiation.

Key Terms
كسوة (kiswah): clothing given as part of kaffarat al-yamin; must be a garment that covers the body sufficiently to negate the name 'naked'.
خمار (khimar): head covering for women; a necessary part of the kiswah for women in kaffarah according to al-Tahawi, though Fath al-Qadir clarifies that the criterion is the name 'clothed', not prayer validity.
سراويل (sarawil): loincloth or trousers; insufficient for kaffarah because it does not remove the name 'naked'.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the main criterion for a garment to suffice in kaffarat al-yamin according to the Hanafi school?
A) It must cover the 'awrah for prayer.
B) It must be new and unused.
C) It must establish the name of being clothed and negate the name of being naked.
D) It must be made of cotton.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi criterion for clothing in kaffarat al-yamin is the customary name of being clothed, not prayer validity.

Intention and Recipient Rules for Kaffarat al-Yamin
Ruling statement on intention and recipients of kaffarah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the requirement of intention for kaffarah and identify which categories of recipients are permitted or prohibited according to the Hanafi school.

Core Idea
Intention is essential for kaffarah; recipients follow zakat except dhimmis and exclude close relatives.

Expiation for a broken oath (kaffarat al-yamin) has strict requirements. The Hanafi school holds that intention (niyyah) is necessary for its validity, and the recipients must meet specific conditions. This lesson from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq clarifies both aspects, highlighting who may and may not receive kaffarah payments.

Guided Path
1
Identify the requirement of intention
The text states that intention (niyyah) is indispensable for the validity of expiation in all three types (freeing slaves, feeding, clothing). Without intention, the expiation is invalid.
2
Recognize the general rule for recipients
The general rule is that the recipients of kaffarah are the same as those eligible for zakat. However, there are exceptions mentioned in the text.
3
List the exceptions
Two key exceptions: (1) A dhimmi (non-Muslim under Muslim protection) may receive kaffarah but not zakat. (2) One cannot give kaffarah to one's ascendants (parents, grandparents) or descendants (children, grandchildren), even if they are poor.
4
Apply the rule to the case of a slave wife
If one's wife is a slave belonging to another, giving kaffarah to her is invalid because she is not a proper recipient for her husband's expiation. The charity is completed by her acceptance, not by her master's, and she is not a valid recipient.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
واعلم أنه لا بد من النية لصحة التكفير في الأنواع الثلاثة كما صرح به في فتح القدير وأن مصرفها مصرف الزكاة. قال في الخانية: كل يجوز صرف الزكاة إليه لا يجوز صرف الكفارة إليه فلا يعطيها لأبيه وإن علا، ولا لولده وإن سفل وكذا الصدقة المنذورة ولو أعطى كفارة يمينه لامرأته وهي أمة لغيره ومولاها فقير لا يجوز ذلك لأن الصدقة تتم بقبولها لا بقبول المولى وهي ليست بمحل لأداء كفارته فلا يجوز كما لو أعطى أباه وأمه وهما مملوكان لفقير لا يجوز ذلك ا هـ. ويرد على الكلية المذكورة الدفع إلى الذمي فإنه جائز في الكفارة دون الزكاة. وفي الخانية أيضاً: لو أعطى في كفارة اليمين عشرة مساكين كل مسكين مداً مداً ثم استغنوا ثم افتقروا ثم أعاد يوسف لا يجوز ذلك لأنهم لما استغنوا صاروا بحال لا يجوز دفع الكفارة إليهم فبطل ما أدى كما لو أدى إلى مكاتب مداً ثم رده في الرق ثم كوتب ثانياً ثم أعطاه مداً لا يجوز ذلك.
Know that intention (niyyah) is indispensable for the validity of expiation in all three types, as clarified in Fath al-Qadir, and that its recipients are the same as the recipients of zakat. He said in al-Khaniyah: Everyone to whom it is permitted to give zakat, it is not permitted to give kaffarah. So one does not give it to his father, however high, nor to his child, however low; and likewise for vowed charity (al-sadaqah al-mandhurah). If one gives the expiation of his oath to his wife while she is a slave belonging to someone else and her master is poor, it is not permitted, because the charity is completed by her acceptance, not by the acceptance of the master, and she is not a proper recipient for his expiation, so it is not permitted, just as if he gave it to his father and mother while they are slaves belonging to a poor person, it is not permitted. End quote. And an exception to the aforementioned general rule is payment to a dhimmi (non-Muslim under Muslim protection), for it is permissible in kaffarah but not in zakat. And in al-Khaniyah also: If one gives in expiation of an oath to ten poor people each one mudd of wheat, then they become rich, then become poor, then Yusuf repeated (the giving?) it is not permitted, because when they became rich they reached a state where it is not permissible to give kaffarah to them, so what was given becomes void, just as if one gave a mudd to a mukatib (slave contracted for freedom) then he is returned to slavery, then he is made a mukatib again, then he gives him a mudd, it is not permitted.
Source pages p. 488

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq addresses two key aspects of kaffarat al-yamin: intention and recipients. First, it emphasizes that intention (niyyah) is a prerequisite for all three types of expiation (freeing slaves, feeding, clothing). Without intention, the expiation is invalid. Second, it discusses who may receive the expiation. The general rule is that the recipients are the same as those eligible for zakat, but with an important exception: while zakat cannot be given to dhimmis (non-Muslim citizens), kaffarah can be given to them. However, certain close relatives are excluded: one cannot give kaffarah to one's parents (ascendants) or children (descendants), even if they are poor. The text also provides a case: if one's wife is a slave belonging to someone else, and her husband gives her the kaffarah, it is invalid because the acceptance is by the wife, not the master, and she is not a valid recipient for her husband's expiation. Additionally, if a recipient becomes rich after receiving the first payment, the expiation is invalidated and must be made again. This shows the strict conditions for validity.

Key Terms
نية (niyyah): Intention; a prerequisite for the validity of expiation; one must intend which expiation they are performing.
صدقة منذورة (sadaqah mandhurah): Vowed charity; used here as an analogy, it also cannot be given to parents or children.
ذمي (dhimmi): A non-Muslim living under Muslim protection; valid recipient for kaffarah but not for zakat.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Who among the following may validly receive kaffarat al-yamin?
A) The giver's own father, if he is poor.
B) A dhimmi who is poor.
C) The giver's wife who is a slave of another poor master.
D) The giver's adult son who is poor.

Key Takeaway
Intention is required for kaffarah, and recipients must not be ascendants or descendants; dhimmis are an exception.

Fasting as Kaffarah: Conditions of Inability and Continuity
Explains that fasting is only valid for kaffarah when one is unable to perform the other three options, and must be consecutive.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two conditions for fasting as kaffarah in the Hanafi school and explain the proof for the requirement of consecutive days.

Core Idea
Fasting for kaffarah is only permissible when truly unable to do the other three options, and the days must be consecutive.

This lesson examines the Hanafi ruling on fasting as an expiation for a broken oath. The source text from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq clarifies two critical conditions: first, that fasting is not a primary option but a last resort when one cannot free a slave, feed, or clothe; second, that the three fast days must be consecutive. We will see how the Hanafi school derives the second condition from a companion's reading of the Quran.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
What is being ruled on? Fasting as a substitute for kaffarat al-yamin. The ruling: it is wajib only when the person is unable to do any of the three primary options (freeing a slave, feeding, clothing).
2
Locate the primary dalil
The Quranic verse 5:89: 'But whoever does not find (the means), then a fast of three days.' This establishes fasting as a substitute when inability is established.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah for the condition of continuity
The verse says 'three days' without specifying. The Hanafi school adds the condition of consecutive days based on the reading of Ibn Mas'ud (radiAllahu anhu), who recited 'mutatabi'at' (consecutive). This reading is treated as a hadith (riwayah) that adds a detail to the absolute text.
The reading is zanni al-thubut but well-known, so it is accepted to increase upon the definitive text.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
The Shafi'i school does not require consecutive days; they take the verse as absolute (mutlaq). Thus the condition remains a point of legitimate ikhtilaf.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi tarjih
The Hanafi position relies on the established reading of Ibn Mas'ud, which is treated as a narration from the Prophet (ﷺ). The condition of continuity is thus considered wajib based on this additional proof.
Mufta bihi: fasting must be consecutive.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (وإن عجز عن أحدها صام ثلاثة أيام متتابعة أي إن لم يقدر على الإعتاق والإطعام والكسوة كفر بالصوم لقوله تعالى فمن لم يجد فصيام ثلاثة أيام ﴾ [المائدة : ٨٩] وشرطنا التتابع عملاً بقراءة ابن مسعود متتابعات وقراءته كروايته وهي مشهورة جاز الزيادة بها على القطعي المطلق. وأشار بالعجز إلى أنه لو كان عنده واحد . من الأصناف الثلاثة لا يجوز له الصوم وإن كان محتاجاً إليه ففي الخانية : ولا يجوز التكفير بالصوم إلا لمن عجز عما سوى ذلك.
His saying: 'And if he is unable to do any of them, he fasts three consecutive days' — meaning if he cannot afford emancipation, feeding, and clothing, he makes expiation by fasting, because of the Exalted's saying: 'But whoever does not find (the means), then a fast of three days' (Quran 5:89). And we stipulated continuity, acting upon the reading of Ibn Mas'ud: 'mutatabi'at' (consecutive), and his reading is like his narration and it is well-known, so it is permissible to increase by it over the absolute definitive. And he indicated by 'inability' that if he possesses one of the three categories, fasting is not permissible for him, even if he needs that (possession) for himself. For in al-Khaniyah: Expiation by fasting is not permissible except for one who is unable to do other than that.
Source pages p. 488

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq explains the ruling on fasting as an option for kaffarat al-yamin. The author (al-Kanz) states that if one is unable to perform any of the three preceding options (freeing a slave, feeding, or clothing), then he fasts three consecutive days. The proof is Quran 5:89, which says 'But whoever does not find (the means), then a fast of three days.' The Hanafi school adds the condition of continuity (tataabu') based on the reading of Ibn Mas'ud (radiAllahu anhu) who recited 'mutatabi'at' (consecutive). This reading is considered a narration (riwayah) from the Prophet (ﷺ) and is well-known, so it is accepted to add a condition to the absolute text. The text also clarifies that the inability must be genuine: if the person possesses even one of the three categories (e.g., enough money to buy a slave or food), he cannot resort to fasting, even if he needs that money for his own sustenance. This is a strict condition to prevent misuse of the easier option.

Key Terms
تتابع (tataabu'): consecutive (fasting days); a required condition for the kaffarah fast.
عجز ('ajz): inability; the condition for resorting to fasting; one must be unable to afford any of the three categories (slave, food, clothing) even if he needs that money for himself.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, when is fasting permissible for kaffarat al-yamin?
A) Whenever the person prefers fasting over the other options.
B) Only when the person is unable to afford any of the three categories (freeing a slave, feeding, or clothing).
C) When the person's income is less than five hundred dirhams.
D) Only if the person is a traveler.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school requires both genuine inability and consecutive fasting for kaffarah, based on the Quran and the reading of Ibn Mas'ud.

Valid Garments for Kaffarah: The Criterion of Being Clothed
Commentary on the ruling for kaffarah clothing

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi criterion for valid clothing in kaffarah and apply it to determine whether a garment is acceptable.

Core Idea
The criterion for kaffarah clothing is making the recipient appear clothed, not suitability for prayer.

When fulfilling the kaffarah for breaking an oath, the giver must provide clothing. But what counts as valid clothing? Is it enough that the garment can be used in prayer? The Hanafi school clarifies that the key is whether the recipient appears clothed (muktas). This distinction has practical implications, such as the insufficiency of trousers for women and the acceptability of worn garments that are still usable for a significant period.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Central Issue
What is the primary criterion for valid kaffarah clothing according to the commentator? Look for the phrase 'makes the poor person clothed'.
The criterion is derived from the command 'clothe them' in the Quran.
2
Distinguish from Prayer Conditions
Why does the commentator emphasize that prayer validity is irrelevant? Understand the difference between covering for prayer and being clothed in society.
The commentator explicitly says prayer conditions have no bearing on kaffarah.
3
Apply to Specific Garments
Why are trousers for a woman not sufficient? Consider what 'appearing clothed' means in her cultural context.
Trousers leave the upper body uncovered, so the woman would still be considered 'naked'.
4
Determine Conditions for Worn Garments
When is a worn-out (khaliq) garment acceptable? Find the specific duration condition stated in the text.
The condition is more than half the lifespan of a new garment, i.e., more than three months.
5
Recognize the General Rule
How do scholars determine suitability? Consider the recipient's condition or the standard of average people.
Shams al-A'immah preferred the criterion of suitability for average people.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
دفع السراويل أنه للمرأة لا يكفي. وهذا كله خلاف ظاهر الجواب، وإنما ظاهر الجواب ما يثبت به اسم المكتسي وينتفي عنه اسم العريان وعليه بنى عدم اجزاء السراويل لا صحة الصلاة وعدمها فإنه لا دخل له في الأمر بالكسوة إذا ليس معناه إلا جعل الفقير مكتسياً وفي الخلاصة : وفي الثوب يعتبر حال القابض إن كان يصلح للقابض يجوز وإلا فلا. وقال بعض مشايخنا : إن كان يصلح لأوساط الناس يجوز. وقال شمس الأئمة : وهذا أشبه بالصواب، ولو أعطى ثوباً خليقاً عن كفارة اليمين إن أمكن الانتفاع به أكثر من نصف مدة الجديد يعني أكثر من ثلاثة أشهر جاز ا هـ.
The removal of trousers [for a woman] is not sufficient. All of this is contrary to the apparent answer. Rather, the apparent answer is what establishes the name 'clothed' and removes the name 'naked' from him, and upon this is based the non-sufficiency of trousers, not the validity of prayer or its absence, for that has no bearing on the command of clothing, since its meaning is only to make the poor person clothed. In al-Khulasa: 'In clothing, the condition of the recipient is considered; if it is suitable for the recipient, it is permissible, otherwise not.' Some of our scholars said: 'If it is suitable for the average people, it is permissible.' Shams al-A'immah said: 'This is more correct.' And if one gives a worn-out garment for the expiation of an oath, and it is possible to benefit from it for more than half the lifespan of a new [garment], i.e., more than three months, it is permissible.
Source pages p. 488

Commentary
This passage discusses the conditions for clothing in kaffarah. The commentator clarifies that the criterion for valid clothing is not whether it is suitable for prayer but whether it makes the recipient 'clothed'. Thus, trousers for a woman are not sufficient because they do not cover the upper body. The garment must be such that it is considered suitable for the recipient or for the average people. Additionally, a worn garment is acceptable if it is usable for more than half the lifespan of a new one, roughly three months. This ruling is based on the apparent meaning of the command 'clothe them' in the Quran, which aims to cover the person, not to meet the conditions for prayer.

Key Terms
مكتسي (muktas): The status of being clothed; a person who is considered covered for the purpose of kaffarah.
خليق (khaliq): A worn-out garment that is still usable for a significant period (more than half the lifespan of a new one).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi commentary, what is the primary criterion for the validity of a garment given as kaffarah?
A) It must be new and of high quality.
B) It must be suitable for prayer.
C) It must make the recipient appear clothed (muktas).
D) It must cover the head.

Key Takeaway
The validity of kaffarah clothing depends on making the recipient appear clothed (muktas), not on prayer suitability, with a minimum usability period of three months for worn garments.

Conditions for Valid Kaffarah: Intention and Recipients
Ruling on intention and recipient eligibility for kaffarah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the requirement of intention for kaffarah and identify which recipients are eligible or ineligible according to the Hanafi school.

Core Idea
Kaffarah requires intention and must be given only to eligible recipients, excluding close relatives and including dhimmis.

This passage from Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq clarifies two essential conditions for a valid kaffarah: the presence of intention (niyyah) at the time of giving, and the proper selection of recipients. While kaffarah recipients generally overlap with zakat recipients, there are key exceptions—most notably, parents and children are excluded, while dhimmis are included. Understanding these rules ensures that the expiation is valid in the sight of Allah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The passage confirms that intention is necessary for the validity of kaffarah in all three types (freeing a slave, fasting, feeding). Without intention, the expiation is invalid.
This aligns with the general Hanafi principle that acts of worship require niyyah.
2
List the conditions for recipients
The general rule is that kaffarah recipients are the same as zakat recipients. However, exceptions are given: one cannot give to one's own parents, children, or a wife who is a slave of another. On the other hand, a dhimmi (non-Muslim citizen) may receive kaffarah, unlike zakat.
The exception for dhimmis is a clear divergence from zakat rules.
3
Note what invalidates after giving
If a recipient later becomes rich, the previously given kaffarah becomes invalid and must be repeated. Similarly, if a mukatib (slave under contract) receives kaffarah and then returns to slavery, the payment is invalid.
This shows that the recipient's status at the time of receipt and its continuity matter.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
واعلم أنه لا بد من النية لصحة التكفير في الأنواع الثلاثة كما صرح به في فتح القدير وأن مصرفها مصرف الزكاة. قال في الخانية: كل يجوز صرف الزكاة إليه لا يجوز صرف الكفارة إليه فلا يعطيها لأبيه وإن علا، ولا لولده وإن سفل وكذا الصدقة المنذورة ولو أعطى كفارة يمينه لامرأته وهي أمة لغيره ومولاها فقير لا يجوز ذلك لأن الصدقة تتم بقبولها لا بقبول المولى وهي ليست بمحل لأداء كفارته فلا يجوز كما لو أعطى أباه وأمه وهما مملوكان لفقير لا يجوز ذلك ا هـ. ويرد على الكلية المذكورة الدفع إلى الذمي فإنه جائز في الكفارة دون الزكاة. وفي الخانية أيضاً: لو أعطى في كفارة اليمين عشرة مساكين كل مسكين مداً مداً ثم استغنوا ثم افتقروا ثم أعاد يوسف لا يجوز ذلك لأنهم لما استغنوا صاروا بحال لا يجوز دفع الكفارة إليهم فبطل ما أدى كما لو أدى إلى مكاتب مداً ثم رده في الرق ثم كوتب ثانياً ثم لا من عليهم مداً مداً عن أبي [؟]. أعطاه مداً لا يجوز ذلك.
And know that intention is necessary for the validity of expiation in all three types, as clarified in Fath al-Qadeer, and that its recipients are the same as the recipients of zakat. He said in al-Khaniyya: 'Everyone to whom it is permissible to give zakat, it is not permissible to give kaffarah to him. Thus, one should not give it to his father, even if ascending, nor to his child, even if descending. Likewise, vowed charity. And if one gives his kaffarah for an oath to his wife who is a slave belonging to another, and her master is poor, it is not permissible, because charity is completed by her acceptance, not by the master's acceptance, and she is not a valid recipient for the performance of his kaffarah. So it is not permissible, just as if he gave to his father and mother who are slaves of a poor person, it is not permissible.' An exception to the general rule mentioned is giving to a dhimmi, for it is permissible in kaffarah but not in zakat. And in al-Khaniyya also: 'If one gives in the kaffarah of an oath to ten poor people each a mudd, then they become rich, then they become poor, then Yusuf repeated it, it is not permissible, because when they became rich, they reached a state in which it is not permissible to give kaffarah to them, so what was given became invalid, just as if he gave to a makatib a mudd, then he returned to slavery, then he was made a makatib a second time, then he gave him a mudd, it is not permissible.'
Source pages p. 488

Commentary
This passage emphasizes the importance of intention (niyyah) for the validity of any expiation, whether freeing a slave, feeding, or clothing. The recipients of kaffarah are generally the same as those eligible for zakat, but there are important exceptions: one cannot give kaffarah to his own ascendants or descendants, even if they are poor. Additionally, giving to one's wife who is a slave of another is invalid because she is not a valid recipient. An important exception to the general rule is that a dhimmi (non-Muslim subject of the state) can receive kaffarah, whereas zakat cannot be given to them. The passage also discusses a scenario where a recipient later becomes rich: if the recipients become wealthy after receiving the food, the kaffarah payment becomes invalid and must be repeated. This is similar to the case of giving to a mukatib (slave under contract of manumission) who later returns to slavery.

Key Terms
نية (niyyah): Intention, which is a necessary condition for the validity of all types of kaffarah.
مصرف الزكاة (masrif al-zakat): The categories of zakat recipients as defined in the Quran (eight categories).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which recipient is valid for kaffarah?
A) One's own father who is poor
B) A poor dhimmi (non-Muslim citizen)
C) One's own child who is poor
D) One's wife who is a slave of another

Key Takeaway
Kaffarah requires intention and must be given to eligible recipients, excluding close relatives but including dhimmis.

Conditions for Fasting as Expiation for an Oath
Ruling with proof and detailed conditions for fasting in oath expiation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions under which fasting is permissible for kaffarah yamin, explain the requirement of consecutiveness, and apply the ruling to scenarios of changing financial status.

Core Idea
Fasting for an oath expiation is only valid if you cannot free a slave, feed, or clothe—assessed at the time of fasting.

This passage explains the detailed conditions for fasting as expiation for a broken oath. The key is establishing genuine inability to perform the other forms of expiation. We will see how the Hanafi school derives the condition of consecutiveness from Ibn Mas'ud's qira'a and the practical rulings for slaves, debt, and changing circumstances.

Guided Path
1
Understand the primary ruling and its evidence
The passage opens with the ruling: if unable to free a slave, feed, or clothe, one must fast three consecutive days. The evidence is Quran 5:89.
The imperative 'fasiyaam' indicates obligation in Hanafi usul.
2
Unpack the condition of inability (al-‘ajz)
Inability is not simply lacking any property; it means having no surplus beyond basic needs (al-kafaf). The text defines kafaf as housing, clothing for covering, and daily food. Some scholars include a month’s food. Inability is assessed at the time of fasting, not when the oath was broken.
If one has surplus over kafaf, fasting is not permissible.
3
Analyze the condition of consecutiveness (al-tataabu‘)
The Hanafi school requires three consecutive days based on Ibn Mas’ud’s reading ‘mutataabi’aat.’ This reading is treated as a narration adding to the absolute text. If fasting is interrupted (e.g., by menstruation), it must be restarted.
This differs from kaffarah for breaking Ramadan fast, where interruption by menstruation does not require restart.
4
Apply the ruling to special cases
Slaves can only expiate by fasting, even if their master offers other forms. If a slave becomes free and gains wealth during the fast, he must restart expiation with wealth. Similarly, if someone had absent wealth that is a slave, fasting is not allowed because he could free him.
Ability is assessed at the moment of performance and must persist throughout the fast.
5
Identify practical consequences and disagreements
There is disagreement on the definition of kafaf (daily vs. monthly) and on fasting before paying a debt. The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is that inability is having no surplus over daily needs, and if one can pay debt, fasting is not allowed.
The consideration is only at the time of performance, not at the time of the oath.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (وإن عجز عن أحدها صام ثلاثة أيام متتابعة أي إن لم يقدر على الإعتاق والإطعام والكسوة كفر بالصوم لقوله تعالى فمن لم يجد فصيام ثلاثة أيام ﴾ [المائدة : ٨٩] وشرطنا التتابع عملاً بقراءة ابن مسعود متتابعات وقراءته كروايته وهي مشهورة جاز الزيادة بها على القطعي المطلق. وأشار بالعجز إلى أنه لو كان عنده واحد . من الأصناف الثلاثة لا يجوز له الصوم وإن كان محتاجاً إليه ففي الخانية : ولا يجوز التكفير بالصوم إلا لمن عجز عما سوى القدير الخ) يوهم أن مراد صاحب الفتح أنه لا يشترط للمرأة الخمار مع الثوب وليس كذلك، وإنما مراده أن التعليل المذكور لا يصح على ظاهر الرواية وأنه يكفي في الخمار أن يستر الرأس وإن لم تصح به الصلاة يدل عليه باقي عبارة الفتح حيث قال : والمرأة إذا كانت لابسة قميصاً سابلاً أو إزاراً وخماراً غطى رأسها وأذنيها دون عنقها لا شك في ثبوت اسم أنها مكتسية لا عريانة ومع هذا لا تصح صلاتها، فالعبرة بثبوت ذلك الاسم صحت الصلاة أو لا ا هـ . قول المصنف : (وإن عجز عن الخ) قال ال الرملي : يعني التحرير والإطعام والكسوة جميعاً لا عن بعضها فإنه إذا كان قادراً على أحدها الصوم فلا يجوز لمن يملك ما هو منصوص عليه في الكفارة أو يملك بدله فوق الكفاف، والكفاف منزل يسكنه وثوب يلبسه ويستر عورته وقوت يومه . ومن الناس من قال قوت شهر وإن كان له عبد وهو محتاج إلى الخدمة لا يجوز له التكفير بالصوم لأنه قادر على الإعتاق. ومن ملك مالاً وعليه دين مثل ذلك ووجبت عليه الكفارة فقضى دينه بذلك المال جاز له التكفير بالصوم، وإن صام قبل قضاء الدين اختلفوا فيه ؛ قال بعضهم يجوز له الصوم، وقال بعضهم لا يجوز وفي الكتاب إشارة إلى القولين ولو كان له مال غائب أو دين على رجل وليس في يده ما يكفر عن يمينه جاز له الصوم قال : هذا إذا لم يكن المال الغائب عبداً، فإن كان عبداً يجوز في الكفارة لا يجوز له التكفير بالصوم لأنه قادر على الإعتاق ا هـ . وفي المجتبى : ظاهر المذهب إذا فضل عن حاجته قدر ما يكفر به لا يجوز له الصوم ا هـ . والاعتبار في العجز وعدمه وقت الأداء لا وقت الحنث، فلو حنث وهو معسر ثم أيسر لا يجوز له الصوم وفي عكسه يجوز. ويشترط استمرار العجز إلى وقت الفراغ من الصوم فلو صام المعسر يومين ثم أيسر لا يجوز له الصوم؛ كذا في الخانية. وقيد بالتتابع لأنه لو صام الثلاثة متفرقة لا يجوز له ولم يستثن العذر لما في الخلاصة : ولو حاضت المرأة في الثلاثة استقبلت بخلاف كفارة الفطر. وأشار المصنف بالعجز إلى أن العبد إذا حنث لا يكفر إلا بالصوم لأنه عاجز عن الثلاثة ولو أعتق عنه مولاه أو أطعم أو كسا لا يجزئه، وكذا المكاتب والمستسعي. ولو صام العبد فعتق قبل أن يفرغ ولو بساعة فأصاب مالاً استئناف الكفارة بالمال ؛ كذا في فتح القدير. وفي المجتبى : كفر بالصوم وفي ملكه رقبة أو ثياب أو طعام قد نسيه ؛ قيل يجزئه عند أبي حنيفة ومحمد والصحيح أنه لا يجزئه. وفي الجامع الأصغر وهب ماله وسلمه ثم صام ثم رجع بالهبة أجزأه الصوم والمعتبر في التكفير حال الأداء لا غير ا.هـ. وهذا يستثنى من قولهم إن الرجوع في الهبة فسخ من الأصل. وفي المجتبى أيضاً، بذل ابن المعسر لأبيه مالاً ليكفر به لا تثبت القدرة به إجماعاً.
His saying: 'And if he is unable to do any of them, he fasts three consecutive days.' That is, if he is not capable of freeing a slave, feeding, or clothing, he expiates by fasting, due to the Almighty's saying: 'But whoever cannot find [the means], then a fast of three days' [Quran 5:89]. And we have conditioned continuity (tataabu') based on the reading of Ibn Mas'ud: 'mutataabi'aat' (consecutive), and his reading is like his narration, and it is well-known, so it is permissible to increase (the condition) upon the absolute definitive. And he pointed by 'inability' to the fact that if he possesses one of the three types, he is not permitted to fast, even if he is in need of it. In al-Khaniyya: 'It is not permissible to expiate by fasting except for one who is unable to do other than [what is in] Fath al-Qadeer etc. It gives the impression that the author of Fath al-Qadeer means that the head covering (khimar) is not required for a woman along with the garment, which is not the case. Rather, his meaning is that the aforementioned reasoning is not valid according to the apparent narration, and that it is sufficient in the khimar to cover the head, even if the prayer is not valid with it. This is indicated by the rest of the statement of Fath where he said: 'When a woman is wearing a long shirt or a loincloth and a khimar that covers her head and ears but not her neck, there is no doubt that the name of being clothed is established for her, not naked. Yet, her prayer is not valid. So the criterion is the establishment of that name, whether the prayer is valid or not.' Then: 'The author's saying: 'And if he is unable to do any of them' said al-Ramli: meaning freeing, feeding, and clothing all together, not partially, for if he is able to do one of them, he does not fast. It is not permissible for one who owns what is prescribed in the kaffarah or owns its equivalent beyond his basic needs (kafaf). Kafaf is a house to live in, a garment to wear and cover his private parts, and his daily food. Some people said: a month's food. If he has a slave and he is in need of his service, it is not permissible for him to expiate by fasting because he is able to free a slave. If he has wealth and has a debt equal to it, and the kaffarah becomes due, then he pays his debt with that wealth, then it is permissible for him to expiate by fasting. But if he fasts before paying the debt, there is disagreement: some said it is permissible for him to fast, some said not, and the book indicates both views. And if he has absent wealth or a debt owed by someone, and he does not have in hand anything to expiate his oath, it is permissible for him to fast. He said: This is if the absent wealth is not a slave; if it is a slave, it is permissible for the kaffarah, but he is not permitted to expiate by fasting because he is able to free him. In al-Mujtaba: 'The apparent madhhab: if there remains surplus over his need sufficient to expiate with, it is not permissible for him to fast.' The consideration of inability or ability is at the time of performance, not at the time of breaking the oath. Thus, if he broke the oath while insolvent then later became wealthy, he is not permitted to fast. In the opposite case, he is permitted. And it is required that inability continues until the completion of the fast. So if an insolvent fasted two days then became wealthy, he is not permitted to fast; as in al-Khaniyya. He conditioned continuity because if he fasts the three days separately, it is not permissible, and no excuse is made, as in al-Khulasa: 'If a woman menstruates during the three days, she must restart, unlike the expiation for breaking the fast (kaffarah al-fitr).' And the author pointed by 'inability' that if a slave breaks an oath, he expiates only by fasting because he is unable to do the three. And if his master frees him or feeds or clothes [on his behalf], it does not suffice. Similarly, a mukatab and a mustas'i. If a slave fasts and then is freed before finishing, even by an hour, and he gains wealth, he must restart the expiation with wealth; as in Fath al-Qadeer. In al-Mujtaba: 'He expiated by fasting while he owned a slave or clothes or food that he had forgotten; it was said it suffices according to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad, but the correct view is that it does not suffice.' In al-Jami' al-Saghir: 'He gave away his wealth and handed it over, then fasted, then took back the gift (hiba), his fast suffices. And the consideration in expiation is only the time of performance.' This is an exception from the principle that retracting a gift is a nullification from the beginning. In al-Mujtaba also: 'If the son of an insolvent gives his father wealth to expiate with, ability is not established by it by consensus.'
Source pages p. 488

Commentary
This passage provides a detailed explanation of when fasting is permissible as expiation for an oath. The key condition is the inability to perform any of the three other types of expiation (freeing a slave, feeding, clothing). This inability is defined as not having a surplus beyond basic needs (kafaf), which includes housing, clothing, and daily food. The assessment of inability is made at the time of performing the expiation, not when the oath was broken. It must persist until the end of the fast; if one becomes able during the fast, it must be restarted with wealth. The fast must be three consecutive days; if broken (e.g., by menstruation), it must be restarted, unlike kaffarah for breaking the fast in Ramadan. Special rulings apply to slaves: they can only fast, even if their master provides other forms of expiation. The passage also discusses cases of debt, absent wealth, and gift-giving, emphasizing that the decisive factor is the state at the time of performance.

Key Terms
التتابع (al-tataabu'): Consecutiveness of the three days of fasting; required based on the qira'a of Ibn Mas'ud.
الكفاف (al-kafaf): Basic needs: house, clothing to cover private parts, and daily food.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi text, if a person breaks an oath while poor but later becomes wealthy during the three-day fast, what must he do?
A) Continue fasting and it suffices
B) Stop fasting and perform one of the other three types
C) Continue fasting but must also give charity later
D) The fast is invalid and he must restart the expiation with wealth

Key Takeaway
Fasting is only a valid expiation for an oath when one is genuinely unable to perform the other three forms, assessed at the time of performance and throughout the fast.

Ruling on Expiation Before Breaking an Oath and Multiple Oaths
Ruling on timing of expiation and multiple oaths

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that expiation before breaking an oath is invalid and apply the rule that multiple oaths require multiple expiations when multiple names of Allah are used with a conjunction.

Core Idea
Expiation covers an offense; no offense exists before breaking the oath, so expiation before is invalid.

The timing of expiation (kaffarah) in oaths is critical. Some might think it is permissible to expiate early to avoid sin, but the Hanafi school strongly disagrees. Additionally, when an oath involves multiple names of Allah, the number of expiations depends on how the names are phrased. This passage from Al-Bahr al-Rai'iq clarifies both issues, drawing a legal analogy and citing the Zahiriyya narrations.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What act is being ruled upon? It is the act of performing expiation (kaffarah) before breaking the oath (al-hinth). The ruling is that such expiation is invalid (batil).
The text says: 'ولا يكفر قبل الحنث' – he does not expiate before breaking.
2
Locate the proof
What is the evidence for this ruling? The author presents a qiyas (analogy): expiation after wounding someone before death is valid because the wound is a cause (muqaddima) of death, whereas an oath is a deterrent (mani') not a cause. Thus, expiation before hinth is not valid.
The qiyas is jaliy (clear analogy).
3
Understand the condition for multiple oaths
When multiple names of Allah are used in an oath (e.g., 'By Allah, by al-Rahman, by al-Rahim') and they are separated by the conjunction 'and' (waw), each name constitutes a separate oath. Therefore, breaking the oath requires multiple expiations.
The conjunction is key: if the names are strung without 'and', some say it is one oath.
4
Apply the ruling to a scenario
Given the rule, if a person says 'Wallahi wa bi al-Rahmani wa bi al-Rahimi la af'alu katha' and then breaks it, three expiations are obligatory, one for each name.
This is from the apparent narrations (riwayat zahira) as per al-Zahiriyya.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله: (ولا يكفر قبل الحنث أي لا يصح التكفير قبل الحنث في اليمين، سواء كان بالمال أو بالصوم، لأن الكفارة لستر الجناية ولا جناية واليمين ليست بسبب لأنها مانعة من الحنث غير مغضية إليه بخلاف التكفير بعد الجرح قبل الموت لأنه مفض، ثم إذا كفر قبله لا يسترده من الفقير لوقوعه صدقة. ولم يذكر المصنف مسألة تعداد الكفارة لتعدد اليمين وهي مهمة. قال في الظهيرية : ولو قال والله والرحمن والرحيم لا أفعل كذا ففعل ففي الروايات الظاهرة يلزمه ثلاث كفارات ويتعدد اليمين بتعدد الاسم لكن يشترط تخلل حرف القسم، واحد من الثلاث لا فعلى هذا يكون أحد دائراً كما أشار إليه بقوله الإعتاق والإطعام والكسوة يصوم فبطل اعتراض من اعترض عليه والله تعالى أعلم.
His saying: 'And he does not expiate before breaking the oath' means that expiation is not valid before breaking the oath, whether with wealth or fasting, because expiation is to cover the offense, and there is no offense yet, and the oath is not a cause because it prevents breaking the oath, it does not lead to it, unlike expiation after a wound before death, because it is a cause. Then if he expiates before it, he cannot take it back from the poor because it has become a charity. And the author did not mention the issue of multiple expiations for multiple oaths, which is important. He said in al-Zahiriyya: 'If one says, "By Allah, by al-Rahman, by al-Rahim, I will not do such and such," then he does it, in the apparent narrations, three expiations are required, and the oath multiplies by the multiplicity of the names, but with the condition that the conjunction (harf al-qasm) intervenes. One of the three is not... so upon this, it is a circle, as he indicated by his saying: "freeing, feeding, clothing, he fasts" so the objection of the one who objected is invalidated. And Allah knows best.'
Source pages p. 489

Commentary
This passage explains that expiation must be performed after breaking the oath, not before. This is because the purpose of expiation is to cover the sin of breaking the oath. Before the oath is broken, no sin exists. The commentator draws a contrast: it is unlike expiation after wounding someone before the victim dies, because that wound is a cause of death, whereas an oath is a deterrent. However, if one does perform expiation prematurely, the given wealth becomes a charity and cannot be reclaimed. The passage also addresses a separate issue: if one swears an oath using multiple names of Allah (e.g., Allah, al-Rahman, al-Rahim) separated by the conjunction 'and', then breaking this oath requires multiple expiations, one for each name. This is based on the narrations in al-Zahiriyya. The clause 'one of the three is not...' suggests an objection, but the author dismisses it, concluding that it is a coherent ruling.

Key Terms
الحنث (al-hinth): Breaking an oath; the act of violating the oath.
حرف القسم (harf al-qasm): The conjunction 'and' (و) that separates multiple names of Allah in an oath.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) One expiation for the entire oath
B) Three expiations, one for each name
C) Two expiations because al-Rahman is a synonym
D) It depends on the intention

Key Takeaway
Expiation covers an offense; it must be after breaking the oath. Multiple names with conjunction trigger multiple expiations.

Conditions for Fasting as Kaffarah in Hanafi Fiqh
Expands the ruling on fasting as kaffarah with detailed conditions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions under which fasting is permissible for kaffarah and apply the principle that ability is assessed at the time of performance, not at the time of the oath.

Core Idea
Fasting for kaffarah is only permitted when one is truly unable to free, feed, or clothe—ability matters when you do it, not when you sinned.

This passage from Kitab al-Ayman clarifies the precise conditions under which a person may resort to fasting as expiation for a broken oath. While freeing a slave, feeding ten poor, or clothing them are the primary obligations, the Shari'ah makes allowance for fasting when these are genuinely impossible. The key is understanding how 'inability' is defined and when it is measured. This lesson will walk you through the Hanafi criteria, distinguishing between surplus wealth, debts, and absent property, and emphasising the critical timing of the assessment.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act in question is fasting as a substitute for the three alternatives (freeing, feeding, clothing) in kaffarah. The ruling is that it is not permissible (la yajuz) if the person owns the alternatives or their equivalent beyond basic needs.
The default ruling is impermissibility; permissibility is the exception.
2
Define 'basic needs' (kafaf)
The text defines kafaf as including a dwelling, a garment covering the private parts, and daily food. Some scholars extend this to monthly food. This sets the threshold for surplus wealth.
The definition of kafaf is context-dependent but serves as the minimum exemption.
3
Assess specific scenarios of inability
Walk through the cases: owning a slave needed for service (not considered surplus), having debt equal to property (paying debt removes ability), having absent property that is a slave (considered ability to free), and absent non-slave property (no ability if not accessible). In each, decide if fasting is permissible.
The principle: what one can actually access and use at the time of performance matters.
4
Apply the timing rule
The text states that ability is considered at the time of performing the expiation (waqt al-ada'), not at the time of the sin (waqt al-hanth). Thus, a rich-turned-poor person cannot fast, while a poor-turned-rich person may fast.
This is a crucial nuance often misunderstood.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الأيمان الصوم فلا يجوز لمن يملك ما هو منصوص عليه في الكفارة أو يملك بدله فوق الكفاف، والكفاف منزل يسكنه وثوب يلبسه ويستر عورته وقوت يومه . ومن الناس من قال قوت شهر وإن كان له عبد وهو محتاج إلى الخدمة لا يجوز له التكفير بالصوم لأنه قادر على الإعتاق. ومن ملك مالاً وعليه دين مثل ذلك ووجبت عليه الكفارة فقضى دينه بذلك المال جاز له التكفير بالصوم، وإن صام قبل قضاء الدين اختلفوا فيه ؛ قال بعضهم يجوز له الصوم، وقال بعضهم لا يجوز وفي الكتاب إشارة إلى القولين ولو كان له مال غائب أو دين على رجل وليس في يده ما يكفر عن يمينه جاز له الصوم قال : هذا إذا لم يكن المال الغائب عبداً، فإن كان عبداً يجوز في الكفارة لا يجوز له التكفير بالصوم لأنه قادر على الإعتاق ا هـ . وفي المجتبى : ظاهر المذهب إذا فضل عن حاجته قدر ما يكفر به لا يجوز له الصوم ا هـ . والاعتبار في العجز وعدمه وقت الأداء لا وقت الحنث، فلو حنث وهو معسر ثم أيسر لا يجوز له الصوم وفي عكسه يجوز.
Book of Oaths: Fasting is not permissible for one who owns what is prescribed for the expiation or owns its equivalent above basic needs. Basic needs are a dwelling to live in, a garment to wear covering his private parts, and his daily food. Some people said monthly food. If he has a slave and needs him for service, fasting is not permissible for him because he is able to free (a slave). If one owns property and owes a debt equivalent to it, and expiation becomes obligatory, then he pays his debt with that property, then fasting becomes permissible for him. If he fasts before paying the debt, they differed: some said it is permissible, some said not, and the book indicates both opinions. If he has absent property or a debt owed by someone, and he does not have in hand what to expiate his oath with, then fasting is permissible for him. He said: This is if the absent property is not a slave; if it is a slave, (he is able to free) for expiation, so fasting is not permissible because he is able to free (the slave). In al-Mujtaba: The apparent position of the school is that if he has surplus beyond his need sufficient for expiation, fasting is not permissible. Consideration of inability or ability is at the time of performance, not at the time of the sin. So if he committed the sin while poor, then became wealthy, fasting is not permissible for him; and in the opposite case, it is permissible.
Source pages p. 489

Commentary
This passage from Kitab al-Ayman sets out the conditions under which a person may use fasting as expiation (kaffarah) for a broken oath. The general rule is that one must be unable to perform the other forms of expiation—freeing a slave, feeding, or clothing the poor. Inability is measured against basic needs (kafaf): a home, clothing for modesty, and one day's food (some say a month's food). If one owns a slave needed for service, that slave is considered part of basic needs, and one is not considered able to free him; however, if the slave is surplus, then one is able and cannot fast. Similarly, if one has property but owes a debt equal to it, paying the debt removes ability, making fasting permissible. There is a difference of opinion on fasting before paying the debt. For absent property (mal gha'ib) or a receivable debt, if the person has nothing in hand, fasting is permissible—except if the absent property is a slave, because one could theoretically free it. The key principle is that ability is judged at the time of performing the expiation, not at the time of the oath. So if one was poor when he broke the oath but later became wealthy, he cannot fast; conversely, if he was wealthy when he broke the oath but later became poor, he may fast. This reinforces the fiqh maxim: al-ibra fi al-a'jaz wa al-qudra waqt al-ada' la waqt al-hinth.

Key Terms
كفاف (kafāf): Basic necessities: dwelling, clothing, and daily food (some extend to monthly food).
إعتاق (i'tāq): Freeing a slave, which is one of the three options for kaffarah (freeing, feeding, clothing).
كفارة (kaffārah): Expiation for a broken oath, consisting of freeing a slave, feeding ten poor, or clothing them; if unable, fasting three days.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, if a person who broke an oath while poor later becomes wealthy before performing expiation, what is the ruling on fasting?
A) He must fast because he was poor at the time of the sin.
B) He cannot fast because ability is assessed at the time of performance.
C) He may fast because he is now wealthy.
D) He can choose between fasting and feeding.

Key Takeaway
Fasting is a fallback for kaffarah, permitted only when genuine inability exists at the time of expiation, measured after deducting basic needs and debts.

Continuous Inability for Kaffarah Fasting
Expands condition of continuous inability for kaffarah fasting

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the condition that inability must persist throughout the kaffarah fast and apply it to scenarios such as becoming wealthy, slave emancipation, forgotten property, and gift revocation.

Core Idea
A kaffarah fast is valid only if inability persists throughout; ability at any point invalidates it.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq expands on the requirement that the person performing kaffarah by fasting must remain unable to perform property-based expiation (freeing a slave, feeding, or clothing) for the entire duration of the three consecutive fasts. If ability arises at any point, even a day before completion, the fast becomes invalid and property expiation becomes obligatory. The text also addresses special cases: slaves, forgotten property, and the effect of gifting property before fasting.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core condition
The passage states: 'continuity of inability until completion of the fast is required.' This means that at every moment of the three consecutive fasts, the person must be unable to free a slave, feed, or clothe. If ability arises, the fast is invalid.
Ability here means ownership of property sufficient for one of the kaffarah acts.
2
Understand the consequence of becoming able
If a person fasts two days but becomes wealthy on the third, the fast is invalid and he must perform kaffarah with property. The moment ability arises, the fast must be abandoned.
This applies even if ability arises near the end of the third day.
3
Recognize the requirement of consecutiveness (tatābu')
The fast must be performed on three consecutive days. Non-consecutive fasting is invalid. Interruptions such as menstruation break consecutiveness and require restarting, unlike the kaffarah for breaking Ramadan fast, where menstruation may be excused.
No excuse is accepted for interruption, except the unique case of menstruation where restarting is required.
4
Apply the principle to cases of slaves and forgotten property
A slave (including mukātab and mustas'ī) is inherently unable to free or feed, so his only option is fasting. If his master performs the expiation on his behalf, it does not count. If a slave is freed during the fast and acquires wealth, he must switch to property expiation. Regarding forgotten property: if one had forgotten owning a slave or food, some scholars (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad) said his fast suffices, but the correct (muftā bihī) view is that it does not, because the property existed at the time of performance.
The muftā bihī is that forgetting does not excuse the obligation to use property.
5
Examine the gift revocation exception
If a person gives away his property (as a gift) before fasting, then after fasting revokes the gift, the fast is valid because at the time of fasting he truly had no property. This is an exception to the principle that revocation annuls a gift from its origin; here the ruling is based on the state at the time of performance.
This shows the general rule: the consideration is always the time of performance (ḥāl al-adā').

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويشترط استمرار العجز إلى وقت الفراغ من الصوم فلو صام المعسر يومين ثم أيسر لا يجوز له الصوم؛ كذا في الخانية. وقيد بالتتابع لأنه لو صام الثلاثة متفرقة لا يجوز له ولم يستثن العذر لما في الخلاصة : ولو حاضت المرأة في الثلاثة استقبلت بخلاف كفارة الفطر. وأشار المصنف بالعجز إلى أن العبد إذا حنث لا يكفر إلا بالصوم لأنه عاجز عن الثلاثة ولو أعتق عنه مولاه أو أطعم أو كسا لا يجزئه، وكذا المكاتب والمستسعي. ولو صام العبد فعتق قبل أن يفرغ ولو بساعة فأصاب مالاً استئناف الكفارة بالمال ؛ كذا في فتح القدير. وفي المجتبى : كفر بالصوم وفي ملكه رقبة أو ثياب أو طعام قد نسيه ؛ قيل يجزئه عند أبي حنيفة ومحمد والصحيح أنه لا يجزئه. وفي الجامع الأصغر وهب ماله وسلمه ثم صام ثم رجع بالهبة أجزأه الصوم والمعتبر في التكفير حال الأداء لا غير ا.هـ. وهذا يستثنى من قولهم إن الرجوع في الهبة فسخ من الأصل.
And continuity of inability until completion of the fast is required. So if a poor person fasts two days then becomes wealthy, his fast is not valid; thus in al-Khaniyyah. And it is conditioned that the fast be consecutive, because if he fasts the three days separately, it is not valid; and no excuse is exempted because in al-Khulasa: If a woman menstruates during the three days, she must start over, unlike the expiation for breaking the fast (of Ramadan). And the author indicated by 'inability' that a slave, when he breaks an oath, only expiates with fasting because he is unable to do the three (other forms). If his master frees (a slave) on his behalf, or feeds, or clothes, it does not suffice him. Similarly, the mukatab and the mustas'i. If a slave fasts, then is freed before completing even by an hour, and acquires wealth, he must start the expiation with property; thus in Fath al-Qadir. And in al-Mujtaba: He expiated with fasting while in his possession was a slave, clothes, or food that he had forgotten; it was said it suffices according to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad, but the correct view is that it does not suffice. And in al-Jami' al-Asghar: He gifted his property and delivered it, then fasted, then took back the gift by revocation, his fast suffices; and the consideration is the time of performance only. This is an exception from their saying that revocation in gift is a cancellation from the origin.
Source pages p. 489

Commentary
This passage builds on the previous rule by adding the condition that inability to perform the other forms of kaffarah must continue throughout the entire fast. If a person starts fasting while poor but becomes wealthy (i.e., gains the means to free a slave, feed, or clothe) before completing the three days, the fast becomes invalid and he must perform the kaffarah with property instead. This is because ability is determined at each moment of the act. Additionally, the fast must be consecutive (mutatabi')—if one fasts the three days non-consecutively, it is not valid, and there is no excuse for interruption other than specific exceptions like menstruation (which requires restarting). The passage then applies this to a slave: a slave is inherently unable to free or feed, so his only option is fasting. If his master performs the expiation on his behalf, it does not count. If a slave is freed during the fast and acquires wealth, he must switch to the property-based expiation. There is also a discussion on forgotten property: if one had forgotten that he owned a slave or food, some scholars (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad) said his fast suffices, but the correct view (sahih) is that it does not. A notable exception: if one gave away his property (gift) before fasting, then after fasting took it back by revocation (ruju' fi al-hiba), the fast is valid because at the time of fasting he had no property; the later revocation is not retroactive—an exception to the general principle that revocation annuls the gift from its origin.

Key Terms
تتابع (tatābu'): Consecutive days of fasting without interruption; if broken, the fast becomes invalid for kaffarah.
مكاتب (mukātab): A slave who has contracted with his master to earn his freedom by paying installments.
مستسعي (mustas'ī): A slave whom the master has authorized to work and pay for his freedom gradually.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
A kaffarah fast is valid only if inability persists throughout; ability at any point invalidates it.
